The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	1	About that time king Antiochus travelling through the highcountries heard say, that Elymais in the country of Persia was acity greatly renowned for riches, silver, and gold;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	2	And that there was in it a very rich temple, wherein werecoverings of gold, and breastplates, and shields, whichAlexander, son of Philip, the Macedonian king, who reigned firstamong the Grecians, had left there.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	4	Rose up against him in battle: so he fled, and departedthence with great heaviness, and returned to Babylon.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	5	Moreover there came one who brought him tidings into Persia,that the armies, which went against the land of Judea, were putto flight:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	6	And that Lysias, who went forth first with a great power wasdriven away of the Jews; and that they were made strong by thearmour, and power, and store of spoils, which they had gotten ofthe armies, whom they had destroyed:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	7	Also that they had pulled down the abomination, which he hadset up upon the altar in Jerusalem, and that they had compassedabout the sanctuary with high walls, as before, and his cityBethsura.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	8	Now when the king heard these words, he was astonished andsore moved: whereupon he laid him down upon his bed, and fellsick for grief, because it had not befallen him as he lookedfor.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	9	And there he continued many days: for his grief was ever moreand more, and he made account that he should die.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	10	Wherefore he called for all his friends, and said unto them,The sleep is gone from mine eyes, and my heart faileth for verycare.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	11	And I thought with myself, Into what tribulation am I come,and how great a flood of misery is it, wherein now I am! for Iwas bountiful and beloved in my power.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	12	But now I remember the evils that I did at Jerusalem, andthat I took all the vessels of gold and silver that weretherein, and sent to destroy the inhabitants of Judea without acause.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	13	I perceive therefore that for this cause these troubles arecome upon me, and, behold, I perish through great grief in astrange land.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	22	And they went unto the king, and said, How long will it beere thou execute judgment, and avenge our brethren?
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	23	We have been willing to serve thy father, and to do as hewould have us, and to obey his commandments;

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	36	These were ready at every occasion: wheresoever the beastwas, and whithersoever the beast went, they went also, neitherdeparted they from him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	37	And upon the beasts were there strong towers of wood, whichcovered every one of them, and were girt fast unto them withdevices: there were also upon every one two and thirty strongmen, that fought upon them, beside the Indian that ruled him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	38	As for the remnant of the horsemen, they set them on thisside and that side at the two parts of the host giving themsigns what to do, and being harnessed all over amidst the ranks.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	39	Now when the sun shone upon the shields of gold and brass,the mountains glistered therewith, and shined like lamps offire.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	40	So part of the king's army being spread upon the highmountains, and part on the valleys below, they marched on safelyand in order.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	41	Wherefore all that heard the noise of their multitude, andthe marching of the company, and the rattling of the harness,were moved: for the army was very great and mighty.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	42	Then Judas and his host drew near, and entered into battle,and there were slain of the king's army six hundred men.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	43	Eleazar also, surnamed Savaran, perceiving that one of thebeasts, armed with royal harness, was higher than all the rest,and supposing that the king was upon him,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	44	Put himself in jeopardy, to the end he might deliver hispeople, and get him a perpetual name:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	45	Wherefore he ran upon him courageously through the midst ofthe battle, slaying on the right hand and on the left, so thatthey were divided from him on both sides.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	46	Which done, he crept under the elephant, and thrust himunder, and slew him: whereupon the elephant fell down upon him,and there he died.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	47	Howbeit the rest of the Jews seeing the strength of the king,and the violence of his forces, turned away from them.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	49	But with them that were in Bethsura he made peace: for theycame out of the city, because they had no victuals there toendure the siege, it being a year of rest to the land.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	50	So the king took Bethsura, and set a garrison there to keepit.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	51	As for the sanctuary, he besieged it many days: and set thereartillery with engines and instruments to cast fire and stones,and pieces to cast darts and slings.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	52	Whereupon they also made engines against their engines, andheld them battle a long season.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	53	Yet at the last, their vessels being without victuals, (forthat it was the seventh year, and they in Judea that weredelivered from the Gentiles, had eaten up the residue of thestore;)
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	54	There were but a few left in the sanctuary, because thefamine did so prevail against them, that they were fain todisperse themselves, every man to his own place.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	55	At that time Lysias heard say, that Philip, whom Antiochusthe king, whiles he lived, had appointed to bring up his sonAntiochus, that he might be king,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	56	Was returned out of Persia and Media, and the king's hostalso that went with him, and that he sought to take unto him theruling of the affairs.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	57	Wherefore he went in all haste, and said to the king and thecaptains of the host and the company, We decay daily, and ourvictuals are but small, and the place we lay siege unto isstrong, and the affairs of the kingdom lie upon us:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	58	Now therefore let us be friends with these men, and makepeace with them, and with all their nation;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	59	And covenant with them, that they shall live after theirlaws, as they did before: for they are therefore displeased, andhave done all these things, because we abolished their laws.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	60	So the king and the princes were content: wherefore he sentunto them to make peace; and they accepted thereof.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	61	Also the king and the princes made an oath unto them:whereupon they went out of the strong hold.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	62	Then the king entered into mount Sion; but when he saw thestrength of the place, he broke his oath that he had made, andgave commandment to pull down the wall round about.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	6	63	Afterward departed he in all haste, and returned untoAntiochia, where he found Philip to be master of the city: so hefought against him, and took the city by force.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	1	In the hundred and one and fiftieth year Demetrius the son ofSeleucus departed from Rome, and came up with a few men unto acity of the sea coast, and reigned there.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	2	And as he entered into the palace of his ancestors, so itwas, that his forces had taken Antiochus and Lysias, to bringthem unto him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	3	Wherefore, when he knew it, he said, Let me not see theirfaces.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	4	So his host slew them. Now when Demetrius was set upon thethrone of his kingdom,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	5	There came unto him all the wicked and ungodly men of Israel,having Alcimus, who was desirous to be high priest, for theircaptain:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	6	And they accused the people to the king, saying, Judas andhis brethren have slain all thy friends, and driven us out ofour own land.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	7	Now therefore send some man whom thou trustest, and let himgo and see what havock he hath made among us, and in the king'sland, and let him punish them with all them that aid them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	8	Then the king chose Bacchides, a friend of the king, whoruled beyond the flood, and was a great man in the kingdom, andfaithful to the king,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	9	And him he sent with that wicked Alcimus, whom he made highpriest, and commanded that he should take vengeance of thechildren of Israel.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	10	So they departed, and came with a great power into the landof Judea, where they sent messengers to Judas and his brethrenwith peaceable words deceitfully.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	11	But they gave no heed to their words; for they saw that theywere come with a great power.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	12	Then did there assemble unto Alcimus and Bacchides a companyof scribes, to require justice.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	13	Now the Assideans were the first among the children of Israelthat sought peace of them:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	14	For said they, One that is a priest of the seed of Aaron iscome with this army, and he will do us no wrong.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	15	So he spake unto them, peaceably, and sware unto them,saying, we will procure the harm neither of you nor yourfriends.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	16	Whereupon they believed him: howbeit he took of themthreescore men, and slew them in one day, according to the wordswhich he wrote,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	17	The flesh of thy saints have they cast out, and their bloodhave they shed round about Jerusalem, and there was none to burythem.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	18	Wherefore the fear and dread of them fell upon all thepeople, who said, There is neither truth nor righteousness inthem; for they have broken the covenant and oath that they made.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	19	After this, removed Bacchides from Jerusalem, and pitched histents in Bezeth, where he sent and took many of the men that hadforsaken him, and certain of the people also, and when he hadslain them, he cast them into the great pit.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	20	Then committed he the country to Alcimus, and left with him apower to aid him: so Bacchides went to the king.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	21	But Alcimus contended for the high priesthood.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	22	And unto him resorted all such as troubled the people, who,after they had gotten the land of Juda into their power, didmuch hurt in Israel.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	23	Now when Judas saw all the mischief that Alcimus and hiscompany had done among the Israelites, even above the heathen,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	24	He went out into all the coasts of Judea round about, andtook vengeance of them that had revolted from him, so that theydurst no more go forth into the country.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	25	On the other side, when Alcimus saw that Judas and hiscompany had gotten the upper hand, and knew that he was not ableto abide their force, he went again to the king, and said allthe worst of them that he could.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	26	Then the king sent Nicanor, one of his honourable princes, aman that bare deadly hate unto Israel, with commandment todestroy the people.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	27	So Nicanor came to Jerusalem with a great force; and sentunto Judas and his brethren deceitfully with friendly words,saying,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	28	Let there be no battle between me and you; I will come with afew men, that I may see you in peace.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	29	He came therefore to Judas, and they saluted one anotherpeaceably. Howbeit the enemies were prepared to take away Judasby violence.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	30	Which thing after it was known to Judas, to wit, that he cameunto him with deceit, he was sore afraid of him, and would seehis face no more.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	31	Nicanor also, when he saw that his counsel was discovered,went out to fight against Judas beside Capharsalama:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	32	Where there were slain of Nicanor's side about five thousandmen, and the rest fled into the city of David.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	33	After this went Nicanor up to mount Sion, and there came outof the sanctuary certain of the priests and certain of theelders of the people, to salute him peaceably, and to shew himthe burnt sacrifice that was offered for the king.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	34	But he mocked them, and laughed at them, and abused themshamefully, and spake proudly,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	35	And sware in his wrath, saying, Unless Judas and his host benow delivered into my hands, if ever I come again in safety, Iwill burn up this house: and with that he went out in a greatrage.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	36	Then the priests entered in, and stood before the altar andthe temple, weeping, and saying,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	37	Thou, O Lord, didst choose this house to be called by thyname, and to be a house of prayer and petition for thy people:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	38	Be avenged of this man and his host, and let them fall by thesword: remember their blasphemies, and suffer them not tocontinue any longer.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	39	So Nicanor went out of Jerusalem, and pitched his tents inBethhoron, where an host out of Syria met him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	40	But Judas pitched in Adasa with three thousand men, and therehe prayed, saying,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	41	O Lord, when they that were sent from the king of theAssyrians blasphemed, thine angel went out, and smote an hundredfourscore and five thousand of them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	42	Even so destroy thou this host before us this day, that therest may know that he hath spoken blasphemously against thysanctuary, and judge thou him according to his wickedness.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	43	So the thirteenth day of the month Adar the hosts joinedbattle: but Nicanor's host was discomfited, and he himself wasfirst slain in the battle.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	44	Now when Nicanor's host saw that he was slain, they cast awaytheir weapons, and fled.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	45	Then they pursued after them a day's journey, from Adasa untoGazera, sounding an alarm after them with their trumpets.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	46	Whereupon they came forth out of all the towns of Judea roundabout, and closed them in; so that they, turning back upon themthat pursued them, were all slain with the sword, and not one ofthem was left.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	47	Afterwards they took the spoils, and the prey, and smote offNicanors head, and his right hand, which he stretched out soproudly, and brought them away, and hanged them up towardJerusalem.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	48	For this cause the people rejoiced greatly, and they keptthat day a day of great gladness.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	49	Moreover they ordained to keep yearly this day, being thethirteenth of Adar.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	7	50	Thus the land of Juda was in rest a little while.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	1	Now Judas had heard of the the Romans, that they were mightyand valiant men, and such as would lovingly accept all thatjoined themselves unto them, and make a league of amity with allthat came unto them;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	2	And that they were men of great valour. It was told him alsoof their wars and noble acts which they had done among theGalatians, and how they had conquered them, and brought themunder tribute;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	3	And what they had done in the country of Spain, for thewinning of the mines of the silver and gold which is there;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	4	And that by their policy and patience they had conquered allthe place, though it were very far from them; and the kings alsothat came against them from the uttermost part of the earth,till they had discomfited them, and given them a greatoverthrow, so that the rest did give them tribute every year:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	5	Beside this, how they had discomfited in battle Philip, andPerseus, king of the Citims, with others that lifted upthemselves against them, and had overcome them:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	6	How also Antiochus the great king of Asia, that came againstthem in battle, having an hundred and twenty elephants, withhorsemen, and chariots, and a very great army, was discomfitedby them;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	7	And how they took him alive, and covenanted that he and suchas reigned after him should pay a great tribute, and givehostages, and that which was agreed upon,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	8	And the country of India, and Media and Lydia and of thegoodliest countries, which they took of him, and gave to kingEumenes:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	9	Moreover how the Grecians had determined to come and destroythem;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	10	And that they, having knowledge thereof sent against them acertain captain, and fighting with them slew many of them, andcarried away captives their wives and their children, andspoiled them, and took possession of their lands, and pulleddown their strong holds, and brought them to be their servantsunto this day:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	11	It was told him besides, how they destroyed and brought undertheir dominion all other kingdoms and isles that at any timeresisted them;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	12	But with their friends and such as relied upon them they keptamity: and that they had conquered kingdoms both far and nigh,insomuch as all that heard of their name were afraid of them:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	13	Also that, whom they would help to a kingdom, those reign;and whom again they would, they displace: finally, that theywere greatly exalted:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	14	Yet for all this none of them wore a crown or was clothed inpurple, to be magnified thereby:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	15	Moreover how they had made for themselves a senate house,wherein three hundred and twenty men sat in council daily,consulting alway for the people, to the end they might be wellordered:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	16	And that they committed their government to one man everyyear, who ruled over all their country, and that all wereobedient to that one, and that there was neither envy noremmulation among them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	17	In consideration of these things, Judas chose Eupolemus theson of John, the son of Accos, and Jason the son of Eleazar, andsent them to Rome, to make a league of amity and confederacywith them,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	18	And to intreat them that they would take the yoke from them;for they saw that the kingdom of the Grecians did oppress Israelwith servitude.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	19	They went therefore to Rome, which was a very great journey,and came into the senate, where they spake and said.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	20	Judas Maccabeus with his brethren, and the people of theJews, have sent us unto you, to make a confederacy and peacewith you, and that we might be registered your confederates andfriends.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	21	So that matter pleased the Romans well.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	22	And this is the copy of the epistle which the senate wroteback again in tables of brass, and sent to Jerusalem, that therethey might have by them a memorial of peace and confederacy:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	23	Good success be to the Romans, and to the people of the Jews,by sea and by land for ever: the sword also and enemy be farfrom them,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	24	If there come first any war upon the Romans or any of theirconfederates throughout all their dominion,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	25	The people of the Jews shall help them, as the time shall beappointed, with all their heart:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	26	Neither shall they give any thing unto them that make warupon them, or aid them with victuals, weapons, money, or ships,as it hath seemed good unto the Romans; but they shall keeptheir covenants without taking any thing therefore.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	27	In the same manner also, if war come first upon the nation ofthe Jews, the Romans shall help them with all their heart,according as the time shall be appointed them:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	28	Neither shall victuals be given to them that take partagainst them, or weapons, or money, or ships, as it hath seemedgood to the Romans; but they shall keep their covenants, andthat without deceit.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	29	According to these articles did the Romans make a covenantwith the people of the Jews.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	30	Howbeit if hereafter the one party or the other shall thinkto meet to add or diminish any thing, they may do it at theirpleasures, and whatsoever they shall add or take away shall beratified.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	31	And as touching the evils that Demetrius doeth to the Jews,we have written unto him, saying, Wherefore thou made thy yokeheavy upon our friends and confederates the Jews?
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	8	32	If therefore they complain any more against thee, we will dothem justice, and fight with thee by sea and by land.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	1	Furthermore, when Demetrius heard the Nicanor and his hostwere slain in battle, he sent Bacchides and Alcimus into theland of Judea the second time, and with them the chief strengthof his host:

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	4	From whence they removed, and went to Berea, with twentythousand footmen and two thousand horsemen.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	5	Now Judas had pitched his tents at Eleasa, and three thousandchosen men with him:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	6	Who seeing the multitude of the other army to he so greatwere sore afraid; whereupon many conveyed themselves out of thehost, insomuch as abode of them no more but eight hundred men.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	7	When Judas therefore saw that his host slipt away, and thatthe battle pressed upon him, he was sore troubled in mind, andmuch distressed, for that he had no time to gather themtogether.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	8	Nevertheless unto them that remained he said, Let us ariseand go up against our enemies, if peradventure we may be able tofight with them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	9	But they dehorted him, saying, We shall never be able: let usnow rather save our lives, and hereafter we will return with ourbrethren, and fight against them: for we are but few.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	10	Then Judas said, God forbid that I should do this thing, andflee away from them: if our time be come, let us die manfullyfor our brethren, and let us not stain our honour.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	11	With that the host of Bacchides removed out of their tents,and stood over against them, their horsemen being divided intotwo troops, and their slingers and archers going before the hostand they that marched in the foreward were all mighty men.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	12	As for Bacchides, he was in the right wing: so the host drewnear on the two parts, and sounded their trumpets.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	13	They also of Judas' side, even they sounded their trumpetsalso, so that the earth shook at the noise of the armies, andthe battle continued from morning till night.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	14	Now when Judas perceived that Bacchides and the strength ofhis army were on the right side, he took with him all the hardymen,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	15	Who discomfited the right wing, and pursued them unto themount Azotus.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	16	But when they of the left wing saw that they of the rightwing were discomfited, they followed upon Judas and those thatwere with him hard at the heels from behind:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	17	Whereupon there was a sore battle, insomuch as many wereslain on both parts.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	18	Judas also was killed, and the remnant fled.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	19	THen Jonathan and Simon took Judas their brother, and buriedhim in the sepulchre of his fathers in Modin.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	20	Moreover they bewailed him, and all Israel made greatlamentation for him, and mourned many days, saying,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	21	How is the valiant man fallen, that delivered Israel!
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	22	As for the other things concerning Judas and his wars, andthe noble acts which he did, and his greatness, they are notwritten: for they were very many.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	23	Now after the death of Judas the wicked began to put forththeir heads in all the coasts of Israel, and there arose up allsuch as wrought iniquity.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	24	In those days also was there a very great famine, by reasonwhereof the country revolted, and went with them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	25	Then Bacchides chose the wicked men, and made them lords ofthe country.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	26	And they made enquiry and search for Judas' friends, andbrought them unto Bacchides, who took vengeance of them, andused them despitefully.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	27	So was there a great affliction in Israel, the like whereofwas not since the time that a prophet was not seen among them.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	29	Since thy brother Judas died, we have no man like him to goforth against our enemies, and Bacchides, and against them ofour nation that are adversaries to us.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	30	Now therefore we have chosen thee this day to be our princeand captain in his stead, that thou mayest fight our battles.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	31	Upon this Jonathan took the governance upon him at that time,and rose up instead of his brother Judas.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	32	But when Bacchides gat knowledge thereof, he sought for toslay him

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	34	Which when Bacchides understood, he came near to Jordan withall his host upon the sabbath day.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	35	Now Jonathan had sent his brother John, a captain of thepeople, to pray his friends the Nabathites, that they mightleave with them their carriage, which was much.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	36	But the children of Jambri came out of Medaba, and took John,and all that he had, and went their way with it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	37	After this came word to Jonathan and Simon his brother, thatthe children of Jambri made a great marriage, and were bringingthe bride from Nadabatha with a great train, as being thedaughter of one of the great princes of Chanaan.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	38	Therefore they remembered John their brother, and went up,and hid themselves under the covert of the mountain:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	39	Where they lifted up their eyes, and looked, and, behold,there was much ado and great carriage: and the bridegroom cameforth, and his friends and brethren, to meet them with drums,and instruments of musick, and many weapons.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	40	Then Jonathan and they that were with him rose up againstthem from the place where they lay in ambush, and made aslaughter of them in such sort, as many fell down dead, and theremnant fled into the mountain, and they took all their spoils.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	41	Thus was the marriage turned into mourning, and the noise oftheir melody into lamentation.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	42	So when they had avenged fully the blood of their brother,they turned again to the marsh of Jordan.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	43	Now when Bacchides heard hereof, he came on the sabbath dayunto the banks of Jordan with a great power.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	44	Then Jonathan said to his company, Let us go up now and fightfor our lives, for it standeth not with us to day, as in timepast:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	45	For, behold, the battle is before us and behind us, and thewater of Jordan on this side and that side, the marsh likewiseand wood, neither is there place for us to turn aside.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	46	Wherefore cry ye now unto heaven, that ye may be deliveredfrom the hand of your enemies.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	47	With that they joined battle, and Jonathan stretched forthhis hand to smite Bacchides, but he turned back from him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	48	Then Jonathan and they that were with him leapt into Jordan,and swam over unto the other bank: howbeit the other passed notover Jordan unto them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	49	So there were slain of Bacchides' side that day about athousand men.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	50	Afterward returned Bacchides to Jerusalem and repaired thestrong cites in Judea; the fort in Jericho, and Emmaus, andBethhoron, and Bethel, and Thamnatha, Pharathoni, and Taphon,these did he strengthen with high walls, with gates and withbars.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	53	Besides, he took the chief men's sons in the country forhostages, and put them into the tower at Jerusalem to be kept.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	54	Moreover in the hundred fifty and third year, in the secondmonth, Alcimus commanded that the wall of the inner court of thesanctuary should be pulled down; he pulled down also the worksof the prophets
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	55	And as he began to pull down, even at that time was Alcimusplagued, and his enterprizes hindered: for his mouth wasstopped, and he was taken with a palsy, so that he could no morespeak any thing, nor give order concerning his house.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	57	Now when Bacchides saw that Alcimus was dead, he returned tothe king: whereupon the land of Judea was in rest two years.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	58	Then all the ungodly men held a council, saying, Behold,Jonathan and his company are at ease, and dwell without care:now therefore we will bring Bacchides hither, who shall takethem all in one night.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	59	So they went and consulted with him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	60	Then removed he, and came with a great host, and sent lettersprivily to his adherents in Judea, that they should takeJonathan and those that were with him: howbeit they could not,because their counsel was known unto them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	61	Wherefore they took of the men of the country, that wereauthors of that mischief, about fifty persons, and slew them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	62	Afterward Jonathan, and Simon, and they that were with him,got them away to Bethbasi, which is in the wilderness, and theyrepaired the decays thereof, and made it strong.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	63	Which thing when Bacchides knew, he gathered together all hishost, and sent word to them that were of Judea.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	64	Then went he and laid siege against Bethbasi; and they foughtagainst it a long season and made engines of war.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	65	But Jonathan left his brother Simon in the city, and wentforth himself into the country, and with a certain number wenthe forth.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	66	And he smote Odonarkes and his brethren, and the children ofPhasiron in their tent.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	67	And when he began to smite them, and came up with his forces,Simon and his company went out of the city, and burned up theengines of war,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	68	And fought against Bacchides, who was discomfited by them,and they afflicted him sore: for his counsel and travail was invain.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	69	Wherefore he was very wroth at the wicked men that gave himcounsel to come into the country, inasmuch as he slew many ofthem, and purposed to return into his own country.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	70	Whereof when Jonathan had knowledge, he sent ambassadors untohim, to the end he should make peace with him, and deliver themthe prisoners.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	71	Which thing he accepted, and did according to his demands,and sware unto him that he would never do him harm all the daysof his life.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	72	When therefore he had restored unto him the prisoners that hehad taken aforetime out of the land of Judea, he returned andwent his way into his own land, neither came he any more intotheir borders.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	9	73	Thus the sword ceased from Israel: but Jonathan dwelt atMachmas, and began to govern the people; and he destroyed theungodly men out of Israel.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	1	In the hundred and sixtieth year Alexander, the son ofAntiochus surnamed Epiphanes, went up and took Ptolemais: forthe people had received him, by means whereof he reigned there,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	2	Now when king Demetrius heard thereof, he gathered togetheran exceeding great host, and went forth against him to fight.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	3	Moreover Demetrius sent letters unto Jonathan with lovingwords, so as he magnified him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	4	For said he, Let us first make peace with him, before he joinwith Alexander against us:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	5	Else he will remember all the evils that we have done againsthim, and against his brethren and his people.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	6	Wherefore he gave him authority to gather together an host,and to provide weapons, that he might aid him in battle: hecommanded also that the hostages that were in the tower shouldbe delivered him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	7	Then came Jonathan to Jerusalem, and read the letters in theaudience of all the people, and of them that were in the tower:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	8	Who were sore afraid, when they heard that the king had givenhim authority to gather together an host.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	9	Whereupon they of the tower delivered their hostages untoJonathan, and he delivered them unto their parents.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	10	This done, Jonathan settled himself in Jerusalem, and beganto build and repair the city.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	11	And he commanded the workmen to build the walls and the mountSion and about with square stones for fortification; and theydid so.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	12	Then the strangers, that were in the fortresses whichBacchides had built, fled away;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	13	Insomuch as every man left his place, and went into his owncountry.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	14	Only at Bethsura certain of those that had forsaken the lawand the commandments remained still: for it was their place ofrefuge.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	15	Now when king Alexander had heard what promises Demetrius hadsent unto Jonathan: when also it was told him of the battles andnoble acts which he and his brethren had done, and of the painsthat they had endured,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	16	He said, Shall we find such another man? now therefore wewill make him our friend and confederate.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	17	Upon this he wrote a letter, and sent it unto him, accordingto these words, saying,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	18	King Alexander to his brother Jonathan sendeth greeting:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	19	We have heard of thee, that thou art a man of great power,and meet to be our friend.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	20	Wherefore now this day we ordain thee to be the high priestof thy nation, and to be called the king's friend; (andtherewithal he sent him a purple robe and a crown of gold:) andrequire thee to take our part, and keep friendship with us.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	21	So in the seventh month of the hundred and sixtieth year, atthe feast of the tabernacles, Jonathan put on the holy robe, andgathered together forces, and provided much armour.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	22	Whereof when Demetrius heard, he was very sorry, and said,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	23	What have we done, that Alexander hath prevented us in makingamity with the Jews to strengthen himself?
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	24	I also will write unto them words of encouragement, andpromise them dignities and gifts, that I may have their aid.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	25	He sent unto them therefore to this effect: King Demetriusunto the people of the Jews sendeth greeting:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	26	Whereas ye have kept covenants with us, and continued in ourfriendship, not joining yourselves with our enemies, we haveheard hereof, and are glad.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	27	Wherefore now continue ye still to be faithful unto us, andwe will well recompense you for the things ye do in our behalf,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	28	And will grant you many immunities, and give you rewards.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	29	And now do I free you, and for your sake I release all theJews, from tributes, and from the customs of salt, and fromcrown taxes,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	30	And from that which appertaineth unto me to receive for thethird part or the seed, and the half of the fruit of the trees,I release it from this day forth, so that they shall not betaken of the land of Judea, nor of the three governments whichare added thereunto out of the country of Samaria and Galilee,from this day forth for evermore.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	31	Let Jerusalem also be holy and free, with the bordersthereof, both from tenths and tributes.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	32	And as for the tower which is at Jerusalem, I yield upauthority over it, and give the high priest, that he may set init such men as he shall choose to keep it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	33	Moreover I freely set at liberty every one of the Jews, thatwere carried captives out of the land of Judea into any part ofmy kingdom, and I will that all my officers remit the tributeseven of their cattle.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	34	Furthermore I will that all the feasts, and sabbaths, and newmoons, and solemn days, and the three days before the feast, andthe three days after the feast shall be all of immunity andfreedom for all the Jews in my realm.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	35	Also no man shall have authority to meddle with or to molestany of them in any matter.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	36	I will further, that there be enrolled among the king'sforces about thirty thousand men of the Jews, unto whom payshall be given, as belongeth to all king's forces.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	37	And of them some shall be placed in the king's strong holds,of whom also some shall be set over the affairs of the kingdom,which are of trust: and I will that their overseers andgovernors be of themselves, and that they live after their ownlaws, even as the king hath commanded in the land of Judea.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	38	And concerning the three governments that are added to Judeafrom the country of Samaria, let them be joined with Judea, thatthey may be reckoned to be under one, nor bound to obey otherauthority than the high priest's.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	39	As for Ptolemais, and the land pertaining thereto, I give itas a free gift to the sanctuary at Jerusalem for the necessaryexpences of the sanctuary.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	40	Moreover I give every year fifteen thousand shekels of silverout of the king's accounts from the places appertaining.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	41	And all the overplus, which the officers payed not in as informer time, from henceforth shall be given toward the works ofthe temple.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	42	And beside this, the five thousand shekels of silver, whichthey took from the uses of the temple out of the accounts yearby year, even those things shall be released, because theyappertain to the priests that minister.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	43	And whosoever they be that flee unto the temple at Jerusalem,or be within the liberties hereof, being indebted unto the king,or for any other matter, let them be at liberty, and all thatthey have in my realm.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	44	For the building also and repairing of the works of thesanctuary expences shall be given of the king's accounts.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	45	Yea, and for the building of the walls of Jerusalem, and thefortifying thereof round about, expences shall be given out ofthe king's accounts, as also for the building of the walls inJudea.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	46	Now when Jonathan and the people heard these words, they gaveno credit unto them, nor received them, because they rememberedthe great evil that he had done in Israel; for he had afflictedthem very sore.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	47	But with Alexander they were well pleased, because he was thefirst that entreated of true peace with them, and they wereconfederate with him always.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	48	Then gathered king Alexander great forces, and camped overagainst Demetrius.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	49	And after the two kings had joined battle, Demetrius' hostfled: but Alexander followed after him, and prevailed againstthem.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	50	And he continued the battle very sore until the sun wentdown: and that day was Demetrius slain.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	51	Afterward Alexander sent ambassadors to Ptolemee king ofEgypt with a message to this effect:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	52	Forasmuch as I am come again to my realm, and am set in thethrone of my progenitors, and have gotten the dominion, andoverthrown Demetrius, and recovered our country;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	53	For after I had joined battle with him, both he and his hostwas discomfited by us, so that we sit in the throne of hiskingdom:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	54	Now therefore let us make a league of amity together, andgive me now thy daughter to wife: and I will be thy son in law,and will give both thee and her as according to thy dignity.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	55	Then Ptolemee the king gave answer, saying, Happy be the daywherein thou didst return into the land of thy fathers, andsatest in the throne of their kingdom.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	56	And now will I do to thee, as thou hast written: meet metherefore at Ptolemais, that we may see one another; for I willmarry my daughter to thee according to thy desire.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	57	So Ptolemee went out of Egypt with his daughter Cleopatra,and they came unto Ptolemais in the hundred threescore andsecond year:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	58	Where king Alexander meeting him, he gave unto him hisdaughter Cleopatra, and celebrated her marriage at Ptolemaiswith great glory, as the manner of kings is.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	59	Now king Alexander had written unto Jonathan, that he shouldcome and meet him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	60	Who thereupon went honourably to Ptolemais, where he met thetwo kings, and gave them and their friends silver and gold, andmany presents, and found favour in their sight.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	61	At that time certain pestilent fellows of Israel, men of awicked life, assembled themselves against him, to accuse him:but the king would not hear them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	62	Yea more than that, the king commanded to take off hisgarments, and clothe him in purple: and they did so.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	63	And he made him sit by himself, and said into his princes, Gowith him into the midst of the city, and make proclamation, thatno man complain against him of any matter, and that no mantrouble him for any manner of cause.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	64	Now when his accusers saw that he was honored according tothe proclamation, and clothed in purple, they fled all away.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	65	So the king honoured him, and wrote him among his chieffriends, and made him a duke, and partaker of his dominion.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	66	Afterward Jonathan returned to Jerusalem with peace andgladness.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	67	Furthermore in the; hundred threescore and fifth year cameDemetrius son of Demetrius out of Crete into the land of hisfathers:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	68	Whereof when king Alexander heard tell, he was right sorry,and returned into Antioch.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	69	Then Demetrius made Apollonius the governor of Celosyria hisgeneral, who gathered together a great host, and camped inJamnia, and sent unto Jonathan the high priest, saying,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	70	Thou alone liftest up thyself against us, and I am laughed toscorn for thy sake, and reproached: and why dost thou vaunt thypower against us in the mountains?
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	71	Now therefore, if thou trustest in thine own strength, comedown to us into the plain field, and there let us try the mattertogether: for with me is the power of the cities.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	72	Ask and learn who I am, and the rest that take our part, andthey shall tell thee that thy foot is not able to to flight intheir own land.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	73	Wherefore now thou shalt not be able to abide the horsemenand so great a power in the plain, where is neither stone norflint, nor place to flee unto.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	74	So when Jonathan heard these words of Apollonius, he wasmoved in his mind, and choosing ten thousand men he went out ofJerusalem, where Simon his brother met him for to help him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	75	And he pitched his tents against Joppa: but; they of Joppashut him out of the city, because Apollonius had a garrisonthere.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	76	Then Jonathan laid siege unto it: whereupon they of the citylet him in for fear: and so Jonathan won Joppa.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	77	Whereof when Apollonius heard, he took three thousandhorsemen, with a great host of footmen, and went to Azotus asone that journeyed, and therewithal drew him forth into theplain. because he had a great number of horsemen, in whom he puthis trust.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	78	Then Jonathan followed after him to Azotus, where the armiesjoined battle.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	79	Now Apollonius had left a thousand horsemen in ambush.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	80	And Jonathan knew that there was an ambushment behind him;for they had compassed in his host, and cast darts at thepeople, from morning till evening.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	81	But the people stood still, as Jonathan had commanded them:and so the enemies' horses were tired.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	82	Then brought Simon forth his host, and set them against thefootmen, (for the horsemen were spent) who were discomfited byhim, and fled.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	83	The horsemen also, being scattered in the field, fled toAzotus, and went into Bethdagon, their idol's temple, forsafety.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	84	But Jonathan set fire on Azotus, and the cities round aboutit, and took their spoils; and the temple of Dagon, with themthat were fled into it, he burned with fire.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	85	Thus there were burned and slain with the sword well nigheight thousand men.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	87	After this returned Jonathan and his host unto Jerusalem,having any spoils.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	10	89	And sent him a buckle of gold, as the use is to be given tosuch as are of the king's blood: he gave him also Accaron withthe borders thereof in possession.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	1	And the king of Egypt gathered together a great host, likethe sand that lieth upon the sea shore, and many ships, and wentabout through deceit to get Alexander's kingdom, and join it tohis own.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	2	Whereupon he took his journey into Spain in peaceable manner,so as they of the cities opened unto him, and met him: for kingAlexander had commanded them so to do, because he was hisbrother in law.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	3	Now as Ptolemee entered into the cities, he set in every oneof them a garrison of soldiers to keep it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	4	And when he came near to Azotus, they shewed him the templeof Dagon that was burnt, and Azotus and the suburbs thereof thatwere destroyed, and the bodies that were cast abroad and themthat he had burnt in the battle; for they had made heaps of themby the way where he should pass.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	5	Also they told the king whatsoever Jonathan had done, to theintent he might blame him: but the king held his peace.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	10	For I repent that I gave my daughter unto him, for he soughtto slay me.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	11	Thus did he slander him, because he was desirous of hiskingdom.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	12	Wherefore he took his daughter from him, and gave her toDemetrius, and forsook Alexander, so that their hatred wasopenly known.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	13	Then Ptolemee entered into Antioch, where he set two crownsupon his head, the crown of Asia, and of Egypt.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	14	In the mean season was king Alexander in Cilicia, becausethose that dwelt in those parts had revolted from him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	15	But when Alexander heard of this, he came to war against him:whereupon king Ptolemee brought forth his host, and met him witha mighty power, and put him to flight.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	16	So Alexander fled into Arabia there to be defended; but kingPtolemee was exalted:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	17	For Zabdiel the Arabian took off Alexander's head, and sentit unto Ptolemee.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	18	King Ptolemee also died the third day after, and they thatwere in the strong holds were slain one of another.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	19	By this means Demetrius reigned in the hundred threescore andseventh year.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	20	At the same time Jonathan gathered together them that were inJudea to take the tower that was in Jerusalem: and he made manyengines of war against it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	21	Then came ungodly persons, who hated their own people, wentunto the king, and told him that Jonathan besieged the tower,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	22	Whereof when he heard, he was angry, and immediatelyremoving, he came to Ptolemais, and wrote unto Jonathan, that heshould not lay siege to the tower, but come and speak with himat Ptolemais in great haste.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	23	Nevertheless Jonathan, when he heard this, commanded tobesiege it still: and he chose certain of the elders of Israeland the priests, and put himself in peril;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	24	And took silver and gold, and raiment, and divers presentsbesides, and went to Ptolemais unto the king, where he foundfavour in his sight.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	25	And though certain ungodly men of the people had madecomplaints against him,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	26	Yet the king entreated him as his predecessors had donebefore, and promoted him in the sight of all his friends,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	27	And confirmed him in the high priesthood, and in all thehonours that he had before, and gave him preeminence among hischief friends.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	28	Then Jonathan desired the king, that he would make Judea freefrom tribute, as also the three governments, with the country ofSamaria; and he promised him three hundred talents.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	29	So the king consented, and wrote letters unto Jonathan of allthese things after this manner:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	30	King Demetrius unto his brother Jonathan, and unto the nationof the Jews, sendeth greeting:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	31	We send you here a copy of the letter which we did write untoour cousin Lasthenes concerning you, that ye might see it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	32	King Demetrius unto his father Lasthenes sendeth greeting:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	33	We are determined to do good to the people of the Jews, whoare our friends, and keep covenants with us, because of theirgood will toward us.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	34	Wherefore we have ratified unto them the borders of Judea,with the three governments of Apherema and Lydda and Ramathem,that are added unto Judea from the country of Samaria, and allthings appertaining unto them, for all such as do sacrifice inJerusalem, instead of the payments which the king received ofthem yearly aforetime out of the fruits of the earth and oftrees.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	35	And as for other things that belong unto us, of the tithesand customs pertaining unto us, as also the saltpits, and thecrown taxes, which are due unto us, we discharge them of themall for their relief.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	36	And nothing hereof shall be revoked from this time forth forever.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	37	Now therefore see that thou make a copy of these things, andlet it be delivered unto Jonathan, and set upon the holy mountin a conspicuous place.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	38	After this, when king Demetrius saw that the land was quietbefore him, and that no resistance was made against him, he sentaway all his forces, every one to his own place, except certainbands of strangers, whom he had gathered from the isles of theheathen: wherefore all the forces of his fathers hated him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	39	Moreover there was one Tryphon, that had been of Alexander'spart afore, who, seeing that all the host murmured againstDemetrius, went to Simalcue the Arabian that brought upAntiochus the young son of Alexander,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	40	And lay sore upon him to deliver him this young Antiochus,that he might reign in his father's stead: he told him thereforeall that Demetrius had done, and how his men of war were atenmity with him, and there he remained a long season.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	41	In the mean time Jonathan sent unto king Demetrius, that hewould cast those of the tower out of Jerusalem, and those alsoin the fortresses: for they fought against Israel.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	42	So Demetrius sent unto Jonathan, saying, I will not only dothis for thee and thy people, but I will greatly honour thee andthy nation, if opportunity serve.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	43	Now therefore thou shalt do well, if thou send me men to helpme; for all my forces are gone from me.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	44	Upon this Jonathan sent him three thousand strong men untoAntioch: and when they came to the king, the king was very gladof their coming.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	45	Howbeit they that were of the city gathered themselvestogether into the midst of the city, to the number of an hundredand twenty thousand men, and would have slain the king.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	46	Wherefore the king fled into the court, but they of the citykept the passages of the city, and began to fight.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	47	Then the king called to the Jews for help, who came unto himall at once, and dispersing themselves through the city slewthat day in the city to the number of an hundred thousand.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	48	Also they set fire on the city, and gat many spoils that day,and delivered the king.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	49	So when they of the city saw that the Jews had got the cityas they would, their courage was abated: wherefore they madesupplication to the king, and cried, saying,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	50	Grant us peace, and let the Jews cease from assaulting us andthe city.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	51	With that they cast away their weapons, and made peace; andthe Jews were honoured in the sight of the king, and in thesight of all that were in his realm; and they returned toJerusalem, having great spoils.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	52	So king Demetrius sat on the throne of his kingdom, and theland was quiet before him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	53	Nevertheless he dissembled in all that ever he spake, andestranged himself from Jonathan, neither rewarded he himaccording to the benefits which he had received of him, buttroubled him very sore.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	54	After this returned Tryphon, and with him the young childAntiochus, who reigned, and was crowned.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	55	Then there gathered unto him all the men of war, whomDemetrius had put away, and they fought against Demetrius, whoturned his back and fled.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	56	Moreover Tryphon took the elephants, and won Antioch.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	57	At that time young Antiochus wrote unto Jonathan, saying, Iconfirm thee in the high priesthood, and appoint thee ruler overthe four governments, and to be one of the king's friends.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	58	Upon this he sent him golden vessels to be served in, andgave him leave to drink in gold, and to be clothed in purple,and to wear a golden buckle.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	59	His brother Simon also he made captain from the place calledThe ladder of Tyrus unto the borders of Egypt.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	60	Then Jonathan went forth, and passed through the citiesbeyond the water, and all the forces of Syria gatheredthemselves unto him for to help him: and when he came toAscalon, they of the city met him honourably.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	61	From whence he went to Gaza, but they of Gaza shut him out;wherefore he laid siege unto it, and burned the suburbs thereofwith fire, and spoiled them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	62	Afterward, when they of Gaza made supplication unto Jonathan,he made peace with them, and took the sons of their chief menfor hostages, and sent them to Jerusalem, and passed through thecountry unto Damascus.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	63	Now when Jonathan heard that Demetrius' princes were come toCades, which is in Galilee, with a great power, purposing toremove him out of the country,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	64	He went to meet them, and left Simon his brother in thecountry.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	65	Then Simon encamped against Bethsura and fought against it along season, and shut it up:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	66	But they desired to have peace with him, which he grantedthem, and then put them out from thence, and took the city, andset a garrison in it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	67	As for Jonathan and his host, they pitched at the water ofGennesar, from whence betimes in the morning they gat them tothe plain of Nasor.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	68	And, behold, the host of strangers met them in the plain,who, having laid men in ambush for him in the mountains, camethemselves over against him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	69	So when they that lay in ambush rose out of their places andjoined battle, all that were of Jonathan's side fled;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	70	Insomuch as there was not one of them left, except Mattathiasthe son of Absalom, and Judas the son of Calphi, the captains ofthe host.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	71	Then Jonathan rent his clothes, and cast earth upon his head,and prayed.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	72	Afterwards turning again to battle, he put them to flight,and so they ran away.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	73	Now when his own men that were fled saw this, they turnedagain unto him, and with him pursued them to Cades, even untotheir own tents, and there they camped.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	11	74	So there were slain of the heathen that day about threethousand men: but Jonathan returned to Jerusalem.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	1	Now when Jonathan saw that time served him, he chose certainmen, and sent them to Rome, for to confirm and renew thefriendship that they had with them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	2	He sent letters also to the Lacedemonians, and to otherplaces, for the same purpose.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	3	So they went unto Rome, and entered into the senate, andsaid, Jonathan the high priest, and the people of the Jews, sentus unto you, to the end ye should renew the friendship, which yehad with them, and league, as in former time.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	4	Upon this the Romans gave them letters unto the governors ofevery place that they should bring them into the land of Judeapeaceably.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	5	And this is the copy of the letters which Jonathan wrote tothe Lacedemonians:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	6	Jonathan the high priest, and the elders of the nation, andthe priests, and the other of the Jews, unto the Lacedemonianstheir brethren send greeting:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	7	There were letters sent in times past unto Onias the highpriest from Darius, who reigned then among you, to signify thatye are our brethren, as the copy here underwritten doth specify.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	8	At which time Onias entreated the ambassador that was senthonourably, and received the letters, wherein declaration wasmade of the league and friendship.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	9	Therefore we also, albeit we need none of these things, thatwe have the holy books of scripture in our hands to comfort us,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	10	Have nevertheless attempted to send unto you for the renewingof brotherhood and friendship, lest we should become strangersunto you altogether: for there is a long time passed since yesent unto us.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	11	We therefore at all times without ceasing, both in ourfeasts, and other convenient days, do remember you in thesacrifices which we offer, and in our prayers, as reason is, andas it becometh us to think upon our brethren:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	12	And we are right glad of your honour.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	13	As for ourselves, we have had great troubles and wars onevery side, forsomuch as the kings that are round about us havefought against us.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	14	Howbeit we would not be troublesome unto you, nor to othersof our confederates and friends, in these wars:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	15	For we have help from heaven that succoureth us, so as we aredelivered from our enemies, and our enemies are brought underfoot.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	16	For this cause we chose Numenius the son of Antiochus, andAntipater he son of Jason, and sent them unto the Romans, torenew the amity that we had with them, and the former league.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	17	We commanded them also to go unto you, and to salute and todeliver you our letters concerning the renewing of ourbrotherhood.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	18	Wherefore now ye shall do well to give us an answer thereto.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	19	And this is the copy of the letters which Oniares sent.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	20	Areus king of the Lacedemonians to Onias the high priest,greeting:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	21	It is found in writing, that the Lacedemonians and Jews arebrethren, and that they are of the stock of Abraham:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	22	Now therefore, since this is come to our knowledge, ye shalldo well to write unto us of your prosperity.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	23	We do write back again to you, that your cattle and goods areour's, and our's are your's We do command therefore ourambassadors to make report unto you on this wise.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	24	Now when Jonathan heard that Demebius' princes were come tofight against him with a greater host than afore,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	25	He removed from Jerusalem, and met them in the land ofAmathis: for he gave them no respite to enter his country.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	26	He sent spies also unto their tents, who came again, and toldhim that they were appointed to come upon them in the nightseason.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	27	Wherefore so soon as the sun was down, Jonathan commanded hismen to watch, and to be in arms, that all the night long theymight be ready to fight: also he sent forth centinels roundabout the host.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	28	But when the adversaries heard that Jonathan and his men wereready for battle, they feared, and trembled in their hearts, andthey kindled fires in their camp.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	29	Howbeit Jonathan and his company knew it not till themorning: for they saw the lights burning.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	30	Then Jonathan pursued after them, but overtook them not: forthey were gone over the river Eleutherus.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	31	Wherefore Jonathan turned to the Arabians, who were calledZabadeans, and smote them, and took their spoils.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	32	And removing thence, he came to Damascus, and so passedthrough all the country,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	33	Simon also went forth, and passed through the country untoAscalon, and the holds there adjoining, from whence he turnedaside to Joppa, and won it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	34	For he had heard that they would deliver the hold unto themthat took Demetrius' part; wherefore he set a garrison there tokeep it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	35	After this came Jonathan home again, and calling the eldersof the people together, he consulted with them about buildingstrong holds in Judea,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	36	And making the walls of Jerusalem higher, and raising a greatmount between the tower and the city, for to separate it fromthe city, that so it might be alone, that men might neither sellnor buy in it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	37	Upon this they came together to build up the city, forasmuchas part of the wall toward the brook on the east side was fallendown, and they repaired that which was called Caphenatha.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	38	Simon also set up Adida in Sephela, and made it strong withgates and bars.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	39	Now Tryphon went about to get the kingdom of Asia, and tokill Antiochus the king, that he might set the crown upon hisown head.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	40	Howbeit he was afraid that Jonathan would not suffer him, andthat he would fight against him; wherefore he sought a way howto take Jonathan, that he might kill him. So he removed, andcame to Bethsan.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	41	Then Jonathan went out to meet him with forty thousand menchosen for the battle, and came to Bethsan.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	42	Now when Tryphon saw Jonathan came with so great a force, hedurst not stretch his hand against him;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	43	But received him honourably, and commended him unto all hisfriends, and gave him gifts, and commanded his men of war to beas obedient unto him, as to himself.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	44	Unto Jonathan also he said, Why hast thou brought all thispeople to so great trouble, seeing there is no war betwixt us?
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	45	Therefore send them now home again, and choose a few men towait on thee, and come thou with me to Ptolemais, for I willgive it thee, and the rest of the strong holds and forces, andall that have any charge: as for me, I will return and depart:for this is the cause of my coming.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	46	So Jonathan believing him did as he bade him, and sent awayhis host, who went into the land of Judea.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	47	And with himself he retained but three thousand men, of whomhe sent two thousand into Galilee, and one thousand went withhim.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	48	Now as soon as Jonathan entered into Ptolemais, they ofPtolemais shut the gates and took him, and all them that camewith him they slew with the sword.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	49	Then sent Tryphon an host of footmen and horsemen intoGalilee, and into the great plain, to destroy all Jonathan'scompany.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	50	But when they knew that Jonathan and they that were with himwere taken and slain, they encouraged one another; and wentclose together, prepared to fight.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	51	They therefore that followed upon them, perceiving that theywere ready to fight for their lives, turned back again.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	52	Whereupon they all came into the land of Judea peaceably, andthere they bewailed Jonathan, and them that were with him, andthey were sore afraid; wherefore all Israel made greatlamentation.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	12	53	Then all the heathen that were round about then sought todestroy them: for said they, They have no captain, nor any tohelp them: now therefore let us make war upon them, and takeaway their memorial from among men.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	1	Now when Simon heard that Tryphon had gathered together agreat host to invade the land of Judea, and destroy it,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	2	And saw that the people was in great trembling and fear, hewent up to Jerusalem, and gathered the people together,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	3	And gave them exhortation, saying, Ye yourselves know whatgreat things I, and my brethren, and my father's house, havedone for the laws and the sanctuary, the battles also andtroubles which we have seen.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	4	By reason whereof all my brethren are slain for Israel'ssake, and I am left alone.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	5	Now therefore be it far from me, that I should spare mine ownlife in any time of trouble: for I am no better than mybrethren.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	6	Doubtless I will avenge my nation, and the sanctuary, and ourwives, and our children: for all the heathen are gathered todestroy us of very malice.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	7	Now as soon as the people heard these words, their spiritrevived.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	8	And they answered with a loud voice, saying, Thou shalt beour leader instead of Judas and Jonathan thy brother.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	9	Fight thou our battles, and whatsoever, thou commandest us,that will we do.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	10	So then he gathered together all the men of war, and madehaste to finish the walls of Jerusalem, and he fortified itround about.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	11	Also he sent Jonathan the son of Absolom, and with him agreat power, to Joppa: who casting out them that were thereinremained there in it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	12	So Tryphon removed from Ptolemaus with a great power toinvade the land of Judea, and Jonathan was with him in ward.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	13	But Simon pitched his tents at Adida, over against the plain.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	14	Now when Tryphon knew that Simon was risen up instead of hisbrother Jonathan, and meant to join battle with him, he sentmessengers unto him, saying,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	15	Whereas we have Jonathan thy brother in hold, it is for moneythat he is owing unto the king's treasure, concerning thebusiness that was committed unto him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	16	Wherefore now send an hundred talents of silver, and two ofhis sons for hostages, that when he is at liberty he may notrevolt from us, and we will let him go.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	17	Hereupon Simon, albeit he perceived that they spakedeceitfully unto him yet sent he the money and the children,lest peradventure he should procure to himself great hatred ofthe people:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	18	Who might have said, Because I sent him not the money and thechildren, therefore is Jonathan dead.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	19	So he sent them the children and the hundred talents: howbeitTryphon dissembled neither would he let Jonathan go.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	20	And after this came Tryphon to invade the land, and destroyit, going round about by the way that leadeth unto Adora: butSimon and his host marched against him in every place,wheresoever he went.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	21	Now they that were in the tower sent messengers unto Tryphon,to the end that he should hasten his coming unto them by thewilderness, and send them victuals.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	22	Wherefore Tryphon made ready all his horsemen to come thatnight: but there fell a very great snow, by reason whereof hecame not. So he departed, and came into the country of Galaad.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	23	And when he came near to Bascama he slew Jonathan, who wasburied there.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	24	Afterward Tryphon returned and went into his own land.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	25	Then sent Simon, and took the bones of Jonathan his brother,and buried them in Modin, the city of his fathers.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	26	And all Israel made great lamentation for him, and bewailedhim many days.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	27	Simon also built a monument upon the sepulchre of his fatherand his brethren, and raised it aloft to the sight, with hewnstone behind and before.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	28	Moreover he set up seven pyramids, one against another, forhis father, and his mother, and his four brethren.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	29	And in these he made cunning devices, about the which he setgreat pillars, and upon the pillars he made all their armour fora perpetual memory, and by the armour ships carved, that theymight be seen of all that sail on the sea.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	30	This is the sepulchre which he made at Modin, and it standethyet unto this day.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	38	And whatsoever covenants we have made with you shall stand;and the strong holds, which ye have builded, shall be your own.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	39	As for any oversight or fault committed unto this day, weforgive it, and the crown tax also, which ye owe us: and ifthere were any other tribute paid in Jerusalem, it shall no morebe paid.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	40	And look who are meet among you to be in our court, let thenbe enrolled, and let there be peace betwixt us.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	41	Thus the yoke of the heathen was taken away from Israel inthe hundred and seventieth year.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	43	In those days Simon camped against Gaza and besieged it roundabout; he made also an engine of war, and set it by the city,and battered a certain tower, and took it.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	44	And they that were in the engine leaped into the city;whereupon there was a great uproar in the city:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	45	Insomuch as the people of the city rent their clothes, andclimbed upon the walls with their wives and children, and criedwith a loud voice, beseeching Simon to grant them peace.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	46	And they said, Deal not with us according to our wickedness,but according to thy mercy.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	47	So Simon was appeased toward them, and fought no more againstthem, but put them out of the city, and cleansed the houseswherein the idols were, and so entered into it with songs andthanksgiving.
