The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	49	They also of the tower in Jerusalem were kept so strait, thatthey could neither come forth, nor go into the country, nor buy,nor sell: wherefore they were in great distress for want ofvictuals, and a great number of them perished through famine.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	13	50	Then cried they to Simon, beseeching him to be at one withthem: which thing he granted them; and when he had put them outfrom thence, he cleansed the tower from pollutions:

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	32	At which time Simon rose up, and fought for his nation, andspent much of his own substance, and armed the valiant men ofhis nation and gave them wages,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	33	And fortified the cities of Judea, together with Bethsura,that lieth upon the borders of Judea, where the armour of theenemies had been before; but he set a garrison of Jews there:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	34	Moreover he fortified Joppa, which lieth upon the sea, andGazera, that bordereth upon Azotus, where the enemies had dweltbefore: but he placed Jews there, and furnished them with allthings convenient for the reparation thereof.)
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	35	The people therefore sang the acts of Simon, and unto whatglory he thought to bring his nation, made him their governorand chief priest, because he had done all these things, and forthe justice and faith which he kept to his nation, and for thathe sought by all means to exalt his people.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	36	For in his time things prospered in his hands, so that theheathen were taken out of their country, and they also that werein the city of David in Jerusalem, who had made themselves atower, out of which they issued, and polluted all about thesanctuary, and did much hurt in the holy place:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	37	But he placed Jews therein. and fortified it for the safetyof the country and the city, and raised up the walls ofJerusalem.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	38	King Demetrius also confirmed him in the high priesthoodaccording to those things,
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	39	And made him one of his friends, and honoured him with greathonour.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	40	For he had heard say, that the Romans had called the Jewstheir friends and confederates and brethren; and that they hadentertained the ambassadors of Simon honourably;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	41	Also that the Jews and priests were well pleased that Simonshould be their governor and high priest for ever, until thereshould arise a faithful prophet;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	42	Moreover that he should be their captain, and should takecharge of the sanctuary, to set them over their works, and overthe country, and over the armour, and over the fortresses, that,I say, he should take charge of the sanctuary;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	43	Beside this, that he should be obeyed of every man, and thatall the writings in the country should be made in his name, andthat he should be clothed in purple, and wear gold:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	44	Also that it should be lawful for none of the people orpriests to break any of these things, or to gainsay his words,or to gather an assembly in the country without him, or to beclothed in purple, or wear a buckle of gold;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	45	And whosoever should do otherwise, or break any of thesethings, he should be punished.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	46	Thus it liked all the people to deal with Simon, and to do ashath been said.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	47	Then Simon accepted hereof, and was well pleased to be highpriest, and captain and governor of the Jews and priests, and todefend them all.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	48	So they commanded that this writing should be put in tablesof brass, and that they should be set up within the compass ofthe sanctuary in a conspicuous place;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	14	49	Also that the copies thereof should be laid up in thetreasury, to the end that Simon and his sons might have them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	1	Moreover Antiochus son of Demetrius the king sent lettersfrom the isles of the sea unto Simon the priest and prince ofthe Jews, and to all the people;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	2	The contents whereof were these: King Antiochus to Simon thehigh priest and prince of his nation, and to the people of theJews, greeting:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	3	Forasmuch as certain pestilent men have usurped the kingdomof our fathers, and my purpose is to challenge it again, that Imay restore it to the old estate, and to that end have gathereda multitude of foreign soldiers together, and prepared ships ofwar;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	4	My meaning also being to go through the country, that I maybe avenged of them that have destroyed it, and made many citiesin the kingdom desolate:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	5	Now therefore I confirm unto thee all the oblations which thekings before me granted thee, and whatsoever gifts besides theygranted.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	6	I give thee leave also to coin money for thy country withthine own stamp.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	7	And as concerning Jerusalem and the sanctuary, let them befree; and all the armour that thou hast made, and fortressesthat thou hast built, and keepest in thine hands, let themremain unto thee.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	8	And if anything be, or shall be, owing to the king, let it beforgiven thee from this time forth for evermore.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	9	Furthermore, when we have obtained our kingdom, we willhonour thee, and thy nation, and thy temple, with great honour,so that your honour shall be known throughout the world.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	10	In the hundred threescore and fourteenth year went Antiochusinto the land of his fathers: at which time all the forces cametogether unto him, so that few were left with Tryphon.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	11	Wherefore being pursued by king Antiochus, he fled unto Dora,which lieth by the sea side:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	12	For he saw that troubles came upon him all at once, and thathis forces had forsaken him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	13	Then camped Antiochus against Dora, having with him anhundred and twenty thousand men of war, and eight thousandhorsemen.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	14	And when he had compassed the city round about, and joinedships close to the town on the sea side, he vexed the city byland and by sea, neither suffered he any to go out or in.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	15	In the mean season came Numenius and his company from Rome,having letters to the kings and countries; wherein were writtenthese things:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	16	Lucius, consul of the Romans unto king Ptolemee, greeting:

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	18	And they brought a shield of gold of a thousand pound.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	19	We thought it good therefore to write unto the kings andcountries, that they should do them no harm, nor fight againstthem, their cities, or countries, nor yet aid their enemiesagainst them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	20	It seemed also good to us to receive the shield of them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	21	If therefore there be any pestilent fellows, that have fledfrom their country unto you, deliver them unto Simon the highpriest, that he may punish them according to their own law.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	22	The same things wrote he likewise unto Demetrius the king,and Attalus, to Ariarathes, and Arsaces,

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	25	So Antiochus the king camped against Dora the second day,assaulting it continually, and making engines, by which means heshut up Tryphon, that he could neither go out nor in.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	26	At that time Simon sent him two thousand chosen men to aidhim; silver also, and gold, and much armour.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	27	Nevertheless he would not receive them, but brake all thecovenants which he had made with him afore, and became strangeunto him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	28	Furthermore he sent unto him Athenobius, one of his friends,to commune with him, and say, Ye withhold Joppa and Gazera; withthe tower that is in Jerusalem, which are cities of my realm.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	29	The borders thereof ye have wasted, and done great hurt inthe land, and got the dominion of many places within my kingdom.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	30	Now therefore deliver the cities which ye have taken, and thetributes of the places, whereof ye have gotten dominion withoutthe borders of Judea:
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	31	Or else give me for them five hundred talents of silver; andfor the harm that ye have done, and the tributes of the cities,other five hundred talents: if not, we will come and fightagainst you
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	32	So Athenobius the king's friend came to Jerusalem: and whenhe saw the glory of Simon, and the cupboard of gold and silverplate, and his great attendance, he was astonished, and told himthe king's message.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	33	Then answered Simon, and said unto him, We have neither takenother men's land, nor holden that which appertaineth to others,but the inheritance of our fathers, which our enemies hadwrongfully in possession a certain time.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	34	Wherefore we, having opportunity, hold the inheritance of ourfathers.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	35	And whereas thou demandest Joppa and Gazera, albeit they didgreat harm unto the people in our country, yet will we give theean hundred talents for them. Hereunto Athenobius answered himnot a word;
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	36	But returned in a rage to the king, and made report unto himof these speeches, and of the glory of Simon, and of all that hehad seen: whereupon the king was exceeding wroth.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	37	In the mean time fled Tryphon by ship unto Orthosias.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	15	39	And commanded him to remove his host toward Judea; also hecommanded him to build up Cedron, and to fortify the gates, andto war against the people; but as for the king himself, hepursued Tryphon.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	1	Then came up John from Gazera, and told Simon his father whatCendebeus had done.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	2	Wherefore Simon called his two eldest sons, Judas and John,and said unto them, I, and my brethren, and my father's house,have ever from my youth unto this day fought against the enemiesof Israel; and things have prospered so well in our hands, thatwe have delivered Israel oftentimes.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	3	But now I am old, and ye, by God's mercy, are of a sufficientage: be ye instead of me and my brother, and go and fight forour nation, and the help from heaven be with you.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	4	So he chose out of the country twenty thousand men of warwith horsemen, who went out against Cendebeus, and rested thatnight at Modin.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	5	And when as they rose in the morning, and went into theplain, behold, a mighty great host both of footmen and horsemencame against them: howbeit there was a water brook betwixt them.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	6	So he and his people pitched over against them: and when hesaw that the people were afraid to go over the water brook, hewent first over himself, and then the men seeing him passedthrough after him.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	7	That done, he divided his men, and set the horsemen in themidst of the footmen: for the enemies' horsemen were very many.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	8	Then sounded they with the holy trumpets: whereupon Cendebeusand his host were put to flight, so that many of them wereslain, and the remnant gat them to the strong hold.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	9	At that time was Judas John's brother wounded; but John stillfollowed after them, until he came to Cedron, which Cendebeushad built.
The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	10	So they fled even unto the towers in the fields of Azotus;wherefore he burned it with fire: so that there were slain ofthem about two thousand men. Afterward he returned into the landof Judea in peace.

The First Book of The Maccabees	1Mac	16	14	Now Simon was visiting the cities that were in the country,and taking care for the good ordering of them; at which time hecame down himself to Jericho with his sons, Mattathias andJudas, in the hundred threescore and seventeenth year, in theeleventh month, called Sabat:

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	1	21	Then commanded he them to draw it up, and to bring it; andwhen the sacrifices were laid on, Neemias commanded the prieststo sprinkle the wood and the things laid thereupon with thewater.

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	18	As he promised in the law, will shortly have mercy upon us,and gather us together out of every land under heaven into theholy place: for he hath delivered us out of great troubles, andhath purified the place.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	19	Now as concerning Judas Maccabeus, and his brethren, and thepurification of the great temple, and the dedication of thealtar,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	20	And the wars against Antiochus Epiphanes, and Eupator hisson,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	21	And the manifest signs that came from heaven unto those thatbehaved themselves manfully to their honour for Judaism: sothat, being but a few, they overcame the whole country, andchased barbarous multitudes,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	22	And recovered again the temple renowned all the world over,and freed the city, and upheld the laws which were going down,the Lord being gracious unto them with all favour:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	23	All these things, I say, being declared by Jason of Cyrene infive books, we will assay to abridge in one volume.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	24	For considering the infinite number, and the difficulty whichthey find that desire to look into the narrations of the story,for the variety of the matter,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	25	We have been careful, that they that will read may havedelight, and that they that are desirous to commit to memorymight have ease, and that all into whose hands it comes mighthave profit.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	26	Therefore to us, that have taken upon us this painful labourof abridging, it was not easy, but a matter of sweat andwatching;
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	27	Even as it is no ease unto him that prepareth a banquet, andseeketh the benefit of others: yet for the pleasuring of many wewill undertake gladly this great pains;
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	28	Leaving to the author the exact handling of every particular,and labouring to follow the rules of an abridgement.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	29	For as the master builder of a new house must care for thewhole building; but he that undertaketh to set it out, and paintit, must seek out fit things for the adorning thereof: even so Ithink it is with us.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	30	To stand upon every point, and go over things at large, andto be curious in particulars, belongeth to the first author ofthe story:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	31	But to use brevity, and avoid much labouring of the work, isto be granted to him that will make an abridgment.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	2	32	Here then will we begin the story: only adding thus much tothat which hath been said, that it is a foolish thing to make along prologue, and to be short in the story itself.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	1	Now when the holy city was inhabited with all peace, and thelaws were kept very well, because of the godliness of Onias thehigh priest, and his hatred of wickedness,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	2	It came to pass that even the kings themselves did honour theplace, and magnify the temple with their best gifts;
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	3	Insomuch that Seleucus of Asia of his own revenues bare allthe costs belonging to the service of the sacrifices.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	4	But one Simon of the tribe of Benjamin, who was made governorof the temple, fell out with the high priest about disorder inthe city.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	5	And when he could not overcome Onias, he gat him toApollonius the son of Thraseas, who then was governor ofCelosyria and Phenice,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	6	And told him that the treasury in Jerusalem was full ofinfinite sums of money, so that the multitude of their riches,which did not pertain to the account of the sacrifices, wasinnumerable, and that it was possible to bring all into theking's hand.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	7	Now when Apollonius came to the king, and had shewed him ofthe money whereof he was told, the king chose out Heliodorus histreasurer, and sent him with a commandment to bring him theforesaid money.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	8	So forthwith Heliodorus took his journey; under a colour ofvisiting the cities of Celosyria and Phenice, but indeed tofulfil the king's purpose.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	9	And when he was come to Jerusalem, and had been courteouslyreceived of the high priest of the city, he told him whatintelligence was given of the money, and declared wherefore hecame, and asked if these things were so indeed.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	10	Then the high priest told him that there was such money laidup for the relief of widows and fatherless children:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	11	And that some of it belonged to Hircanus son of Tobias, a manof great dignity, and not as that wicked Simon had misinformed:the sum whereof in all was four hundred talents of silver, andtwo hundred of gold:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	12	And that it was altogether impossible that such wrongs shouldbe done unto them, that had committed it to the holiness of theplace, and to the majesty and inviolable sanctity of the temple,honoured over all the world.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	13	But Heliodorus, because of the king's commandment given him,said, That in any wise it must be brought into the king'streasury.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	14	So at the day which he appointed he entered in to order thismatter: wherefore there was no small agony throughout the wholecity.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	15	But the priests, prostrating themselves before the altar intheir priests' vestments, called unto heaven upon him that madea law concerning things given to he kept, that they shouldsafely be preserved for such as had committed them to be kept.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	16	Then whoso had looked the high priest in the face, it wouldhave wounded his heart: for his countenance and the changing ofhis colour declared the inward agony of his mind.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	17	For the man was so compassed with fear and horror of thebody, that it was manifest to them that looked upon him, whatsorrow he had now in his heart.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	18	Others ran flocking out of their houses to the generalsupplication, because the place was like to come into contempt.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	19	And the women, girt with sackcloth under their breasts,abounded in the streets, and the virgins that were kept in ran,some to the gates, and some to the walls, and others looked outof the windows.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	20	And all, holding their hands toward heaven, madesupplication.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	21	Then it would have pitied a man to see the falling down ofthe multitude of all sorts, and the fear of the high priestbeing in such an agony.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	22	They then called upon the Almighty Lord to keep the thingscommitted of trust safe and sure for those that had committedthem.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	23	Nevertheless Heliodorus executed that which was decreed.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	24	Now as he was there present himself with his guard about thetreasury, the Lord of spirits, and the Prince of all power,caused a great apparition, so that all that presumed to come inwith him were astonished at the power of God, and fainted, andwere sore afraid.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	25	For there appeared unto them an horse with a terrible riderupon him, and adorned with a very fair covering, and he ranfiercely, and smote at Heliodorus with his forefeet, and itseemed that he that sat upon the horse had complete harness ofgold.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	26	Moreover two other young men appeared before him, notable instrength, excellent in beauty, and comely in apparel, who stoodby him on either side; and scourged him continually, and gavehim many sore stripes.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	27	And Heliodorus fell suddenly unto the ground, and wascompassed with great darkness: but they that were with himtook him up, and put him into a litter.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	28	Thus him, that lately came with a great train and with allhis guard into the said treasury, they carried out, being unableto help himself with his weapons: and manifestly theyacknowledged the power of God.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	29	For he by the hand of God was cast down, and lay speechlesswithout all hope of life.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	30	But they praised the Lord, that had miraculously honoured hisown place: for the temple; which a little afore was full of fearand trouble, when the Almighty Lord appeared, was filled withjoy and gladness.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	31	Then straightways certain of Heliodorus' friends prayedOnias, that he would call upon the most High to grant him hislife, who lay ready to give up the ghost.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	32	So the high priest, suspecting lest the king shouldmisconceive that some treachery had been done to Heliodorus bythe Jews, offered a sacrifice for the health of the man.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	33	Now as the high priest was making an atonement, the sameyoung men in the same clothing appeared and stood besideHeliodorus, saying, Give Onias the high priest great thanks,insomuch as for his sake the Lord hath granted thee life:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	34	And seeing that thou hast been scourged from heaven, declareunto all men the mighty power of God. And when they had spokenthese words, they appeared no more.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	35	So Heliodorus, after he had offered sacrifice unto the Lord,and made great vows unto him that had saved his life, andsaluted Onias, returned with his host to the king.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	36	Then testified he to all men the works of the great God,which he had seen with his eyes.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	37	And when the king Heliodorus, who might be a fit man to besent yet once again to Jerusalem, he said,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	38	If thou hast any enemy or traitor, send him thither, and thoushalt receive him well scourged, if he escape with his life: forin that place, no doubt; there is an especial power of God.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	39	For he that dwelleth in heaven hath his eye on that place,and defendeth it; and he beateth and destroyeth them that cometo hurt it.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	3	40	And the things concerning Heliodorus, and the keeping of thetreasury, fell out on this sort.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	1	This Simon now, of whom we spake afore, having been abetrayer of the money, and of his country, slandered Onias, asif he ha terrified Heliodorus, and been the worker of theseevils.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	2	Thus was he bold to call him a traitor, that had deservedwell of the city, and tendered his own nation, and was sozealous of the laws.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	3	But when their hatred went so far, that by one of Simon'sfaction murders were committed,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	4	Onias seeing the danger of this contention, and thatApollonius, as being the governor of Celosyria and Phenice, didrage, and increase Simon's malice,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	5	He went to the king, not to be an accuser of his countrymen,but seeking the good of all, both publick and private:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	6	For he saw that it was impossible that the state shouldcontinue quiet, and Simon leave his folly, unless the king didlook thereunto.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	7	But after the death of Seleucus, when Antiochus, calledEpiphanes, took the kingdom, Jason the brother of Onias labouredunderhand to be high priest,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	8	Promising unto the king by intercession three hundred andthreescore talents of silver, and of another revenue eightytalents:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	9	Beside this, he promised to assign an hundred and fifty more,if he might have licence to set him up a place for exercise, andfor the training up of youth in the fashions of the heathen, andto write them of Jerusalem by the name of Antiochians.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	10	Which when the king had granted, and he had gotten into hishand the rule he forthwith brought his own nation to Greekishfashion.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	11	And the royal privileges granted of special favour to theJews by the means of John the father of Eupolemus, who wentambassador to Rome for amity and aid, he took away; and puttingdown the governments which were according to the law, he broughtup new customs against the law:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	12	For he built gladly a place of exercise under the toweritself, and brought the chief young men under his subjection,and made them wear a hat.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	13	Now such was the height of Greek fashions, and increase ofheathenish manners, through the exceeding profaneness of Jason,that ungodly wretch, and no high priest;
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	14	That the priests had no courage to serve any more at thealtar, but despising the temple, and neglecting the sacrifices,hastened to be partakers of the unlawful allowance in the placeof exercise, after the game of Discus called them forth;
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	15	Not setting by the honours of their fathers, but liking theglory of the Grecians best of all.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	16	By reason whereof sore calamity came upon them: for they hadthem to be their enemies and avengers, whose custom theyfollowed so earnestly, and unto whom they desired to be like inall things.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	17	For it is not a light thing to do wickedly against the lawsof God: but the time following shall declare these things.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	18	Now when the game that was used every faith year was kept atTyrus, the king being present,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	19	This ungracious Jason sent special messengers from Jerusalem,who were Antiochians, to carry three hundred drachms of silverto the sacrifice of Hercules, which even the bearers thereofthought fit not to bestow upon the sacrifice, because it was notconvenient, but to be reserved for other charges.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	20	This money then, in regard of the sender, was appointed toHercules' sacrifice; but because of the bearers thereof, it wasemployed to the making of gallies.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	21	Now when Apollonius the son of Menestheus was sent into Egyptfor the coronation of king Ptolemeus Philometor, Antiochus,understanding him not to be well affected to his affairs,provided for his own safety: whereupon he came to Joppa, andfrom thence to Jerusalem:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	22	Where he was honourably received of Jason, and of the city,and was brought in with torch alight, and with great shoutings:and so afterward went with his host unto Phenice.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	23	Three years afterward Jason sent Menelaus, the aforesaidSimon's brother, to bear the money unto the king, and to put himin mind of certain necessary matters.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	24	But he being brought to the presence of the king, when he hadmagnified him for the glorious appearance of his power, got thepriesthood to himself, offering more than Jason by three hundredtalents of silver.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	25	So he came with the king's mandate, bringing nothing worthythe high priesthood, but having the fury of a cruel tyrant, andthe rage of a savage beast.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	26	Then Jason, who had undermined his own brother, beingundermined by another, was compelled to flee into the country ofthe Ammonites.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	27	So Menelaus got the principality: but as for the money thathe had promised unto the king, he took no good order for it,albeit Sostratis the ruler of the castle required it:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	28	For unto him appertained the gathering of the customs.Wherefore they were both called before the king.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	29	Now Menelaus left his brother Lysimachus in his stead in thepriesthood; and Sostratus left Crates, who was governor of theCyprians.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	30	While those things were in doing, they of Tarsus and Mallosmade insurrection, because they were given to the king'sconcubine, called Antiochus.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	31	Then came the king in all haste to appease matters, leavingAndronicus, a man in authority, for his deputy.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	32	Now Menelaus, supposing that he had gotten a convenient time,stole certain vessels of gold out of the temple, and gave someof them to Andronicus, and some he sold into Tyrus and thecities round about.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	33	Which when Onias knew of a surety, he reproved him, andwithdrew himself into a sanctuary at Daphne, that lieth byAntiochia.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	34	Wherefore Menelaus, taking Andronicus apart, prayed, him toget Onias into his hands; who being persuaded thereunto, andcoming to Onias in deceit, gave him his right hand with oaths;and though he were suspected by him, yet persuaded he him tocome forth of the sanctuary: whom forthwith he shut up withoutregard of justice.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	35	For the which cause not only the Jews, but many also of othernations, took great indignation, and were much grieved for theunjust murder of the man.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	36	And when the king was come again from the places aboutCilicia, the Jews that were in the city, and certain of theGreeks that abhorred the fact also, complained because Onias wasslain without cause.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	37	Therefore Antiochus was heartily sorry, and moved to pity,and wept, because of the sober and modest behaviour of him thatwas dead.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	38	And being kindled with anger, forthwith he took awayAndronicus his purple, and rent off his clothes, and leading himthrough the whole city unto that very place, where he hadcommitted impiety against Onias, there slew he the cursedmurderer. Thus the Lord rewarded him his punishment, as he haddeserved.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	39	Now when many sacrileges had been committed in the city byLysimachus with the consent of Menelaus, and the fruit thereofwas spread abroad, the multitude gathered themselves togetheragainst Lysimachus, many vessels of gold being already carriedaway.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	40	Whereupon the common people rising, and being filled withrage, Lysimachus armed about three thousand men, and began firstto offer violence; one Auranus being the leader, a man far gonein years, and no less in folly.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	41	They then seeing the attempt of Lysimachus, some of themcaught stones, some clubs, others taking handfuls of dust, thatwas next at hand, cast them all together upon Lysimachus, andthose that set upon them.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	42	Thus many of them they wounded, and some they struck to theground, and all of them they forced to flee: but as for thechurchrobber himself, him they killed beside the treasury.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	43	Of these matters therefore there was an accusation laidagainst Menelaus.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	44	Now when the king came to Tyrus, three men that were sentfrom the senate pleaded the cause before him:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	45	But Menelaus, being now convicted, promised Ptolemee the sonof Dorymenes to give him much money, if he would pacify the kingtoward him.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	46	Whereupon Ptolemee taking the king aside into a certaingallery, as it were to take the air, brought him to be ofanother mind:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	47	Insomuch that he discharged Menelaus from the accusations,who notwithstanding was cause of all the mischief: and thosepoor men, who, if they had told their cause, yea, before theScythians, should have been judged innocent, them he condemnedto death.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	48	Thus they that followed the matter for the city, and for thepeople, and for the holy vessels, did soon suffer unjustpunishment.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	49	Wherefore even they of Tyrus, moved with hatred of thatwicked deed, caused them to be honourably buried.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	4	50	And so through the covetousness of them that were of powerMenelaus remained still in authority, increasing in malice, andbeing a great traitor to the citizens.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	1	About the same time Antiochus prepared his second voyage intoEgypt:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	2	And then it happened, that through all the city, for thespace almost of forty days, there were seen horsemen running inthe air, in cloth of gold, and armed with lances, like a band ofsoldiers,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	3	And troops of horsemen in array, encountering and running oneagainst another, with shaking of shields, and multitude ofpikes, and drawing of swords, and casting of darts, andglittering of golden ornaments, and harness of all sorts.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	4	Wherefore every man prayed that that apparition might turn togood.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	5	Now when there was gone forth a false rumour, as thoughAntiochus had been dead, Jason took at the least a thousand men,and suddenly made an assault upon the city; and they that wereupon the walls being put back, and the city at length taken,Menelaus fled into the castle:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	6	But Jason slew his own citizens without mercy, notconsidering that to get the day of them of his own nation wouldbe a most unhappy day for him; but thinking they had been hisenemies, and not his countrymen, whom he conquered.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	7	Howbeit for all this he obtained not the principality, but atthe last received shame for the reward of his treason, and fledagain into the country of the Ammonites.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	8	In the end therefore he had an unhappy return, being accusedbefore Aretas the king of the Arabians, fleeing from city tocity, pursued of all men, hated as a forsaker of the laws, andbeing had in abomination as an open enemy of his country andcountrymen, he was cast out into Egypt.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	9	Thus he that had driven many out of their country perished ina strange land, retiring to the Lacedemonians, and thinkingthere to find succour by reason of his kindred:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	10	And he that had cast out many unburied had none to mourn forhim, nor any solemn funerals at all, nor sepulchre with hisfathers.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	11	Now when this that was done came to the king's car, hethought that Judea had revolted: whereupon removing out of Egyptin a furious mind, he took the city by force of arms,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	12	And commanded his men of war not to spare such as they met,and to slay such as went up upon the houses.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	13	Thus there was killing of young and old, making away of men,women, and children, slaying of virgins and infants.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	14	And there were destroyed within the space of three whole daysfourscore thousand, whereof forty thousand were slain in theconflict; and no fewer sold than slain.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	15	Yet was he not content with this, but presumed to go intothe most holy temple of all the world; Menelaus, that traitor tothe laws, and to his own country, being his guide:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	16	And taking the holy vessels with polluted hands, and withprofane hands pulling down the things that were dedicated byother kings to the augmentation and glory and honour of theplace, he gave them away.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	17	And so haughty was Antiochus in mind, that he considered notthat the Lord was angry for a while for the sins of them thatdwelt in the city, and therefore his eye was not upon the place.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	18	For had they not been formerly wrapped in many sins, thisman, as soon as he had come, had forthwith been scourged, andput back from his presumption, as Heliodorus was, whom Seleucusthe king sent to view the treasury.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	19	Nevertheless God did not choose the people for the place'ssake, but the place far the people's sake.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	20	And therefore the place itself, that was partaker with themof the adversity that happened to the nation, did afterwardcommunicate in the benefits sent from the Lord: and as it wasforsaken in the wrath of the Almighty, so again, the great Lordbeing reconciled, it was set up with all glory.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	21	So when Antiochus had carried out of the temple a thousandand eight hundred talents, he departed in all haste untoAntiochia, weening in his pride to make the land navigable, andthe sea passable by foot: such was the haughtiness of his mind.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	22	And he left governors to vex the nation: at Jerusalem,Philip, for his country a Phrygian, and for manners morebarbarous than he that set him there;
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	23	And at Garizim, Andronicus; and besides, Menelaus, who worsethan all the rest bare an heavy hand over the citizens, having amalicious mind against his countrymen the Jews.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	24	He sent also that detestable ringleader Apollonius with anarmy of two and twenty thousand, commanding him to slay allthose that were in their best age, and to sell the women and theyounger sort:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	25	Who coming to Jerusalem, and pretending peace, did forbeartill the holy day of the sabbath, when taking the Jews keepingholy day, he commanded his men to arm themselves.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	26	And so he slew all them that were gone to the celebrating ofthe sabbath, and running through the city with weapons slewgreat multitudes.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	5	27	But Judas Maccabeus with nine others, or thereabout, withdrewhimself into the wilderness, and lived in the mountains afterthe manner of beasts, with his company, who fed on herbscontinually, lest they should be partakers of the pollution.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	1	Not long after this the king sent an old man of Athens tocompel the Jews to depart from the laws of their fathers, andnot to live after the laws of God:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	2	And to pollute also the temple in Jerusalem, and to call itthe temple of Jupiter Olympius; and that in Garizim, of Jupiterthe Defender of strangers, as they did desire that dwelt in theplace.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	3	The coming in of this mischief was sore and grievous to thepeople:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	4	For the temple was filled with riot and revelling by theGentiles, who dallied with harlots, and had to do with womenwithin the circuit of the holy places, and besides that broughtin things that were not lawful.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	5	The altar also was filled with profane things, which the lawforbiddeth.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	6	Neither was it lawful for a man to keep sabbath days orancient fasts, or to profess himself at all to be a Jew.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	7	And in the day of the king's birth every month they werebrought by bitter constraint to eat of the sacrifices; and whenthe fast of Bacchus was kept, the Jews were compelled to go inprocession to Bacchus, carrying ivy.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	8	Moreover there went out a decree to the neighbour cities ofthe heathen, by the suggestion of Ptolemee, against the Jews,that they should observe the same fashions, and be partakers oftheir sacrifices:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	9	And whoso would not conform themselves to the manners of theGentiles should be put to death. Then might a man have seen thepresent misery.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	10	For there were two women brought, who had circumcised theirchildren; whom when they had openly led round about the city,the babes handing at their breasts, they cast them down headlongfrom the wall.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	11	And others, that had run together into caves near by, to keepthe sabbath day secretly, being discovered by Philip, were allburnt together, because they made a conscience to helpthemselves for the honour of the most sacred day.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	12	Now I beseech those that read this book, that they be notdiscouraged for these calamities, but that they judge thosepunishments not to be for destruction, but for a chastening ofour nation.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	13	For it is a token of his great goodness, when wicked doersare not suffered any long time, but forthwith punished.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	14	For not as with other nations, whom the Lord patientlyforbeareth to punish, till they be come to the fulness of theirsins, so dealeth he with us,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	15	Lest that, being come to the height of sin, afterwards heshould take vengeance of us.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	16	And therefore he never withdraweth his mercy from us: andthough he punish with adversity, yet doth he never forsake hispeople.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	17	But let this that we at spoken be for a warning unto us. Andnow will we come to the declaring of the matter in a few words.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	18	Eleazar, one of the principal scribes, an aged man, and of awell favoured countenance, was constrained to open his mouth,and to eat swine's flesh.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	19	But he, choosing rather to die gloriously, than to livestained with such an abomination, spit it forth, and came of hisown accord to the torment,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	20	As it behoved them to come, that are resolute to stand outagainst such things, as are not lawful for love of life to betasted.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	21	But they that had the charge of that wicked feast, for theold acquaintance they had with the man, taking him aside,besought him to bring flesh of his own provision, such as waslawful for him to use, and make as if he did eat of the fleshtaken from the sacrifice commanded by the king;
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	22	That in so doing he might be delivered from death, and forthe old friendship with them find favour.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	23	But he began to consider discreetly, and as became his age,and the excellency of his ancient years, and the honour of hisgray head, whereon was come, and his most honest education froma child, or rather the holy law made and given by God: thereforehe answered accordingly, and willed them straightways to sendhim to the grave.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	24	For it becometh not our age, said he, in any wise todissemble, whereby many young persons might think that Eleazar,being fourscore years old and ten, were now gone to a strangereligion;
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	25	And so they through mine hypocrisy, and desire to live alittle time and a moment longer, should be deceived by me, and Iget a stain to mine old age, and make it abominable.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	26	For though for the present time I should be delivered fromthe punishment of men: yet should I not escape the hand of theAlmighty, neither alive, nor dead.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	27	Wherefore now, manfully changing this life, I will shewmyself such an one as mine age requireth,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	28	And leave a notable example to such as be young to diewillingly and courageously for the honourable and holy laws. Andwhen he had said these words, immediately he went to thetorment:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	29	They that led him changing the good will they bare him alittle before into hatred, because the foresaid speechesproceeded, as they thought, from a desperate mind.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	30	But when he was ready to die with stripes, he groaned, andsaid, It is manifest unto the Lord, that hath the holyknowledge, that whereas I might have been delivered from death,I now endure sore pains in body by being beaten: but in soul amwell content to suffer these things, because I fear him.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	6	31	And thus this man died, leaving his death for an example of anoble courage, and a memorial of virtue, not only unto youngmen, but unto all his nation.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	1	It came to pass also, that seven brethren with their motherwere taken, and compelled by the king against the law to tasteswine's flesh, and were tormented with scourges and whips.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	2	But one of them that spake first said thus, What wouldestthou ask or learn of us? we are ready to die, rather than totransgress the laws of our fathers.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	3	Then the king, being in a rage, commanded pans and caldronsto be made hot:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	4	Which forthwith being heated, he commanded to cut out thetongue of him that spake first, and to cut off the utmost partsof his body, the rest of his brethren and his mother looking on.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	5	Now when he was thus maimed in all his members, he commandedhim being yet alive to be brought to the fire, and to be friedin the pan: and as the vapour of the pan was for a good spacedispersed, they exhorted one another with the mother to diemanfully, saying thus,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	6	The Lord God looketh upon us, and in truth hath comfort inus, as Moses in his song, which witnessed to their faces,declared, saying, And he shall be comforted in his servants.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	7	So when the first was dead after this number, they broughtthe second to make him a mocking stock: and when they had pulledoff the skin of his head with the hair, they asked him, Wiltthou eat, before thou be punished throughout every member of thybody?
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	8	But he answered in his own language, and said, No. Whereforehe also received the next torment in order, as the former did.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	9	And when he was at the last gasp, he said, Thou like a furytakest us out of this present life, but the King of the worldshall raise us up, who have died for his laws, unto everlastinglife.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	10	After him was the third made a mocking stock: and when he wasrequired, he put out his tongue, and that right soon, holdingforth his hands manfully.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	11	And said courageously, These I had from heaven; and for hislaws I despise them; and from him I hope to receive them again.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	12	Insomuch that the king, and they that were with him,marvelled at the young man's courage, for that he nothingregarded the pains.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	13	Now when this man was dead also, they tormented and mangledthe fourth in like manner.

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	17	But abide a while, and behold his great power, how he willtorment thee and thy seed.

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	19	But think not thou, that takest in hand to strive againstGod, that thou shalt escape unpunished.

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	21	Yea, she exhorted every one of them in her own language,filled with courageous spirits; and stirring up her womanishthoughts with a manly stomach, she said unto them,

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	23	But doubtless the Creator of the world, who formed thegeneration of man, and found out the beginning of all things,will also of his own mercy give you breath and life again, as yenow regard not your own selves for his laws' sake.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	7	24	Now Antiochus, thinking himself despised, and suspecting itto be a reproachful speech, whilst the youngest was yet alive,did not only exhort him by words, but also assured him withoaths, that he would make him both a rich and a happy man, if hewould turn from the laws of his fathers; and that also he wouldtake him for his friend, and trust him with affairs.

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	21	But when it was told Maccabeus what was done, he called thegovernors of the people together, and accused those men, thatthey had sold their brethren for money, and set their enemiesfree to fight against them.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	22	So he slew those that were found traitors, and immediatelytook the two castles.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	23	And having good success with his weapons in all things hetook in hand, he slew in the two holds more than twentythousand.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	24	Now Timotheus, whom the Jews had overcome before, when he hadgathered a great multitude of foreign forces, and horses out ofAsia not a few, came as though he would take Jewry by force ofarms.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	25	But when he drew near, they that were with Maccabeus turnedthemselves to pray unto God, and sprinkled earth upon theirheads, and girded their loins with sackcloth,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	26	And fell down at the foot of the altar, and besought him tobe merciful to them, and to be an enemy to their enemies, and anadversary to their adversaries, as the law declareth.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	27	So after the prayer they took their weapons, and went onfurther from the city: and when they drew near to their enemies,they kept by themselves.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	28	Now the sun being newly risen, they joined both together; theone part having together with their virtue their refuge alsounto the Lord for a pledge of their success and victory: theother side making their rage leader of their battle
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	29	But when the battle waxed strong, there appeared unto theenemies from heaven five comely men upon horses, with bridles ofgold, and two of them led the Jews,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	30	And took Maccabeus betwixt them, and covered him on everyside weapons, and kept him safe, but shot arrows and lightningsagainst the enemies: so that being confounded with blindness,and full of trouble, they were killed.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	31	And there were slain of footmen twenty thousand and fivehundred, and six hundred horsemen.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	32	As for Timotheus himself, he fled into a very strong hold,called Gawra, where Chereas was governor.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	33	But they that were with Maccabeus laid siege against thefortress courageously four days.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	34	And they that were within, trusting to the strength of theplace, blasphemed exceedingly, and uttered wicked words.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	35	Nevertheless upon the fifth day early twenty young men ofMaccabeus' company, inflamed with anger because of theblasphemies, assaulted the wall manly, and with a fierce couragekilled all that they met withal.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	36	Others likewise ascending after them, whiles they were busiedwith them that were within, burnt the towers, and kindling firesburnt the blasphemers alive; and others broke open the gates,and, having received in the rest of the army, took the city,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	37	And killed Timotheus, that was hid in a certain pit, andChereas his brother, with Apollophanes.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	10	38	When this was done, they praised the Lord with psalms andthanksgiving, who had done so great things for Israel, and giventhem the victory.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	1	Not long after the, Lysias the king's protector and cousin,who also managed the affairs, took sore displeasure for thethings that were done.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	2	And when he had gathered about fourscore thousand with allthe horsemen, he came against the Jews, thinking to make thecity an habitation of the Gentiles,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	3	And to make a gain of the temple, as of the other chapels ofthe heathen, and to set the high priesthood to sale every year:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	4	Not at all considering the power of God but puffed up withhis ten thousands of footmen, and his thousands of horsemen, andhis fourscore elephants.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	5	So he came to Judea, and drew near to Bethsura, which was astrong town, but distant from Jerusalem about five furlongs, andhe laid sore siege unto it.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	6	Now when they that were with Maccabeus heard that he besiegedthe holds, they and all the people with lamentation and tearsbesought the Lord that he would send a good angel to deliverIsrael.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	7	Then Maccabeus himself first of all took weapons, exhortingthe other that they would jeopard themselves together with himto help their brethren: so they went forth together with awilling mind.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	8	And as they were at Jerusalem, there appeared before them onhorseback one in white clothing, shaking his armour of gold.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	9	Then they praised the merciful God all together, and tookheart, insomuch that they were ready not only to fight with men,but with most cruel beasts, and to pierce through walls of iron.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	10	Thus they marched forward in their armour, having an helperfrom heaven: for the Lord was merciful unto them
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	11	And giving a charge upon their enemies like lions, they sleweleven thousand footmen, and sixteen hundred horsemen, and putall the other to flight.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	12	Many of them also being wounded escaped naked; and Lysiashimself fled away shamefully, and so escaped.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	13	Who, as he was a man of understanding, casting with himselfwhat loss he had had, and considering that the Hebrews could notbe overcome, because the Almighty God helped them, he sent untothem,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	14	And persuaded them to agree to all reasonable conditions, andpromised that he would persuade the king that he must needs be afriend unto them.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	15	Then Maccabeus consented to all that Lysias desired, beingcareful of the common good; and whatsoever Maccabeus wrote untoLysias concerning the Jews, the king granted it.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	16	For there were letters written unto the Jews from Lysias tothis effect: Lysias unto the people of the Jews sendethgreeting:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	17	John and Absolom, who were sent from you, delivered me thepetition subscribed, and made request for the performance of thecontents thereof.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	18	Therefore what things soever were meet to be reported to theking, I have declared them, and he hath granted as much as mightbe.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	19	And if then ye will keep yourselves loyal to the state,hereafter also will I endeavour to be a means of your good.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	20	But of the particulars I have given order both to these andthe other that came from me, to commune with you.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	21	Fare ye well. The hundred and eight and fortieth year, thefour and twentieth day of the month Dioscorinthius.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	22	Now the king's letter contained these words: King Antiochusunto his brother Lysias sendeth greeting:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	23	Since our father is translated unto the gods, our will is,that they that are in our realm live quietly, that every one mayattend upon his own affairs.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	24	We understand also that the Jews would not consent to ourfather, for to be brought unto the custom of the Gentiles, buthad rather keep their own manner of living: for the which causethey require of us, that we should suffer them to live aftertheir own laws.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	25	Wherefore our mind is, that this nation shall be in rest, andwe have determined to restore them their temple, that they maylive according to the customs of their forefathers.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	26	Thou shalt do well therefore to send unto them, and grantthem peace, that when they are certified of our mind, they maybe of good comfort, and ever go cheerfully about their ownaffairs.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	27	And the letter of the king unto the nation of the Jews wasafter this manner: King Antiochus sendeth greeting unto thecouncil, and the rest of the Jews:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	28	If ye fare well, we have our desire; we are also in goodhealth.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	29	Menelaus declared unto us, that your desire was to returnhome, and to follow your own business:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	30	Wherefore they that will depart shall have safe conduct tillthe thirtieth day of Xanthicus with security.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	31	And the Jews shall use their own kind of meats and laws, asbefore; and none of them any manner of ways shall be molestedfor things ignorantly done.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	32	I have sent also Menelaus, that he may comfort you.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	33	Fare ye well. In the hundred forty and eighth year, and thefifteenth day of the month Xanthicus.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	34	The Romans also sent unto them a letter containing thesewords: Quintus Memmius and Titus Manlius, ambassadors of theRomans, send greeting unto the people of the Jews.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	35	Whatsoever Lysias the king's cousin hath granted, therewithwe also are well pleased.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	36	But touching such things as he judged to be referred to theking, after ye have advised thereof, send one forthwith, that wemay declare as it is convenient for you: for we are now going toAntioch.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	37	Therefore send some with speed, that we may know what is yourmind.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	11	38	Farewell. This hundred and eight and fortieth year, thefifteenth day of the month Xanthicus.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	1	When these covenants were made, Lysias went unto the king,and the Jews were about their husbandry.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	2	But of the governours of several places, Timotheus, andApollonius the son of Genneus, also Hieronymus, and Demophon,and beside them Nicanor the governor of Cyprus, would not sufferthem to be quiet and live in peace.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	3	The men of Joppa also did such an ungodly deed: they prayedthe Jews that dwelt among them to go with their wives andchildren into the boats which they had prepared, as though theyhad meant them no hurt.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	4	Who accepted of it according to the common decree of thecity, as being desirous to live in peace, and suspectingnothing: but when they were gone forth into the deep, theydrowned no less than two hundred of them.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	5	When Judas heard of this cruelty done unto his countrymen, hecommanded those that were with him to make them ready.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	6	And calling upon God the righteous Judge, he came againstthose murderers of his brethren, and burnt the haven by night,and set the boats on fire, and those that fled thither he slew.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	7	And when the town was shut up, he went backward, as if hewould return to root out all them of the city of Joppa.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	8	But when he heard that the Jamnites were minded to do in likemanner unto the Jews that dwelt among them,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	9	He came upon the Jamnites also by night, and set fire on thehaven and the navy, so that the light of the fire was seen atJerusalem two hundred and forty furlongs off.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	10	Now when they were gone from thence nine furlongs in theirjourney toward Timotheus, no fewer than five thousand men onfoot and five hundred horsemen of the Arabians set upon him.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	11	Whereupon there was a very sore battle; but Judas' side bythe help of God got the victory; so that the Nomades of Arabia,being overcome, besought Judas for peace, promising both to givehim cattle, and to pleasure him otherwise.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	12	Then Judas, thinking indeed that they would be profitable inmany things, granted them peace: whereupon they shook hands, andso they departed to their tents.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	13	He went also about to make a bridge to a certain strong city,which was fenced about with walls, and inhabited by people ofdivers countries; and the name of it was Caspis.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	14	But they that were within it put such trust in the strengthof the walls and provision of victuals, that they behavedthemselves rudely toward them that were with Judas, railing andblaspheming, and uttering such words as were not to be spoken.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	15	Wherefore Judas with his company, calling upon the great Lordof the world, who without rams or engines of war did cast downJericho in the time of Joshua, gave a fierce assault against thewalls,
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	16	And took the city by the will of God, and made unspeakableslaughters, insomuch that a lake two furlongs broad nearadjoining thereunto, being filled full, was seen running withblood.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	17	Then departed they from thence seven hundred and fiftyfurlongs, and came to Characa unto the Jews that are calledTubieni.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	18	But as for Timotheus, they found him not in the places: forbefore he had dispatched any thing, he departed from thence,having left a very strong garrison in a certain hold.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	19	Howbeit Dositheus and Sosipater, who were of Maccabeus'captains, went forth, and slew those that Timotheus had left inthe fortress, above ten thousand men.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	20	And Maccabeus ranged his army by bands, and set them over thebands, and went against Timotheus, who had about him an hundredand twenty thousand men of foot, and two thousand and fivehundred horsemen.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	21	Now when Timotheus had knowledge of Judas' coming, he sentthe women and children and the other baggage unto a fortresscalled Carnion: for the town was hard to besiege, and uneasy tocome unto, by reason of the straitness of all the places.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	22	But when Judas his first band came in sight, the enemies,being smitten with fear and terror through the appearing of himwho seeth all things, fled amain, one running into this way,another that way, so as that they were often hurt of their ownmen, and wounded with the points of their own swords.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	23	Judas also was very earnest in pursuing them, killing thosewicked wretches, of whom he slew about thirty thousand men.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	24	Moreover Timotheus himself fell into the hands of Dositheusand Sosipater, whom he besought with much craft to let him gowith his life, because he had many of the Jews' parents, and thebrethren of some of them, who, if they put him to death, shouldnot be regarded.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	25	So when he had assured them with many words that he wouldrestore them without hurt, according to the agreement, they lethim go for the saving of their brethren.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	26	Then Maccabeus marched forth to Carnion, and to the temple ofAtargatis, and there he slew five and twenty thousand persons.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	27	And after he had put to flight and destroyed them, Judasremoved the host toward Ephron, a strong city, wherein Lysiasabode, and a great multitude of divers nations, and the strongyoung men kept the walls, and defended them mightily: whereinalso was great provision of engines and darts.

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	32	And after the feast, called Pentecost, they went forthagainst Gorgias the governor of Idumea,

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	36	Now when they that were with Gorgias had fought long, andwere weary, Judas called upon the Lord, that he would shewhimself to be their helper and leader of the battle.

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	39	And upon the day following, as the use had been, Judas andhis company came to take up the bodies of them that were slain,and to bury them with their kinsmen in their fathers' graves.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	40	Now under the coats of every one that was slain they foundthings consecrated to the idols of the Jamnites, which isforbidden the Jews by the law. Then every man saw that this wasthe cause wherefore they were slain.

Besides, thatnoble Judas exhorted the people to keep themselves from sin,forsomuch as they saw before their eyes the things that came topass for the sins of those that were slain.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	43	And when he had made a gathering throughout the company tothe sum of two thousand drachms of silver, he sent it toJerusalem to offer a sin offering, doing therein very well andhonestly, in that he was mindful of the resurrection:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	44	For if he had not hoped that they that were slain should haverisen again, it had been superfluous and vain to pray for thedead.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	12	45	And also in that he perceived that there was great favourlaid up for those that died godly, it was an holy and goodthought. Whereupon he made a reconciliation for the dead, thatthey might be delivered from sin.

The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	14	6	Those of the Jews that he called Assideans, whose captain isJudas Maccabeus, nourish war and are seditious, and will not letthe rest be in peace.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	14	7	Therefore I, being deprived of mine ancestors' honour, I meanthe high priesthood, am now come hither:
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	14	8	First, verily for the unfeigned care I have of thingspertaining to the king; and secondly, even for that I intend thegood of mine own countrymen: for all our nation is in no smallmisery through the unadvised dealing of them aforersaid.
The Second Book of the Maccabees	2Mac	14	9	Wherefore, O king, seeing knowest all these things, becareful for the country, and our nation, which is pressed onevery side, according to the clemency that thou readily shewestunto all.
