The Book of Judith	Jdt	14	17	After he went into the tent where Judith lodged: and when hefound her not, he leaped out to the people, and cried,
The Book of Judith	Jdt	14	18	These slaves have dealt treacherously; one woman of theHebrews hath brought shame upon the house of kingNabuchodonosor: for, behold, Holofernes lieth upon the groundwithout a head.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	14	19	When the captains of the Assyrians' army heard these words,they rent their coats and their minds were wonderfully troubled,and there was a cry and a very great noise throughout the camp.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	1	And when they that were in the tents heard, they wereastonished at the thing that was done.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	2	And fear and trembling fell upon them, so that there was noman that durst abide in the sight of his neighbour, but rushingout all together, they fled into every way of the plain, and ofthe hill country.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	3	They also that had camped in the mountains round aboutBethulia fled away. Then the children of Israel, every one thatwas a warrior among them, rushed out upon them.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	4	Then sent Ozias to Betomasthem, and to Bebai, and Chobai, andCola and to all the coasts of Israel, such as should tell thethings that were done, and that all should rush forth upon theirenemies to destroy them.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	5	Now when the children of Israel heard it, they all fell uponthem with one consent, and slew them unto Chobai: likewise alsothey that came from Jerusalem, and from all the hill country,(for men had told them what things were done in the camp oftheir enemies) and they that were in Galaad, and in Galilee,chased them with a great slaughter, until they were pastDamascus and the borders thereof.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	6	And the residue that dwelt at Bethulia, fell upon the camp ofAssur, and spoiled them, and were greatly enriched.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	7	And the children of Israel that returned from the slaughterhad that which remained; and the villages and the cities, thatwere in the mountains and in the plain, gat many spoils: for themultitude was very great.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	8	Then Joacim the high priest, and the ancients of the childrenof Israel that dwelt in Jerusalem, came to behold the goodthings that God had shewed to Israel, and to see Judith, and tosalute her.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	9	And when they came unto her, they blessed her with oneaccord, and said unto her, Thou art the exaltation of Jerusalem,thou art the great glory of Israel, thou art the great rejoicingof our nation:
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	10	Thou hast done all these things by thine hand: thou hast donemuch good to Israel, and God is pleased therewith: blessed bethou of the Almighty Lord for evermore. And all the people said,So be it.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	11	And the people spoiled the camp the space of thirty days: andthey gave unto Judith Holofernes his tent, and all his plate,and beds, and vessels, and all his stuff: and she took it andlaid it on her mule; and made ready her carts, and laid themthereon.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	12	Then all the women of Israel ran together to see her, andblessed her, and made a dance among them for her: and she tookbranches in her hand, and gave also to the women that were withher.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	15	13	And they put a garland of olive upon her and her maid thatwas with her, and she went before all the people in the dance,leading all the women: and all the men of Israel followed intheir armour with garlands, and with songs in their mouths.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	1	Then Judith began to sing this thanksgiving in all Israel,and all the people sang after her this song of praise.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	2	And Judith said, Begin unto my God with timbrels, sing untomy Lord with cymbals: tune unto him a new psalm: exalt him, andcall upon his name.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	3	For God breaketh the battles: for among the camps in themidst of the people he hath delivered me out of the hands ofthem that persecuted me.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	4	Assur came out of the mountains from the north, he came withten thousands of his army, the multitude whereof stopped thetorrents, and their horsemen have covered the hills.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	5	He bragged that he would burn up my borders, and kill myyoung men with the sword, and dash the sucking children againstthe ground, and make mine infants as a prey, and my virgins as aspoil.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	6	But the Almighty Lord hath disappointed them by the hand of awoman.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	7	For the mighty one did not fall by the young men, neither didthe sons of the Titans smite him, nor high giants set upon him:but Judith the daughter of Merari weakened him with the beautyof her countenance.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	8	For she put off the garment of her widowhood for theexaltation of those that were oppressed in Israel, and anointedher face with ointment, and bound her hair in a tire, and took alinen garment to deceive him.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	9	Her sandals ravished his eyes, her beauty took his mindprisoner, and the fauchion passed through his neck.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	10	The Persians quaked at her boldness, and the Medes weredaunted at her hardiness.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	11	Then my afflicted shouted for joy, and my weak ones criedaloud; but they were astonished: these lifted up their voices,but they were overthrown.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	12	The sons of the damsels have pierced them through, andwounded them as fugatives' children: they perished by the battleof the Lord.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	13	I will sing unto the Lord a new song: O Lord, thou art greatand glorious, wonderful in strength, and invincible.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	14	Let all creatures serve thee: for thou spakest, and they weremade, thou didst send forth thy spirit, and it created them, andthere is none that can resist thy voice.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	15	For the mountains shall be moved from their foundations withthe waters, the rocks shall melt as wax at thy presence: yetthou art merciful to them that fear thee.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	16	For all sacrifice is too little for a sweet savour unto thee,and all the fat is not sufficient for thy burnt offering: but hethat feareth the Lord is great at all times.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	17	Woe to the nations that rise up against my kindred! the LordAlmighty will take vengeance of them in the day of judgment, inputting fire and worms in their flesh; and they shall feel them,and weep for ever.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	18	Now as soon as they entered into Jerusalem, they worshippedthe Lord; and as soon as the people were purified, they offeredtheir burnt offerings, and their free offerings, and theirgifts.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	19	Judith also dedicated all the stuff of Holofernes, which thepeople had given her, and gave the canopy, which she had takenout of his bedchamber, for a gift unto the Lord.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	20	So the people continued feasting in Jerusalem before thesanctuary for the space of three months and Judith remained withthem.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	21	After this time every one returned to his own inheritance,and Judith went to Bethulia, and remained in her own possession,and was in her time honourable in all the country.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	22	And many desired her, but none knew her all the days of herlife, after that Manasses her husband was dead, and was gatheredto his people.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	23	But she increased more and more in honour, and waxed old inher husband's house, being an hundred and five years old, andmade her maid free; so she died in Bethulia: and they buried herin the cave of her husband Manasses.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	24	And the house of Israel lamented her seven days: and beforeshe died, she did distribute her goods to all them that werenearest of kindred to Manasses her husband, and to them thatwere the nearest of her kindred.
The Book of Judith	Jdt	16	25	And there was none that made the children of Israel any moreafraid in the days of Judith, nor a long time after her death.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	1	Love righteousness, ye that be judges of the earth: think ofthe Lord with a good (heart,) and in simplicity of heart seekhim.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	2	For he will be found of them that tempt him not; and shewethhimself unto such as do not distrust him.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	3	For froward thoughts separate from God: and his power, whenit is tried, reproveth the unwise.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	4	For into a malicious soul wisdom shall not enter; nor dwellin the body that is subject unto sin.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	5	For the holy spirit of discipline will flee deceit, andremove from thoughts that are without understanding, and willnot abide when unrighteousness cometh in.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	6	For wisdom is a loving spirit; and will not acquit ablasphemer of his words: for God is witness of his reins, and atrue beholder of his heart, and a hearer of his tongue.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	7	For the Spirit of the Lord filleth the world: and that whichcontaineth all things hath knowledge of the voice.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	8	Therefore he that speaketh unrighteous things cannot be hid:neither shall vengeance, when it punisheth, pass by him.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	9	For inquisition shall be made into the counsels of theungodly: and the sound of his words shall come unto the Lord forthe manifestation of his wicked deeds.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	10	For the ear of jealousy heareth all things: and the noise ofmurmurings is not hid.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	11	Therefore beware of murmuring, which is unprofitable; andrefrain your tongue from backbiting: for there is no word sosecret, that shall go for nought: and the mouth that beliethslayeth the soul.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	12	Seek not death in the error of your life: and pull not uponyourselves destruction with the works of your hands.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	13	For God made not death: neither hath he pleasure in thedestruction of the living.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	14	For he created all things, that they might have their being:and the generations of the world were healthful; and there is nopoison of destruction in them, nor the kingdom of death upon theearth:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	15	(For righteousness is immortal:)
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	1	16	But ungodly men with their works and words called it to them:for when they thought to have it their friend, they consumed tonought, and made a covenant with it, because they are worthy totake part with it.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	1	For the ungodly said, reasoning with themselves, but notaright, Our life is short and tedious, and in the death of a manthere is no remedy: neither was there any man known to havereturned from the grave.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	2	For we are born at all adventure: and we shall be hereafteras though we had never been: for the breath in our nostrils isas smoke, and a little spark in the moving of our heart:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	3	Which being extinguished, our body shall be turned intoashes, and our spirit shall vanish as the soft air,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	4	And our name shall be forgotten in time, and no man shallhave our works in remembrance, and our life shall pass away asthe trace of a cloud, and shall be dispersed as a mist, that isdriven away with the beams of the sun, and overcome with theheat thereof.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	5	For our time is a very shadow that passeth away; and afterour end there is no returning: for it is fast sealed, so that noman cometh again.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	6	Come on therefore, let us enjoy the good things that arepresent: and let us speedily use the creatures like as in youth.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	7	Let us fill ourselves with costly wine and ointments: and letno flower of the spring pass by us:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	8	Let us crown ourselves with rosebuds, before they bewithered:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	9	Let none of us go without his part of our voluptuousness: letus leave tokens of our joyfulness in every place: for this isour portion, and our lot is this.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	10	Let us oppress the poor righteous man, let us not spare thewidow, nor reverence the ancient gray hairs of the aged.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	11	Let our strength be the law of justice: for that which isfeeble is found to be nothing worth.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	12	Therefore let us lie in wait for the righteous; because he isnot for our turn, and he is clean contrary to our doings: heupbraideth us with our offending the law, and objecteth to ourinfamy the transgressings of our education.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	13	He professeth to have the knowledge of God: and he callethhimself the child of the Lord.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	14	He was made to reprove our thoughts.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	15	He is grievous unto us even to behold: for his life is notlike other men's, his ways are of another fashion.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	16	We are esteemed of him as counterfeits: he abstaineth fromour ways as from filthiness: he pronounceth the end of the justto be blessed, and maketh his boast that God is his father.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	17	Let us see if his words be true: and let us prove what shallhappen in the end of him.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	18	For if the just man be the son of God, he will help him, anddeliver him from the hand of his enemies.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	19	Let us examine him with despitefulness and torture, that wemay know his meekness, and prove his patience.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	20	Let us condemn him with a shameful death: for by his ownsaying he shall be respected.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	21	Such things they did imagine, and were deceived: for theirown wickedness hath blinded them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	22	As for the mysteries of God, they kn ew them not: neitherhoped they for the wages of righteousness, nor discerned areward for blameless souls.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	23	For God created man to be immortal, and made him to be animage of his own eternity.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	2	24	Nevertheless through envy of the devil came death into theworld: and they that do hold of his side do find it.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	1	But the souls of the righteous are in the hand of God, andthere shall no torment touch them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	2	In the sight of the unwise they seemed to die: and theirdeparture is taken for misery,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	3	And their going from us to be utter destruction: but they arein peace.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	4	For though they be punished in the sight of men, yet is theirhope full of immortality.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	5	And having been a little chastised, they shall be greatlyrewarded: for God proved them, and found them worthy forhimself.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	6	As gold in the furnace hath he tried them, and received themas a burnt offering.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	7	And in the time of their visitation they shall shine, and runto and fro like sparks among the stubble.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	8	They shall judge the nations, and have dominion over thepeople, and their Lord shall reign for ever.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	9	They that put their trust in him shall understand the truth:and such as be faithful in love shall abide with him: for graceand mercy is to his saints, and he hath care for his elect.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	10	But the ungodly shall be punished according to their ownimaginations, which have neglected the righteous, and forsakenthe Lord.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	11	For whoso despiseth wisdom and nurture, he is miserable, andtheir hope is vain, their labours unfruitful, and their worksunprofitable:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	12	Their wives are foolish, and their children wicked:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	13	Their offspring is cursed. Wherefore blessed is the barrenthat is undefiled, which hath not known the sinful bed: sheshall have fruit in the visitation of souls.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	14	And blessed is the eunuch, which with his hands hath wroughtno iniquity, nor imagined wicked things against God: for untohim shall be given the special gift of faith, and an inheritancein the temple of the Lord more acceptable to his mind.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	15	For glorious is the fruit of good labours: and the root ofwisdom shall never fall away.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	16	As for the children of adulterers, they shall not come totheir perfection, and the seed of an unrighteous bed shall berooted out.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	17	For though they live long, yet shall they be nothingregarded: and their last age shall be without honour.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	18	Or, if they die quickly, they have no hope, neither comfortin the day of trial.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	3	19	For horrible is the end of the unrighteous generation.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	1	Better it is to have no children, and to have virtue: for thememorial thereof is immortal: because it is known with God, andwith men.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	2	When it is present, men take example at it; and when it isgone, they desire it: it weareth a crown, and triumpheth forever, having gotten the victory, striving for undefiled rewards.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	3	But the multiplying brood of the ungodly shall not thrive,nor take deep rooting from bastard slips, nor lay any fastfoundation.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	4	For though they flourish in branches for a time; yet standingnot last, they shall be shaken with the wind, and through theforce of winds they shall be rooted out.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	5	The imperfect branches shall be broken off, their fruitunprofitable, not ripe to eat, yea, meet for nothing.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	6	For children begotten of unlawful beds are witnesses ofwickedness against their parents in their trial.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	7	But though the righteous be prevented with death, yet shallhe be in rest.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	8	For honourable age is not that which standeth in length oftime, nor that is measured by number of years.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	9	But wisdom is the gray hair unto men, and an unspotted lifeis old age.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	10	He pleased God, and was beloved of him: so that living amongsinners he was translated.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	11	Yea speedily was he taken away, lest that wickedness shouldalter his understanding, or deceit beguile his soul.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	12	For the bewitching of naughtiness doth obscure things thatare honest; and the wandering of concupiscence doth underminethe simple mind.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	13	He, being made perfect in a short time, fulfilled a longtime:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	14	For his soul pleased the Lord: therefore hasted he to takehim away from among the wicked.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	15	This the people saw, and understood it not, neither laid theyup this in their minds, That his grace and mercy is with hissaints, and that he hath respect unto his chosen.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	16	Thus the righteous that is dead shall condemn the ungodlywhich are living; and youth that is soon perfected the manyyears and old age of the unrighteous.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	17	For they shall see the end of the wise, and shall notunderstand what God in his counsel hath decreed of him, and towhat end the Lord hath set him in safety.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	18	They shall see him, and despise him; but God shall laugh themto scorn: and they shall hereafter be a vile carcase, and areproach among the dead for evermore.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	19	For he shall rend them, and cast them down headlong, thatthey shall be speechless; and he shall shake them from thefoundation; and they shall be utterly laid waste, and be insorrow; and their memorial shall perish.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	4	20	And when they cast up the accounts of their sins, they shallcome with fear: and their own iniquities shall convince them totheir face.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	1	Then shall the righteous man stand in great boldness beforethe face of such as have afflicted him, and made no account ofhis labours.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	2	When they see it, they shall be troubled with terrible fear,and shall be amazed at the strangeness of his salvation, so farbeyond all that they looked for.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	3	And they repenting and groaning for anguish of spirit shallsay within themselves, This was he, whom we had sometimes inderision, and a proverb of reproach:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	4	We fools accounted his life madness, and his end to bewithout honour:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	5	How is he numbered among the children of God, and his lot isamong the saints!
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	6	Therefore have we erred from the way of truth, and the lightof righteousness hath not shined unto us, and the sun ofrighteousness rose not upon us.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	7	We wearied ourselves in the way of wickedness anddestruction: yea, we have gone through deserts, where there layno way: but as for the way of the Lord, we have not known it.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	8	What hath pride profited us? or what good hath riches withour vaunting brought us?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	9	All those things are passed away like a shadow, and as a postthat hasted by;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	10	And as a ship that passeth over the waves of the water, whichwhen it is gone by, the trace thereof cannot be found, neitherthe pathway of the keel in the waves;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	11	Or as when a bird hath flown through the air, there is notoken of her way to be found, but the light air being beatenwith the stroke of her wings and parted with the violent noiseand motion of them, is passed through, and therein afterwards nosign where she went is to be found;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	12	Or like as when an arrow is shot at a mark, it parteth theair, which immediately cometh together again, so that a mancannot know where it went through:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	13	Even so we in like manner, as soon as we were born, began todraw to our end, and had no sign of virtue to shew; but wereconsumed in our own wickedness.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	14	For the hope of the Godly is like dust that is blown awaywith the wind; like a thin froth that is driven away with thestorm; like as the smoke which is dispersed here and there witha tempest, and passeth away as the remembrance of a guest thattarrieth but a day.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	15	But the righteous live for evermore; their reward also iswith the Lord, and the care of them is with the most High.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	16	Therefore shall they receive a glorious kingdom, and abeautiful crown from the Lord's hand: for with his right handshall he cover them, and with his arm shall he protect them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	17	He shall take to him his jealousy for complete armour, andmake the creature his weapon for the revenge of his enemies.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	18	He shall put on righteousness as a breastplate, and truejudgment instead of an helmet.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	19	He shall take holiness for an invincible shield.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	20	His severe wrath shall he sharpen for a sword, and the worldshall fight with him against the unwise.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	21	Then shall the right aiming thunderbolts go abroad; and fromthe clouds, as from a well drawn bow, shall they fly to themark.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	22	And hailstones full of wrath shall be cast as out of a stonebow, and the water of the sea shall rage against them, and thefloods shall cruelly drown them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	5	23	Yea, a mighty wind shall stand up against them, and like astorm shall blow them away: thus iniquity shall lay waste thewhole earth, and ill dealing shall overthrow the thrones of themighty.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	1	Hear therefore, O ye kings, and understand; learn, ye that bejudges of the ends of the earth.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	2	Give ear, ye that rule the people, and glory in the multitudeof nations.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	3	For power is given you of the Lord, and sovereignty from theHighest, who shall try your works, and search out your counsels.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	4	Because, being ministers of his kingdom, ye have not judgedaright, nor kept the law, nor walked after the counsel of God;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	5	Horribly and speedily shall he come upon you: for a sharpjudgment shall be to them that be in high places.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	6	For mercy will soon pardon the meanest: but mighty men shallbe mightily tormented.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	7	For he which is Lord over all shall fear no man's person,neither shall he stand in awe of any man's greatness: for hehath made the small and great, and careth for all alike.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	8	But a sore trial shall come upon the mighty.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	9	Unto you therefore, O kings, do I speak, that ye may learnwisdom, and not fall away.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	10	For they that keep holiness holily shall be judged holy: andthey that have learned such things shall find what to answer.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	11	Wherefore set your affection upon my words; desire them, andye shall be instructed.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	12	Wisdom is glorious, and never fadeth away: yea, she is easilyseen of them that love her, and found of such as seek her.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	13	She preventeth them that desire her, in making herself firstknown unto them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	14	Whoso seeketh her early shall have no great travail: for heshall find her sitting at his doors.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	15	To think therefore upon her is perfection of wisdom: andwhoso watcheth for her shall quickly be without care.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	16	For she goeth about seeking such as are worthy of her,sheweth herself favourably unto them in the ways, and meeteththem in every thought.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	17	For the very true beginning of her is the desire ofdiscipline; and the care of discipline is love;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	18	And love is the keeping of her laws; and the giving heed untoher laws is the assurance of incorruption;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	19	And incorruption maketh us near unto God:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	20	Therefore the desire of wisdom bringeth to a kingdom.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	21	If your delight be then in thrones and sceptres, O ye kingsof the people, honour wisdom, that ye may reign for evermore.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	22	As for wisdom, what she is, and how she came up, I will tellyou, and will not hide mysteries from you: but will seek her outfrom the beginning of her nativity, and bring the knowledge ofher into light, and will not pass over the truth.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	23	Neither will I go with consuming envy; for such a man shallhave no fellowship with wisdom.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	24	But the multitude of the wise is the welfare of the world:and a wise king is the upholding of the people.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	6	25	Receive therefore instruction through my words, and it shalldo you good.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	1	I myself also am a mortal man, like to all, and the offspringof him that was first made of the earth,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	2	And in my mother's womb was fashioned to be flesh in the timeof ten months, being compacted in blood, of the seed of man, andthe pleasure that came with sleep.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	3	And when I was born, I drew in the common air, and fell uponthe earth, which is of like nature, and the first voice which Iuttered was crying, as all others do.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	4	I was nursed in swaddling clothes, and that with cares.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	5	For there is no king that had any other beginning of birth.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	6	For all men have one entrance into life, and the like goingout.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	7	Wherefore I prayed, and understanding was given me: I calledupon God, and the spirit of wisdom came to me.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	8	I preferred her before sceptres and thrones, and esteemedriches nothing in comparison of her.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	9	Neither compared I unto her any precious stone, because allgold in respect of her is as a little sand, and silver shall becounted as clay before her.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	10	I loved her above health and beauty, and chose to have herinstead of light: for the light that cometh from her never goethout.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	11	All good things together came to me with her, and innumerableriches in her hands.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	12	And I rejoiced in them all, because wisdom goeth before them:and I knew not that she was the mother of them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	13	I learned diligently, and do communicate her liberally: I donot hide her riches.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	14	For she is a treasure unto men that never faileth: which theythat use become the friends of God, being commended for thegifts that come from learning.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	15	God hath granted me to speak as I would, and to conceive asis meet for the things that are given me: because it is he thatleadeth unto wisdom, and directeth the wise.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	16	For in his hand are both we and our words; all wisdom also,and knowledge of workmanship.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	17	For he hath given me certain knowledge of the things thatare, namely, to know how the world was made, and the operationof the elements:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	18	The beginning, ending, and midst of the times: thealterations of the turning of the sun, and the change ofseasons:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	19	The circuits of years, and the positions of stars:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	20	The natures of living creatures, and the furies of wildbeasts: the violence of winds, and the reasonings of men: thediversities of plants and the virtues of roots:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	21	And all such things as are either secret or manifest, them Iknow.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	22	For wisdom, which is the worker of all things, taught me: forin her is an understanding spirit holy, one only, manifold,subtil, lively, clear, undefiled, plain, not subject to hurt,loving the thing that is good quick, which cannot be letted,ready to do good,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	23	Kind to man, steadfast, sure, free from care, having allpower, overseeing all things, and going through allunderstanding, pure, and most subtil, spirits.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	24	For wisdom is more moving than any motion: she passeth andgoeth through all things by reason of her pureness.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	25	For she is the breath of the power of God, and a pureinfluence flowing from the glory of the Almighty: therefore canno defiled thing fall into her.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	26	For she is the brightness of the everlasting light, theunspotted mirror of the power of God, and the image of hisgoodness.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	27	And being but one, she can do all things: and remaining inherself, she maketh all things new: and in all ages enteringinto holy souls, she maketh them friends of God, and prophets.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	28	For God loveth none but him that dwelleth with wisdom.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	29	For she is more beautiful than the sun, and above all theorder of stars: being compared with the light, she is foundbefore it.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	7	30	For after this cometh night: but vice shall not prevailagainst wisdom.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	1	Wisdom reacheth from one end to another mightily: and sweetlydoth she order all things.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	2	I loved her, and sought her out from my youth, I desired tomake her my spouse, and I was a lover of her beauty.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	3	In that she is conversant with God, she magnifieth hernobility: yea, the Lord of all things himself loved her.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	4	For she is privy to the mysteries of the knowledge of God,and a lover of his works.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	5	If riches be a possession to be desired in this life; what isricher than wisdom, that worketh all things?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	6	And if prudence work; who of all that are is a more cunningworkman than she?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	7	And if a man love righteousness her labours are virtues: forshe teacheth temperance and prudence, justice and fortitude:which are such things, as en can have nothing more profitable intheir life.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	8	If a man desire much experience, she knoweth things of old,and conjectureth aright what is to come: she knoweth thesubtilties of speeches, and can expound dark sentences: sheforeseeth signs and wonders, and the events of seasons andtimes.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	9	Therefore I purposed to take her to me to live with me,knowing that she would be a counsellor of good things, and acomfort in cares and grief.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	10	For her sake I shall have estimation among the multitude, andhonour with the elders, though I be young.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	11	I shall be found of a quick conceit in judgment, and shall beadmired in the sight of great men.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	12	When I hold my tongue, they shall bide my leisure, and when Ispeak, they shall give good ear unto me: if I talk much, theyshall lay their hands upon their mouth.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	13	Moreover by the means of her I shall obtain immortality, andleave behind me an everlasting memorial to them that come afterme.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	14	I shall set the people in order, and the nations shall besubject unto me.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	15	Horrible tyrants shall be afraid, when they do but hear ofme; I shall be found good among the multitude, and valiant inwar.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	16	After I am come into mine house, I will repose myself withher: for her conversation hath no bitterness; and to live withher hath no sorrow, but mirth and joy.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	17	Now when I considered these things in myself, and ponderedthem in my heart, how that to be allied unto wisdom isimmortality;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	18	And great pleasure it is to have her friendship; and in theworks of her hands are infinite riches; and in the exercise ofconference with her, prudence; and in talking with her, a goodreport; I went about seeking how to take her to me.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	19	For I was a witty child, and had a good spirit.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	20	Yea rather, being good, I came into a body undefiled.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	8	21	Nevertheless, when I perceived that I could not otherwiseobtain her, except God gave her me; and that was a point ofwisdom also to know whose gift she was; I prayed unto the Lord,and besought him, and with my whole heart I said,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	1	O God of my fathers, and Lord of mercy, who hast made allthings with thy word,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	2	And ordained man through thy wisdom, that he should havedominion over the creatures which thou hast made,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	3	And order the world according to equity and righteousness,and execute judgment with an upright heart:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	4	Give me wisdom, that sitteth by thy throne; and reject me notfrom among thy children:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	5	For I thy servant and son of thine handmaid am a feebleperson, and of a short time, and too young for the understandingof judgment and laws.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	6	For though a man be never so perfect among the children ofmen, yet if thy wisdom be not with him, he shall be nothingregarded.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	7	Thou hast chosen me to be a king of thy people, and a judgeof thy sons and daughters:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	8	Thou hast commanded me to build a temple upon thy holy mount,and an altar in the city wherein thou dwellest, a resemblance ofthe holy tabernacle, which thou hast prepared from thebeginning.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	9	And wisdom was with thee: which knoweth thy works, and waspresent when thou madest the world, and knew what was acceptablein thy sight, and right in thy commandments.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	10	O send her out of thy holy heavens, and from the throne ofthy glory, that being present she may labour with me, that I mayknow what is pleasing unto thee.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	11	For she knoweth and understandeth all things, and she shalllead me soberly in my doings, and preserve me in her power.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	12	So shall my works be acceptable, and then shall I judge thypeople righteously, and be worthy to sit in my father's seat.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	13	For what man is he that can know the counsel of God? or whocan think what the will of the Lord is?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	14	For the thoughts of mortal men are miserable, and our devicesare but uncertain.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	15	For the corruptible body presseth down the soul, and theearthy tabernacle weigheth down the mind that museth upon manythings.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	16	And hardly do we guess aright at things that are upon earth,and with labour do we find the things that are before us: butthe things that are in heaven who hath searched out?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	17	And thy counsel who hath known, except thou give wisdom, andsend thy Holy Spirit from above?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	9	18	For so the ways of them which lived on the earth werereformed, and men were taught the things that are pleasing untothee, and were saved through wisdom.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	1	She preserved the first formed father of the world, that wascreated alone, and brought him out of his fall,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	2	And gave him power to rule all things.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	3	But when the unrighteous went away from her in his anger, heperished also in the fury wherewith he murdered his brother.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	4	For whose cause the earth being drowned with the flood,wisdom again preserved it, and directed the course of therighteous in a piece of wood of small value.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	5	Moreover, the nations in their wicked conspiracy beingconfounded, she found out the righteous, and preserved himblameless unto God, and kept him strong against his tendercompassion toward his son.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	6	When the ungodly perished, she delivered the righteous man,who fled from the fire which fell down upon the five cities.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	7	Of whose wickedness even to this day the waste land thatsmoketh is a testimony, and plants bearing fruit that never cometo ripeness: and a standing pillar of salt is a monument of anunbelieving soul.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	8	For regarding not wisdom, they gat not only this hurt, thatthey knew not the things which were good; but also left behindthem to the world a memorial of their foolishness: so that inthe things wherein they offended they could not so much as behid.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	9	Rut wisdom delivered from pain those that attended upon her.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	10	When the righteous fled from his brother's wrath she guidedhim in right paths, shewed him the kingdom of God, and gave himknowledge of holy things, made him rich in his travels, andmultiplied the fruit of his labours.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	11	In the covetousness of such as oppressed him she stood byhim, and made him rich.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	12	She defended him from his enemies, and kept him safe fromthose that lay in wait, and in a sore conflict she gave him thevictory; that he might know that goodness is stronger than all.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	13	When the righteous was sold, she forsook him not, butdelivered him from sin: she went down with him into the pit,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	14	And left him not in bonds, till she brought him the sceptreof the kingdom, and power against those that oppressed him: asfor them that had accused him, she shewed them to be liars, andgave him perpetual glory.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	15	She delivered the righteous people and blameless seed fromthe nation that oppressed them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	16	She entered into the soul of the servant of the Lord, andwithstood dreadful kings in wonders and signs;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	17	Rendered to the righteous a reward of their labours, guidedthem in a marvellous way, and was unto them for a cover by day,and a light of stars in the night season;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	18	Brought them through the Red sea, and led them through muchwater:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	19	But she drowned their enemies, and cast them up out of thebottom of the deep.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	20	Therefore the righteous spoiled the ungodly, and praised thyholy name, O Lord, and magnified with one accord thine hand,that fought for them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	10	21	For wisdom opened the mouth of the dumb, and made the tonguesof them that cannot speak eloquent.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	1	She prospered their works in the hand of the holy prophet.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	2	They went through the wilderness that was not inhabited, andpitched tents in places where there lay no way.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	3	They stood against their enemies, and were avenged of theiradversaries.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	4	When they were thirsty, they called upon thee, and water wasgiven them out of the flinty rock, and their thirst was quenchedout of the hard stone.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	5	For by what things their enemies were punished, by the samethey in their need were benefited.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	6	For instead of of a perpetual running river troubled withfoul blood,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	7	For a manifest reproof of that commandment, whereby theinfants were slain, thou gavest unto them abundance of water bya means which they hoped not for:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	8	Declaring by that thirst then how thou hadst punished theiradversaries.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	9	For when they were tried albeit but in mercy chastised, theyknew how the ungodly were judged in wrath and tormented,thirsting in another manner than the just.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	10	For these thou didst admonish and try, as a father: but theother, as a severe king, thou didst condemn and punish.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	11	Whether they were absent or present, they were vexed alike.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	12	For a double grief came upon them, and a groaning for theremembrance of things past.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	13	For when they heard by their own punishments the other to bebenefited, they had some feeling of the Lord.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	14	For whom they respected with scorn, when he was long beforethrown out at the casting forth of the infants, him in the end,when they saw what came to pass, they admired.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	15	But for the foolish devices of their wickedness, wherewithbeing deceived they worshipped serpents void of reason, and vilebeasts, thou didst send a multitude of unreasonable beasts uponthem for vengeance;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	16	That they might know, that wherewithal a man sinneth, by thesame also shall he be punished.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	17	For thy Almighty hand, that made the world of matter withoutform, wanted not means to send among them a multitude of bearsor fierce lions,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	18	Or unknown wild beasts, full of rage, newly created,breathing out either a fiery vapour, or filthy scents ofscattered smoke, or shooting horrible sparkles out of theireyes:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	19	Whereof not only the harm might dispatch them at once, butalso the terrible sight utterly destroy them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	20	Yea, and without these might they have fallen down with oneblast, being persecuted of vengeance, and scattered abroadthrough the breath of thy power: but thou hast ordered allthings in measure and number and weight.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	21	For thou canst shew thy great strength at all times when thouwilt; and who may withstand the power of thine arm?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	22	For the whole world before thee is as a little grain of thebalance, yea, as a drop of the morning dew that falleth downupon the earth.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	23	But thou hast mercy upon all; for thou canst do all things,and winkest at the sins of men, because they should amend.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	24	For thou lovest all the things that are, and abhorrestnothing which thou hast made: for never wouldest thou have madeany thing, if thou hadst hated it.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	25	And how could any thing have endured, if it had not been thywill? or been preserved, if not called by thee?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	11	26	But thou sparest all: for they are thine, O Lord, thou loverof souls.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	1	For thine incorruptible Spirit is in all things.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	2	Therefore chastenest thou them by little and little thatoffend, and warnest them by putting them in remembrance whereinthey have offended, that leaving their wickedness they maybelieve on thee, O Lord.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	3	For it was thy will to destroy by the hands of our fathersboth those old inhabitants of thy holy land,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	4	Whom thou hatedst for doing most odious works of witchcrafts,and wicked sacrifices;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	5	And also those merciless murderers of children, and devourersof man's flesh, and the feasts of blood,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	6	With their priests out of the midst of their idolatrous crew,and the parents, that killed with their own hands soulsdestitute of help:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	7	That the land, which thou esteemedst above all other, mightreceive a worthy colony of God's children.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	8	Nevertheless even those thou sparedst as men, and didst sendwasps, forerunners of thine host, to destroy them by little andlittle.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	9	Not that thou wast unable to bring the ungodly under the handof the righteous in battle, or to destroy them at once withcruel beasts, or with one rough word:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	10	But executing thy judgments upon them by little and little,thou gavest them place of repentance, not being ignorant thatthey were a naughty generation, and that their malice was bredin them, and that their cogitation would never be changed.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	11	For it was a cursed seed from the beginning; neither didstthou for fear of any man give them pardon for those thingswherein they sinned.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	12	For who shall say, What hast thou done? or who shallwithstand thy judgment? or who shall accuse thee for the nationsthat perish, whom thou made? or who shall come to stand againstthee, to be revenged for the unrighteous men?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	13	For neither is there any God but thou that careth for all, towhom thou mightest shew that thy judgment is not unright.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	14	Neither shall king or tyrant be able to set his face againstthee for any whom thou hast punished.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	15	Forsomuch then as thou art righteous thyself, thou orderestall things righteously: thinking it not agreeable with thy powerto condemn him that hath not deserved to be punished.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	16	For thy power is the beginning of righteousness, and becausethou art the Lord of all, it maketh thee to be gracious untoall.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	17	For when men will not believe that thou art of a full power,thou shewest thy strength, and among them that know it thoumakest their boldness manifest.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	18	But thou, mastering thy power, judgest with equity, andorderest us with great favour: for thou mayest use power whenthou wilt.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	19	But by such works hast thou taught thy people that the justman should be merciful, and hast made thy children to be of agood hope that thou givest repentance for sins.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	20	For if thou didst punish the enemies of thy children, and thecondemned to death, with such deliberation, giving them time andplace, whereby they might be delivered from their malice:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	21	With how great circumspection didst thou judge thine ownsons, unto whose fathers thou hast sworn, and made covenants ofgood promises?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	22	Therefore, whereas thou dost chasten us, thou scourgest ourenemies a thousand times more, to the intent that, when wejudge, we should carefully think of thy goodness, and when weourselves are judged, we should look for mercy.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	23	Wherefore, whereas men have lived dissolutely andunrighteously, thou hast tormented them with their ownabominations.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	24	For they went astray very far in the ways of error, and heldthem for gods, which even among the beasts of their enemies weredespised, being deceived, as children of no understanding.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	25	Therefore unto them, as to children without the use ofreason, thou didst send a judgment to mock them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	26	But they that would not be reformed by that correction,wherein he dallied with them, shall feel a judgment worthy ofGod.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	12	27	For, look, for what things they grudged, when they werepunished, that is, for them whom they thought to be gods; [now]being punished in them, when they saw it, they acknowledged himto be the true God, whom before they denied to know: andtherefore came extreme damnation upon them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	1	Surely vain are all men by nature, who are ignorant of God,and could not out of the good things that are seen know him thatis: neither by considering the works did they acknowledge theworkmaster;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	2	But deemed either fire, or wind, or the swift air, or thecircle of the stars, or the violent water, or the lights ofheaven, to be the gods which govern the world.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	3	With whose beauty if they being delighted took them to begods; let them know how much better the Lord of them is: for thefirst author of beauty hath created them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	4	But if they were astonished at their power and virtue, letthem understand by them, how much mightier he is that made them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	5	For by the greatness and beauty of the creaturesproportionably the maker of them is seen.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	6	But yet for this they are the less to be blamed: for theyperadventure err, seeking God, and desirous to find him.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	7	For being conversant in his works they search him diligently,and believe their sight: because the things are beautiful thatare seen.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	8	Howbeit neither are they to be pardoned.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	9	For if they were able to know so much, that they could aim atthe world; how did they not sooner find out the Lord thereof?
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	10	But miserable are they, and in dead things is their hope, whocall them gods, which are the works of men's hands, gold andsilver, to shew art in, and resemblances of beasts, or a stonegood for nothing, the work of an ancient hand.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	11	Now a carpenter that felleth timber, after he hath sawn downa tree meet for the purpose, and taken off all the barkskilfully round about, and hath wrought it handsomely, and madea vessel thereof fit for the service of man's life;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	12	And after spending the refuse of his work to dress his meat,hath filled himself;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	13	And taking the very refuse among those which served to nouse, being a crooked piece of wood, and full of knots, hathcarved it diligently, when he had nothing else to do, and formedit by the skill of his understanding, and fashioned it to theimage of a man;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	14	Or made it like some vile beast, laying it over withvermilion, and with paint colouring it red, and covering everyspot therein;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	15	And when he had made a convenient room for it, set it in awall, and made it fast with iron:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	16	For he provided for it that it might not fall, knowing thatit was unable to help itself; for it is an image, and hath needof help:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	17	Then maketh he prayer for his goods, for his wife andchildren, and is not ashamed to speak to that which hath nolife.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	18	For health he calleth upon that which is weak: for lifeprayeth to that which is dead; for aid humbly beseecheth thatwhich hath least means to help: and for a good journey he askethof that which cannot set a foot forward:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	13	19	And for gaining and getting, and for good success of hishands, asketh ability to do of him, that is most unable to doany thing.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	1	Again, one preparing himself to sail, and about to passthrough the raging waves, calleth upon a piece of wood morerotten than the vessel that carrieth him.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	2	For verily desire of gain devised that, and the workman builtit by his skill.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	3	But thy providence, O Father, governeth it: for thou hastmade a way in the sea, and a safe path in the waves;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	4	Shewing that thou canst save from all danger: yea, though aman went to sea without art.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	5	Nevertheless thou wouldest not that the works of thy wisdomshould be idle, and therefore do men commit their lives to asmall piece of wood, and passing the rough sea in a weak vesselare saved.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	6	For in the old time also, when the proud giants perished, thehope of the world governed by thy hand escaped in a weak vessel,and left to all ages a seed of generation.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	7	For blessed is the wood whereby righteousness cometh.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	8	But that which is made with hands is cursed, as well it, ashe that made it: he, because he made it; and it, because, beingcorruptible, it was called god.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	9	For the ungodly and his ungodliness are both alike hatefulunto God.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	10	For that which is made shall be punished together with himthat made it.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	11	Therefore even upon the idols of the Gentiles shall there bea visitation: because in the creature of God they are become anabomination, and stumblingblocks to the souls of men, and asnare to the feet of the unwise.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	12	For the devising of idols was the beginning of spiritualfornication, and the invention of them the corruption of life.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	13	For neither were they from the beginning, neither shall theybe for ever.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	14	For by the vain glory of men they entered into the world, andtherefore shall they come shortly to an end.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	15	For a father afflicted with untimely mourning, when he hathmade an image of his child soon taken away, now honoured him asa god, which was then a dead man, and delivered to those thatwere under him ceremonies and sacrifices.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	16	Thus in process of time an ungodly custom grown strong waskept as a law, and graven images were worshipped by thecommandments of kings.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	17	Whom men could not honour in presence, because they dwelt faroff, they took the counterfeit of his visage from far, and madean express image of a king whom they honoured, to the end thatby this their forwardness they might flatter him that wasabsent, as if he were present.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	18	Also the singular diligence of the artificer did help to setforward the ignorant to more superstition.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	19	For he, peradventure willing to please one in authority,forced all his skill to make the resemblance of the bestfashion.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	20	And so the multitude, allured by the grace of the work, tookhim now for a god, which a little before was but honoured.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	21	And this was an occasion to deceive the world: for men,serving either calamity or tyranny, did ascribe unto stones andstocks the incommunicable name.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	22	Moreover this was not enough for them, that they erred in theknowledge of God; but whereas they lived in the great war ofignorance, those so great plagues called they peace.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	23	For whilst they slew their children in sacrifices, or usedsecret ceremonies, or made revellings of strange rites;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	24	They kept neither lives nor marriages any longer undefiled:but either one slew another traiterously, or grieved him byadultery.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	25	So that there reigned in all men without exception blood,manslaughter, theft, and dissimulation, corruption,unfaithfulness, tumults, perjury,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	26	Disquieting of good men, forgetfulness of good turns,defiling of souls, changing of kind, disorder in marriages,adultery, and shameless uncleanness.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	27	For the worshipping of idols not to be named is thebeginning, the cause, and the end, of all evil.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	28	For either they are mad when they be merry, or prophesy lies,or live unjustly, or else lightly forswear themselves.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	29	For insomuch as their trust is in idols, which have no life;though they swear falsely, yet they look not to be hurt.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	30	Howbeit for both causes shall they be justly punished: bothbecause they thought not well of God, giving heed unto idols,and also unjustly swore in deceit, despising holiness.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	14	31	For it is not the power of them by whom they swear: but it isthe just vengeance of sinners, that punisheth always the offenceof the ungodly.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	1	But thou, O God, art gracious and true, longsuffering, and inmercy ordering all things,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	2	For if we sin, we are thine, knowing thy power: but we willnot sin, knowing that we are counted thine.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	3	For to know thee is perfect righteousness: yea, to know thypower is the root of immortality.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	4	For neither did the mischievous invention of men deceive us,nor an image spotted with divers colours, the painter'sfruitless labour;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	5	The sight whereof enticeth fools to lust after it, and sothey desire the form of a dead image, that hath no breath.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	6	Both they that make them, they that desire them, and theythat worship them, are lovers of evil things, and are worthy tohave such things to trust upon.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	7	For the potter, tempering soft earth, fashioneth every vesselwith much labour for our service: yea, of the same clay hemaketh both the vessels that serve for clean uses, and likewisealso all such as serve to the contrary: but what is the use ofeither sort, the potter himself is the judge.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	8	And employing his labours lewdly, he maketh a vain god of thesame clay, even he which a little before was made of earthhimself, and within a little while after returneth to the same,out when his life which was lent him shall be demanded.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	9	Notwithstanding his care is, not that he shall have muchlabour, nor that his life is short: but striveth to excelgoldsmiths and silversmiths, and endeavoureth to do like theworkers in brass, and counteth it his glory to make counterfeitthings.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	10	His heart is ashes, his hope is more vile than earth, and hislife of less value than clay:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	11	Forasmuch as he knew not his Maker, and him that inspiredinto him an active soul, and breathed in a living spirit.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	12	But they counted our life a pastime, and our time here amarket for gain: for, say they, we must be getting every way,though it be by evil means.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	13	For this man, that of earthly matter maketh brittle vesselsand graven images, knoweth himself to offend above all others.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	14	And all the enemies of thy people, that hold them insubjection, are most foolish, and are more miserable than verybabes.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	15	For they counted all the idols of the heathen to be gods:which neither have the use of eyes to see, nor noses to drawbreath, nor ears to hear, nor fingers of hands to handle; and asfor their feet, they are slow to go.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	16	For man made them, and he that borrowed his own spiritfashioned them: but no man can make a god like unto himself.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	17	For being mortal, he worketh a dead thing with wicked hands:for he himself is better than the things which he worshippeth:whereas he lived once, but they never.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	18	Yea, they worshipped those beasts also that are most hateful:for being compared together, some are worse than others.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	15	19	Neither are they beautiful, so much as to be desired inrespect of beasts: but they went without the praise of God andhis blessing.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	1	Therefore by the like were they punished worthily, and by themultitude of beasts tormented.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	2	Instead of which punishment, dealing graciously with thineown people, thou preparedst for them meat of a strange taste,even quails to stir up their appetite:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	3	To the end that they, desiring food, might for the ugly sightof the beasts sent among them lothe even that, which they mustneeds desire; but these, suffering penury for a short space,might be made partakers of a strange taste.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	4	For it was requisite, that upon them exercising tyrannyshould come penury, which they could not avoid: but to these itshould only be shewed how their enemies were tormented.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	5	For when the horrible fierceness of beasts came upon these,and they perished with the stings of crooked serpents, thy wrathendured not for ever:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	6	But they were troubled for a small season, that they might beadmonished, having a sign of salvation, to put them inremembrance of the commandment of thy law.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	7	For he that turned himself toward it was not saved by thething that he saw, but by thee, that art the Saviour of all.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	8	And in this thou madest thine enemies confess, that it isthou who deliverest from all evil:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	9	For them the bitings of grasshoppers and flies killed,neither was there found any remedy for their life: for they wereworthy to be punished by such.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	10	But thy sons not the very teeth of venomous dragons overcame:for thy mercy was ever by them, and healed them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	11	For they were pricked, that they should remember thy words;and were quickly saved, that not falling into deepforgetfulness, they might be continually mindful of thygoodness.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	12	For it was neither herb, nor mollifying plaister, thatrestored them to health: but thy word, O Lord, which healeth allthings.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	13	For thou hast power of life and death: thou leadest to thegates of hell, and bringest up again.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	14	A man indeed killeth through his malice: and the spirit, whenit is gone forth, returneth not; neither the soul received upcometh again.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	15	But it is not possible to escape thine hand.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	16	For the ungodly, that denied to know thee, were scourged bythe strength of thine arm: with strange rains, hails, andshowers, were they persecuted, that they could not avoid, andthrough fire were they consumed.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	17	For, which is most to be wondered at, the fire had more forcein the water, that quencheth all things: for the world fightethfor the righteous.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	18	For sometime the flame was mitigated, that it might not burnup the beasts that were sent against the ungodly; but themselvesmight see and perceive that they were persecuted with thejudgment of God.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	19	And at another time it burneth even in the midst of waterabove the power of fire, that it might destroy the fruits of anunjust land.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	20	Instead whereof thou feddest thine own people with angels'food, and didst send them from heaven bread prepared withouttheir labour, able to content every man's delight, and agreeingto every taste.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	21	For thy sustenance declared thy sweetness unto thy children,and serving to the appetite of the eater, tempered itself toevery man's liking.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	22	But snow and ice endured the fire, and melted not, that theymight know that fire burning in the hail, and sparkling in therain, did destroy the fruits of the enemies.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	23	But this again did even forget his own strength, that therighteous might be nourished.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	24	For the creature that serveth thee, who art the Makerincreaseth his strength against the unrighteous for theirpunishment, and abateth his strength for the benefit of such asput their trust in thee.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	25	Therefore even then was it altered into all fashions, and wasobedient to thy grace, that nourisheth all things, according tothe desire of them that had need:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	26	That thy children, O Lord, whom thou lovest, might know, thatit is not the growing of fruits that nourisheth man: but that itis thy word, which preserveth them that put their trust in thee.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	27	For that which was not destroyed of the fire, being warmedwith a little sunbeam, soon melted away:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	28	That it might be known, that we must prevent the sun to givethee thanks, and at the dayspring pray unto thee.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	16	29	For the hope of the unthankful shall melt away as thewinter's hoar frost, and shall run away as unprofitable water.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	1	For great are thy judgments, and cannot be expressed:therefore unnurtured souls have erred.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	2	For when unrighteous men thought to oppress the holy nation;they being shut up in their houses, the prisoners of darkness,and fettered with the bonds of a long night, lay [there] exiledfrom the eternal providence.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	3	For while they supposed to lie hid in their secret sins, theywere scattered under a dark veil of forgetfulness, beinghorribly astonished, and troubled with [strange] apparitions.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	4	For neither might the corner that held them keep them fromfear: but noises [as of waters] falling down sounded about them,and sad visions appeared unto them with heavy countenances.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	5	No power of the fire might give them light: neither could thebright flames of the stars endure to lighten that horriblenight.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	6	Only there appeared unto them a fire kindled of itself, verydreadful: for being much terrified, they thought the thingswhich they saw to be worse than the sight they saw not.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	7	As for the illusions of art magick, they were put down, andtheir vaunting in wisdom was reproved with disgrace.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	8	For they, that promised to drive away terrors and troublesfrom a sick soul, were sick themselves of fear, worthy to belaughed at.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	9	For though no terrible thing did fear them; yet being scaredwith beasts that passed by, and hissing of serpents,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	10	They died for fear, denying that they saw the air, whichcould of no side be avoided.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	11	For wickedness, condemned by her own witness, is verytimorous, and being pressed with conscience, always forecastethgrievous things.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	12	For fear is nothing else but a betraying of the succourswhich reason offereth.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	13	And the expectation from within, being less, counteth theignorance more than the cause which bringeth the torment.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	14	But they sleeping the same sleep that night, which was indeedintolerable, and which came upon them out of the bottoms ofinevitable hell,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	15	Were partly vexed with monstrous apparitions, and partlyfainted, their heart failing them: for a sudden fear, and notlooked for, came upon them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	16	So then whosoever there fell down was straitly kept, shut upin a prison without iron bars,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	17	For whether he were husbandman, or shepherd, or a labourer inthe field, he was overtaken, and endured that necessity, whichcould not be avoided: for they were all bound with one chain ofdarkness.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	18	Whether it were a whistling wind, or a melodious noise ofbirds among the spreading branches, or a pleasing fall of waterrunning violently,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	19	Or a terrible sound of stones cast down, or a running thatcould not be seen of skipping beasts, or a roaring voice of mostsavage wild beasts, or a rebounding echo from the hollowmountains; these things made them to swoon for fear.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	20	For the whole world shined with clear light, and none werehindered in their labour:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	17	21	Over them only was spread an heavy night, an image of thatdarkness which should afterward receive them: but yet were theyunto themselves more grievous than the darkness.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	1	Nevertheless thy saints had a very great light, whose voicethey hearing, and not seeing their shape, because they also hadnot suffered the same things, they counted them happy.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	2	But for that they did not hurt them now, of whom they hadbeen wronged before, they thanked them, and besought them pardonfor that they had been enemies.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	3	Instead whereof thou gavest them a burning pillar of fire,both to be a guide of the unknown journey, and an harmless sunto entertain them honourably.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	4	For they were worthy to be deprived of light and imprisonedin darkness, who had kept thy sons shut up, by whom theuncorrupt light of the law was to be given unto the world.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	5	And when they had determined to slay the babes of the saints,one child being cast forth, and saved, to reprove them, thoutookest away the multitude of their children, and destroyedstthem altogether in a mighty water.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	6	Of that night were our fathers certified afore, thatassuredly knowing unto what oaths they had given credence, theymight afterwards be of good cheer.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	7	So of thy people was accepted both the salvation of therighteous, and destruction of the enemies.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	8	For wherewith thou didst punish our adversaries, by the samethou didst glorify us, whom thou hadst called.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	9	For the righteous children of good men did sacrificesecretly, and with one consent made a holy law, that the saintsshould be like partakers of the same good and evil, the fathersnow singing out the songs of praise.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	10	But on the other side there sounded an ill according cry ofthe enemies, and a lamentable noise was carried abroad forchildren that were bewailed.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	11	The master and the servant were punished after one manner;and like as the king, so suffered the common person.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	12	So they all together had innumerable dead with one kind ofdeath; neither were the living sufficient to bury them: for inone moment the noblest offspring of them was destroyed.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	13	For whereas they would not believe any thing by reason of theenchantments; upon the destruction of the firstborn, theyacknowledged this people to be the sons of God.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	14	For while all things were in quiet silence, and that nightwas in the midst of her swift course,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	15	Thine Almighty word leaped down from heaven out of thy royalthrone, as a fierce man of war into the midst of a land ofdestruction,
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	16	And brought thine unfeigned commandment as a sharp sword, andstanding up filled all things with death; and it touched theheaven, but it stood upon the earth.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	17	Then suddenly visions of horrible dreams troubled them sore,and terrors came upon them unlooked for.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	18	And one thrown here, and another there, half dead, shewed thecause of his death.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	19	For the dreams that troubled them did foreshew this, lestthey should perish, and not know why they were afflicted.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	20	Yea, the tasting of death touched the righteous also, andthere was a destruction of the multitude in the wilderness: butthe wrath endured not long.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	21	For then the blameless man made haste, and stood forth todefend them; and bringing the shield of his proper ministry,even prayer, and the propitiation of incense, set himselfagainst the wrath, and so brought the calamity to an end,declaring that he was thy servant.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	22	So he overcame the destroyer, not with strength of body, norforce of arms, but with a word subdued him that punished,alleging the oaths and covenants made with the fathers.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	23	For when the dead were now fallen down by heaps one uponanother, standing between, he stayed the wrath, and parted theway to the living.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	24	For in the long garment was the whole world, and in the fourrows of the stones was the glory of the fathers graven, and thyMajesty upon the daidem of his head.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	18	25	Unto these the destroyer gave place, and was afraid of them:for it was enough that they only tasted of the wrath.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	1	As for the ungodly, wrath came upon them without mercy untothe end: for he knew before what they would do;
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	2	How that having given them leave to depart, and sent themhastily away, they would repent and pursue them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	3	For whilst they were yet mourning and making lamentation atthe graves of the dead, they added another foolish device, andpursued them as fugitives, whom they had intreated to be gone.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	4	For the destiny, whereof they were worthy, drew them untothis end, and made them forget the things that had alreadyhappened, that they might fulfil the punishment which waswanting to their torments:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	5	And that thy people might pass a wonderful way: but theymight find a strange death.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	6	For the whole creature in his proper kind was fashioned againanew, serving the peculiar commandments that were given untothem, that thy children might be kept without hurt:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	7	As namely, a cloud shadowing the camp; and where water stoodbefore, dry land appeared; and out of the Red sea a way withoutimpediment; and out of the violent stream a green field:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	8	Wherethrough all the people went that were defended with thyhand, seeing thy marvellous strange wonders.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	9	For they went at large like horses, and leaped like lambs,praising thee, O Lord, who hadst delivered them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	10	For they were yet mindful of the things that were done whilethey sojourned in the strange land, how the ground brought forthflies instead of cattle, and how the river cast up a multitudeof frogs instead of fishes.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	11	But afterwards they saw a new generation of fowls, when,being led with their appetite, they asked delicate meats.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	12	For quails came up unto them from the sea for theircontentment.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	13	And punishments came upon the sinners not without formersigns by the force of thunders: for they suffered justlyaccording to their own wickedness, insomuch as they used a morehard and hateful behaviour toward strangers.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	14	For the Sodomites did not receive those, whom they knew notwhen they came: but these brought friends into bondage, that hadwell deserved of them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	15	And not only so, but peradventure some respect shall be hadof those, because they used strangers not friendly:
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	16	But these very grievously afflicted them, whom they hadreceived with feastings, and were already made partakers of thesame laws with them.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	17	Therefore even with blindness were these stricken, as thosewere at the doors of the righteous man: when, being compassedabout with horrible great darkness, every one sought the passageof his own doors.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	18	For the elements were changed in themselves by a kind ofharmony, like as in a psaltery notes change the name of thetune, and yet are always sounds; which may well be perceived bythe sight of the things that have been done.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	19	For earthly things were turned into watery, and the things,that before swam in the water, now went upon the ground.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	20	The fire had power in the water, forgetting his own virtue:and the water forgat his own quenching nature.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	21	On the other side, the flames wasted not the flesh of thecorruptible living things, though they walked therein; neithermelted they the icy kind of heavenly meat that was of nature aptto melt.
The Wisdom of Solomon	Wis	19	22	For in all things, O Lord, thou didst magnify thy people, andglorify them, neither didst thou lightly regard them: but didstassist them in every time and place.
