The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	A Prologue made by an uncertain Author]	This Jesus was the son of Sirach, and grandchild toJesus of the same name with him: this man therefore lived in thelatter times, after the people had been led away captive, andcalled home a again, and almost after all the prophets. Now hisgrandfather Jesus, as he himself witnesseth, was a man of greatdiligence and wisdom among the Hebrews, who did not only gatherthe grave and short sentences of wise men, that had been beforehim, but himself also uttered some of his own, full of muchunderstanding and wisdom. When as therefore the first Jesusdied, leaving this book almost perfected, Sirach his sonreceiving it after him left it to his own son Jesus, who, havinggotten it into his hands, compiled it all orderly into onevolume, and called it Wisdom, intituling it both by his ownname, his father's name, and his grandfather's; alluring thehearer by the very name of Wisdom to have a greater love to thestudy of this book. It containeth therefore wise sayings, darksentences, and parables, and certain particular ancient godlystories of men that pleased God; also his prayer and song;moreover, what benefits God had vouchsafed his people, and whatplagues he had heaped upon their enemies. This Jesus did imitateSolomon, and was no less famous for wisdom and learning, bothbeing indeed a man of great learning, and so reputed also.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	[The	Prologue o	 the Wisdom of Jesus the Son of Sirach.]	Whereas many and great things have been delivered unto us by the lawand the prophets, and by others that have followed their steps,for the which things Israel ought to be commended for learningand wisdom; and whereof not only the readers must needs becomeskilful themselves, but also they that desire to learn be ableto profit them which are without, both by speaking and writing:my grandfather Jesus, when he had much given himself to thereading of the law, and the prophets, and other books of ourfathers, and had gotten therein good judgment, was drawn on alsohimself to write something pertaining to learning and wisdom; tothe intent that those which are desirous to learn, and areaddicted to these things, might profit much more in livingaccording to the law. Wherefore let me intreat you to read itwith favour and attention, and to pardon us, wherein we may seemto come short of some words, which we have laboured tointerpret. For the same things uttered in Hebrew, and translatedinto another tongue, have not the same force in them: and notonly these things, but the law itself, and the prophets, and therest of the books, have no small difference, when they arespoken in their own language. For in the eight and thirtiethyear coming into Egypt, when Euergetes was king, and continuingthere some time, I found a book of no small learning: thereforeI thought it most necessary for me to bestow some diligence andtravail to interpret it; using great watchfulness and skill inthat space to bring the book to an end, and set it forth forthem also, which in a strange country are willing to learn,being prepared before in manners to live after the law.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	1	All wisdom cometh from the Lord, and is with him for ever.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	2	Who can number the sand of the sea, and the drops of rain,and the days of eternity?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	3	Who can find out the height of heaven, and the breadth of theearth, and the deep, and wisdom?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	4	Wisdom hath been created before all things, and theunderstanding of prudence from everlasting.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	5	The word of God most high is the fountain of wisdom; and herways are everlasting commandments.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	6	To whom hath the root of wisdom been revealed? or who hathknown her wise counsels?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	7	[Unto whom hath the knowledge of wisdom been made manifest?and who hath understood her great experience?]
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	8	There is one wise and greatly to be feared, the Lord sittingupon his throne.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	9	He created her, and saw her, and numbered her, and poured herout upon all his works.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	10	She is with all flesh according to his gift, and he hathgiven her to them that love him.

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	14	To fear the Lord is the beginning of wisdom: and it wascreated with the faithful in the womb.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	15	She hath built an everlasting foundation with men, and sheshall continue with their seed.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	16	To fear the Lord is fulness of wisdom, and filleth men withher fruits.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	17	She filleth all their house with things desirable, and thegarners with her increase.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	18	The fear of the Lord is a crown of wisdom, making peace andperfect health to flourish; both which are the gifts of God: andit enlargeth their rejoicing that love him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	19	Wisdom raineth down skill and knowledge of understandingstanding, and exalteth them to honour that hold her fast.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	20	The root of wisdom is to fear the Lord, and the branchesthereof are long life.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	21	The fear of the Lord driveth away sins: and where it ispresent, it turneth away wrath.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	22	A furious man cannot be justified; for the sway of his furyshall be his destruction.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	23	A patient man will tear for a time, and afterward joy shallspring up unto him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	24	He will hide his words for a time, and the lips of many shalldeclare his wisdom.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	25	The parables of knowledge are in the treasures of wisdom: butgodliness is an abomination to a sinner.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	26	If thou desire wisdom, keep the commandments, and the Lordshall give her unto thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	27	For the fear of the Lord is wisdom and instruction: and faithand meekness are his delight.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	28	Distrust not the fear of the Lord when thou art poor: andcome not unto him with a double heart.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	29	Be not an hypocrite in the sight of men, and take good heedwhat thou speakest.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	1	30	Exalt not thyself, lest thou fall, and bring dishonour uponthy soul, and so God discover thy secrets, and cast thee down inthe midst of the congregation, because thou camest not in truthto the fear of the Lord, but thy heart is full of deceit.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	1	My son, if thou come to serve the Lord, prepare thy soul fortemptation.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	2	Set thy heart aright, and constantly endure, and make nothaste in time of trouble.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	3	Cleave unto him, and depart not away, that thou mayest beincreased at thy last end.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	4	Whatsoever is brought upon thee take cheerfully, and bepatient when thou art changed to a low estate.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	5	For gold is tried in the fire, and acceptable men in thefurnace of adversity.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	6	Believe in him, and he will help thee; order thy way aright,and trust in him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	7	Ye that fear the Lord, wait for his mercy; and go not aside,lest ye fall.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	8	Ye that fear the Lord, believe him; and your reward shall notfail.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	9	Ye that fear the Lord, hope for good, and for everlasting joyand mercy.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	10	Look at the generations of old, and see; did ever any trustin the Lord, and was confounded? or did any abide in his fear,and was forsaken? or whom did he ever despise, that called uponhim?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	11	For the Lord is full of compassion and mercy, longsuffering,and very pitiful, and forgiveth sins, and saveth in time ofaffliction.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	12	Woe be to fearful hearts, and faint hands, and the sinnerthat goeth two ways!
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	13	Woe unto him that is fainthearted! for he believeth not;therefore shall he not be defended.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	14	Woe unto you that have lost patience! and what will ye dowhen the Lord shall visit you?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	15	They that fear the Lord will not disobey his Word; and theythat love him will keep his ways.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	16	They that fear the Lord will seek that which is well,pleasing unto him; and they that love him shall be filled withthe law.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	17	They that fear the Lord will prepare their hearts, and humbletheir souls in his sight,
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	2	18	Saying, We will fall into the hands of the Lord, and not intothe hands of men: for as his majesty is, so is his mercy.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	1	Hear me your father, O children, and do thereafter, that yemay be safe.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	2	For the Lord hath given the father honour over the children,and hath confirmed the authority of the mother over the sons.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	3	Whoso honoureth his father maketh an atonement for his sins:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	4	And he that honoureth his mother is as one that layeth uptreasure.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	5	Whoso honoureth his father shall have joy of his ownchildren; and when he maketh his prayer, he shall be heard.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	6	He that honoureth his father shall have a long life; and hethat is obedient unto the Lord shall be a comfort to his mother.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	7	He that feareth the Lord will honour his father, and will doservice unto his parents, as to his masters.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	8	Honour thy father and mother both in word and deed, that ablessing may come upon thee from them.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	9	For the blessing of the father establisheth the houses ofchildren; but the curse of the mother rooteth out foundations.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	10	Glory not in the dishonour of thy father; for thy father'sdishonour is no glory unto thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	11	For the glory of a man is from the honour of his father; anda mother in dishonour is a reproach to the children.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	12	My son, help thy father in his age, and grieve him not aslong as he liveth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	13	And if his understanding fail, have patience with him; anddespise him not when thou art in thy full strength.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	14	For the relieving of thy father shall not be forgotten: andinstead of sins it shall be added to build thee up.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	15	In the day of thine affliction it shall be remembered; thysins also shall melt away, as the ice in the fair warm weather.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	16	He that forsaketh his father is as a blasphemer; and he thatangereth his mother is cursed: of God.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	17	My son, go on with thy business in meekness; so shalt thou bebeloved of him that is approved.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	18	The greater thou art, the more humble thyself, and thou shaltfind favour before the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	19	Many are in high place, and of renown: but mysteries arerevealed unto the meek.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	20	For the power of the Lord is great, and he is honoured of thelowly.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	21	Seek not out things that are too hard for thee, neithersearch the things that are above thy strength.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	22	But what is commanded thee, think thereupon with reverence,for it is not needful for thee to see with thine eyes the thingsthat are in secret.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	23	Be not curious in unnecessary matters: for more things areshewed unto thee than men understand.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	24	For many are deceived by their own vain opinion; and an evilsuspicion hath overthrown their judgment.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	25	Without eyes thou shalt want light: profess not the knowledgetherefore that thou hast not.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	26	A stubborn heart shall fare evil at the last; and he thatloveth danger shall perish therein.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	27	An obstinate heart shall be laden with sorrows; and thewicked man shall heap sin upon sin.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	28	In the punishment of the proud there is no remedy; for theplant of wickedness hath taken root in him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	29	The heart of the prudent will understand a parable; and anattentive ear is the desire of a wise man.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	30	Water will quench a flaming fire; and alms maketh anatonement for sins.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	3	31	And he that requiteth good turns is mindful of that which maycome hereafter; and when he falleth, he shall find a stay.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	1	My son, defraud not the poor of his living, and make not theneedy eyes to wait long.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	2	Make not an hungry soul sorrowful; neither provoke a man inhis distress.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	3	Add not more trouble to an heart that is vexed; and defer notto give to him that is in need.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	4	Reject not the supplication of the afflicted; neither turnaway thy face from a poor man.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	5	Turn not away thine eye from the needy, and give him noneoccasion to curse thee:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	6	For if he curse thee in the bitterness of his soul, hisprayer shall be heard of him that made him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	7	Get thyself the love of the congregation, and bow thy head toa great man.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	8	Let it not grieve thee to bow down thine ear to the poor, andgive him a friendly answer with meekness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	9	Deliver him that suffereth wrong from the hand of theoppressor; and be not fainthearted when thou sittest injudgment.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	10	Be as a father unto the fatherless, and instead of an husbandunto their mother: so shalt thou be as the son of the most High,and he shall love thee more than thy mother doth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	11	Wisdom exalteth her children, and layeth hold of them thatseek her.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	12	He that loveth her loveth life; and they that seek to herearly shall be filled with joy.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	13	He that holdeth her fast shall inherit glory; and wheresoevershe entereth, the Lord will bless.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	14	They that serve her shall minister to the Holy One: and themthat love her the Lord doth love.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	15	Whoso giveth ear unto her shall judge the nations: and hethat attendeth unto her shall dwell securely.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	16	If a man commit himself unto her, he shall inherit her; andhis generation shall hold her in possession.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	17	For at the first she will walk with him by crooked ways, andbring fear and dread upon him, and torment him with herdiscipline, until she may trust his soul, and try him by herlaws.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	18	Then will she return the straight way unto him, and comforthim, and shew him her secrets.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	19	But if he go wrong, she will forsake him, and give him overto his own ruin.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	20	Observe the opportunity, and beware of evil; and be notashamed when it concerneth thy soul.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	21	For there is a shame that bringeth sin; and there is a shamewhich is glory and grace.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	22	Accept no person against thy soul, and let not the reverenceof any man cause thee to fall.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	23	And refrain not to speak, when there is occasion to do good,and hide not thy wisdom in her beauty.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	24	For by speech wisdom shall be known: and learning by the wordof the tongue.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	25	In no wise speak against the truth; but be abashed of theerror of thine ignorance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	26	Be not ashamed to confess thy sins; and force not the courseof the river.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	27	Make not thyself an underling to a foolish man; neitheraccept the person of the mighty.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	28	Strive for the truth unto death, and the Lord shall fight forthee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	29	Be not hasty in thy tongue, and in thy deeds slack andremiss.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	30	Be not as a lion in thy house, nor frantick among thyservants.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	4	31	Let not thine hand be stretched out to receive, and shut whenthou shouldest repay.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	1	Set thy heart upon thy goods; and say not, I have enough formy life.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	2	Follow not thine own mind and thy strength, to walk in theways of thy heart:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	3	And say not, Who shall controul me for my works? for the Lordwill surely revenge thy pride.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	4	Say not, I have sinned, and what harm hath happened unto me?for the Lord is longsuffering, he will in no wise let thee go.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	5	Concerning propitiation, be not without fear to add sin untosin:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	6	And say not His mercy is great; he will be pacified for themultitude of my sins: for mercy and wrath come from him, and hisindignation resteth upon sinners.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	7	Make no tarrying to turn to the Lord, and put not off fromday to day: for suddenly shall the wrath of the Lord come forth,and in thy security thou shalt be destroyed, and perish in theday of vengeance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	8	Set not thine heart upon goods unjustly gotten, for theyshall not profit thee in the day of calamity.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	9	Winnow not with every wind, and go not into every way: for sodoth the sinner that hath a double tongue.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	10	Be stedfast in thy understanding; and let thy word be thesame.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	11	Be swift to hear; and let thy life be sincere; and withpatience give answer.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	12	If thou hast understanding, answer thy neighbour; if not, laythy hand upon thy mouth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	13	Honour and shame is in talk: and the tongue of man is hisfall.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	14	Be not called a whisperer, and lie not in wait with thytongue: for a foul shame is upon the thief, and an evilcondemnation upon the double tongue.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	5	15	Be not ignorant of any thing in a great matter or a small.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	1	Instead of a friend become not an enemy; for [thereby] thoushalt inherit an ill name, shame, and reproach: even so shall asinner that hath a double tongue.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	2	Extol not thyself in the counsel of thine own heart; that thysoul be not torn in pieces as a bull [straying alone.]
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	3	Thou shalt eat up thy leaves, and lose thy fruit, and leavethyself as a dry tree.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	4	A wicked soul shall destroy him that hath it, and shall makehim to be laughed to scorn of his enemies.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	5	Sweet language will multiply friends: and a fairspeakingtongue will increase kind greetings.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	6	Be in peace with many: nevertheless have but one counsellorof a thousand.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	7	If thou wouldest get a friend, prove him first and be nothasty to credit him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	8	For some man is a friend for his own occasion, and will notabide in the day of thy trouble.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	9	And there is a friend, who being turned to enmity, and strifewill discover thy reproach.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	10	Again, some friend is a companion at the table, and will notcontinue in the day of thy affliction.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	11	But in thy prosperity he will be as thyself, and will be boldover thy servants.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	12	If thou be brought low, he will be against thee, and willhide himself from thy face.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	13	Separate thyself from thine enemies, and take heed of thyfriends.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	14	A faithfu1l friend is a strong defence: and he that hathfound such an one hath found a treasure.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	15	Nothing doth countervail a faithful friend, and hisexcellency is invaluable.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	16	A faithful friend is the medicine of life; and they that fearthe Lord shall find him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	17	Whoso feareth the Lord shall direct his friendship aright:for as he is, so shall his neighbour be also.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	18	My son, gather instruction from thy youth up: so shalt thoufind wisdom till thine old age.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	19	Come unto her as one that ploweth and soweth, and wait forher good fruits: for thou shalt not toil much in labouring abouther, but thou shalt eat of her fruits right soon.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	20	She is very unpleasant to the unlearned: he that is withoutunderstanding will not remain with her.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	21	She will lie upon him as a mighty stone of trial; and he willcast her from him ere it be long.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	22	For wisdom is according to her name, and she is not manifestunto many.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	23	Give ear, my son, receive my advice, and refuse not mycounsel,
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	24	And put thy feet into her fetters, and thy neck into herchain.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	25	Bow down thy shoulder, and bear her, and be not grieved withher bonds.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	26	Come unto her with thy whole heart, and keep her ways withall thy power.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	27	Search, and seek, and she shall be made known unto thee: andwhen thou hast got hold of her, let her not go.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	28	For at the last thou shalt find her rest, and that shall beturned to thy joy.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	29	Then shall her fetters be a strong defence for thee, and herchains a robe of glory.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	30	For there is a golden ornament upon her, and her bands arepurple lace.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	31	Thou shalt put her on as a robe of honour, and shalt put herabout thee as a crown of joy.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	32	My son, if thou wilt, thou shalt be taught: and if thou wiltapply thy mind, thou shalt be prudent.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	33	If thou love to hear, thou shalt receive understanding: andif thou bow thine ear, thou shalt be wise,
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	34	Stand in the multitude of the elders; and cleave unto himthat is wise.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	35	Be willing to hear every godly discourse; and let not theparables of understanding escape thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	36	And if thou seest a man of understanding, get thee betimesunto him, and let thy foot wear the steps of his door.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	6	37	Let thy mind be upon the ordinances of the Lord and meditatecontinually in his commandments: he shall establish thine heart,and give thee wisdom at thine owns desire.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	1	Do no evil, so shall no harm come unto thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	2	Depart from the unjust, and iniquity shall turn away fromthee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	3	My son, sow not upon the furrows of unrighteousness, and thoushalt not reap them sevenfold.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	4	Seek not of the Lord preeminence, neither of the king theseat of honour.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	5	justify not thyself before the Lord; and boast not of thywisdom before the king.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	6	Seek not to be judge, being not able to take away iniquity;lest at any time thou fear the person of the mighty, anstumblingblock in the way of thy uprightness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	7	Offend not against the multitude of a city, and then thoushalt not cast thyself down among the people.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	8	Bind not one sin upon another; for in one thou shalt not beunpunished.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	9	Say not, God will look upon the multitude of my oblations,and when I offer to the most high God, he will accept it.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	10	Be not fainthearted when thou makest thy prayer, and neglectnot to give alms.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	11	Laugh no man to scorn in the bitterness of his soul: forthere is one which humbleth and exalteth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	12	Devise not a lie against thy brother; neither do the like tothy friend.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	13	Use not to make any manner of lie: for the custom thereof isnot good.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	14	Use not many words in a multitude of elders, and make notmuch babbling when thou prayest.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	15	Hate not laborious work, neither husbandry, which the mostHigh hath ordained.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	16	Number not thyself among the multitude of sinners, butremember that wrath will not tarry long.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	17	Humble thyself greatly: for the vengeance of the ungodly isfire and worms.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	18	Change not a friend for any good by no means; neither afaithful brother for the gold of Ophir.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	19	Forego not a wise and good woman: for her grace is abovegold.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	20	Whereas thy servant worketh truly, entreat him not evil. northe hireling that bestoweth himself wholly for thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	21	Let thy soul love a good servant, and defraud him not ofliberty.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	22	Hast thou cattle? have an eye to them: and if they be for thyprofit, keep them with thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	23	Hast thou children? instruct them, and bow down their neckfrom their youth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	24	Hast thou daughters? have a care of their body, and shew notthyself cheerful toward them.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	25	Marry thy daughter, and so shalt thou have performed aweighty matter: but give her to a man of understanding.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	26	Hast thou a wife after thy mind? forsake her not: but givenot thyself over to a light woman.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	27	Honour thy father with thy whole heart, and forget not thesorrows of thy mother.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	28	Remember that thou wast begotten of them; and how canst thourecompense them the things that they have done for thee?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	29	Fear the Lord with all thy soul, and reverence his priests.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	30	Love him that made thee with all thy strength, and forsakenot his ministers.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	31	Fear the Lord, and honor the priest; and give him hisportion, as it is commanded thee; the firstfruits, and thetrespass offering, and the gift of the shoulders, and thesacrifice of sanctification, and the firstfruits of the holythings.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	32	And stretch thine hand unto the poor, that thy blessing maybe perfected.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	33	A gift hath grace in the sight of every man living; and forthe dead detain it not.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	34	Fail not to be with them that weep, and mourn with them thatmourn.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	35	Be not slow to visit the sick: fir that shall make thee to bebeloved.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	7	36	Whatsoever thou takest in hand, remember the end, and thoushalt never do amiss.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	1	Strive not with a mighty man' lest thou fall into his hands.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	2	Be not at variance with a rich man, lest he overweigh thee:for gold hath destroyed many, and perverted the hearts of kings.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	3	Strive not with a man that is full of tongue, and heap notwood upon his fire.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	4	Jest not with a rude man, lest thy ancestors be disgraced.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	5	Reproach not a man that turneth from sin, but remember thatwe are all worthy of punishment.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	6	Dishonour not a man in his old age: for even some of us waxold.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	7	Rejoice not over thy greatest enemy being dead, but rememberthat we die all.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	8	Despise not the discourse of the wise, but acquaint thyselfwith their proverbs: for of them thou shalt learn instruction,and how to serve great men with ease.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	9	Miss not the discourse of the elders: for they also learnedof their fathers, and of them thou shalt learn understanding,and to give answer as need requireth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	10	Kindle not the coals of a sinner, lest thou be burnt with theflame of his fire.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	11	Rise not up [in anger] at the presence of an injuriousperson, lest he lie in wait to entrap thee in thy words
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	12	Lend not unto him that is mightier than thyself; for if thoulendest him, count it but lost.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	13	Be not surety above thy power: for if thou be surety, takecare to pay it.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	14	Go not to law with a judge; for they will judge for himaccording to his honour.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	15	Travel not by the way with a bold fellow, lest he becomegrievous unto thee: for he will do according to his own will,and thou shalt perish with him through his folly.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	16	Strive not with an angry man, and go not with him into asolitary place: for blood is as nothing in his sight, and wherethere is no help, he will overthrow thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	17	Consult not with a fool; for he cannot keep counsel.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	18	Do no secret thing before a stranger; for thou knowest notwhat he will bring forth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	8	19	Open not thine heart to every man, lest he requite thee witha shrewd turn.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	1	Be not jealous over the wife of thy bosom, and teach her notan evil lesson against thyself.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	2	Give not thy soul unto a woman to set her foot upon thysubstance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	3	Meet not with an harlot, lest thou fall into her snares.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	4	Use not much the company of a woman that is a singer, lestthou be taken with her attempts.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	5	Gaze not on a maid, that thou fall not by those things thatare precious in her.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	6	Give not thy soul unto harlots, that thou lose not thineinheritance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	7	Look not round about thee in the streets of the city, neitherwander thou in the solitary place thereof.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	8	Turn away thine eye from a beautiful woman, and look not uponanother's beauty; for many have been deceived by the beauty of awoman; for herewith love is kindled as a fire.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	9	Sit not at all with another man's wife, nor sit down with herin thine arms, and spend not thy money with her at the wine;lest thine heart incline unto her, and so through thy desirethou fall into destruction.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	10	Forsake not an old friend; for the new is not comparable tohim: a new friend is as new wine; when it is old, thou shaltdrink it with pleasure.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	11	Envy not the glory of a sinner: for thou knowest not whatshall be his end.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	12	Delight not in the thing that the ungodly have pleasure in;but remember they shall not go unpunished unto their grave.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	13	Keep thee far from the man that hath power to kill; so shaltthou not doubt the fear of death: and if thou come unto him,make no fault, lest he take away thy life presently: rememberthat thou goest in the midst of snares, and that thou walkestupon the battlements of the city.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	14	As near as thou canst, guess at thy neighbour, and consultwith the wise.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	15	Let thy talk be with the wise, and all thy communication inthe law of the most High.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	16	And let just men eat and drink with thee; and let thyglorying be in the fear of the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	17	For the hand of the artificer the work shall be commended:and the wise ruler of the people for his speech.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	9	18	A man of an ill tongue is dangerous in his city; and he thatis rash in his talk shall be hated.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	1	A wise judge will instruct his people; and the government ofa prudent man is well ordered.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	2	As the judge of the people is himself, so are his officers;and what manner of man the ruler of the city is, such are allthey that dwell therein.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	3	An unwise king destroyeth his people; but through theprudence of them which are in authority the city shall beinhabited.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	4	The power of the earth is in the hand of the Lord, and in duetime he will set over it one that is profitable.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	5	In the hand of God is the prosperity of man: and upon theperson of the scribe shall he lay his honour.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	6	Bear not hatred to thy neighbour for every wrong; and donothing at all by injurious practices.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	7	Pride is hateful before God and man: and by both doth onecommit iniquity.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	8	Because of unrighteous dealings, injuries, and riches got bydeceit, the kingdom is translated from one people to another.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	9	Why is earth and ashes proud? There is not a more wickedthing than a covetous man: for such an one setteth his own soulto sale; because while he liveth he casteth away his bowels.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	10	The physician cutteth off a long disease; and he that is today a king to morrow shall die.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	11	For when a man is dead, he shall inherit creeping things,beasts, and worms.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	12	The beginning of pride is when one departeth from God, andhis heart is turned away from his Maker.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	13	For pride is the beginning of sin, and he that hath it shallpour out abomination: and therefore the Lord brought upon themstrange calamities, and overthrew them utterly.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	14	The Lord hath cast down the thrones of proud princes, and setup the meek in their stead.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	15	The Lord hath plucked up the roots of the proud nations, andplanted the lowly in their place.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	16	The Lord overthrew countries of the heathen, and destroyedthem to the foundations of the earth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	17	He took some of them away, and destroyed them, and hath madetheir memorial to cease from the earth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	18	Pride was not made for men, nor furious anger for them thatare born of a woman.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	19	They that fear the Lord are a sure seed, and they that lovehim an honourable plant: they that regard not the law are adishonourable seed; they that transgress the commandments are adeceivable seed.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	20	Among brethren he that is chief is honorable; so are theythat fear the Lord in his eyes.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	21	The fear of the Lord goeth before the obtaining of authority:but roughness and pride is the losing thereof.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	22	Whether he be rich, noble, or poor, their glory is the fearof the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	23	It is not meet to despise the poor man that hathunderstanding; neither is it convenient to magnify a sinfulman.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	24	Great men, and judges, and potentates, shall be honoured; yetis there none of them greater than he that feareth the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	25	Unto the servant that is wise shall they that are free doservice: and he that hath knowledge will not grudge when he isreformed.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	26	Be not overwise in doing thy business; and boast not thyselfin the time of thy distress.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	27	Better is he that laboureth, and aboundeth in all things,than he that boasteth himself, and wanteth bread.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	28	My son, glorify thy soul in meekness, and give it honouraccording to the dignity thereof.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	29	Who will justify him that sinneth against his own soul? andwho will honour him that dishonoureth his own life?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	30	The poor man is honoured for his skill, and the rich man ishonoured for his riches.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	10	31	He that is honoured in poverty, how much more in riches? andhe that is dishonourable in riches, how much more in poverty?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	1	Wisdom lifteth up the head of him that is of low degree, andmaketh him to sit among great men.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	2	Commend not a man for his beauty; neither abhor a man for hisoutward appearance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	3	The bee is little among such as fly; but her fruit is thechief of sweet things.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	4	Boast not of thy clothing and raiment, and exalt not thyselfin the day of honour: for the works of the Lord are wonderful,and his works among men are hidden.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	5	Many kings have sat down upon the ground; and one that wasnever thought of hath worn the crown.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	6	Many mighty men have been greatly disgraced; and thehonourable delivered into other men's hands.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	7	Blame not before thou hast examined the truth: understandfirst, and then rebuke.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	8	Answer not before thou hast heard the cause: neitherinterrupt men in the midst of their talk.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	9	Strive not in a matter that concerneth thee not; and sit notin judgment with sinners.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	10	My son, meddle not with many matters: for if thou meddlemuch, thou shalt not be innocent; and if thou follow after, thoushalt not obtain, neither shalt thou escape by fleeing.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	11	There is one that laboureth, and taketh pains, and makethhaste, and is so much the more behind.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	12	Again, there is another that is slow, and hath need of help,wanting ability, and full of poverty; yet the eye of the Lordlooked upon him for good, and set him up from his low estate,
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	13	And lifted up his head from misery; so that many that sawfrom him is peace over all the
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	14	Prosperity and adversity, life and death, poverty and riches,come of the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	15	Wisdom, knowledge, and understanding of the law, are of theLord: love, and the way of good works, are from him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	16	Error and darkness had their beginning together with sinners:and evil shall wax old with them that glory therein.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	17	The gift of the Lord remaineth with the ungodly, and hisfavour bringeth prosperity for ever.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	18	There is that waxeth rich by his wariness and pinching, andthis his the portion of his reward:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	19	Whereas he saith, I have found rest, and now will eatcontinually of my goods; and yet he knoweth not what time shallcome upon him, and that he must leave those things to others,and die.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	20	Be stedfast in thy covenant, and be conversant therein, andwax old in thy work.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	21	Marvel not at the works of sinners; but trust in the Lord,and abide in thy labour: for it is an easy thing in the sight ofthe Lord on the sudden to make a poor man rich.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	22	The blessing of the Lord is in the reward of the godly, andsuddenly he maketh his blessing flourish.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	23	Say not, What profit is there of my service? and what goodthings shall I have hereafter?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	24	Again, say not, I have enough, and possess many things, andwhat evil shall I have hereafter?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	25	In the day of prosperity there is a forgetfulness ofaffliction: and in the day of affliction there is no moreremembrance of prosperity.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	26	For it is an easy thing unto the Lord in the day of death toreward a man according to his ways.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	27	The affliction of an hour maketh a man forget pleasure: andin his end his deeds shall be discovered.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	28	Judge none blessed before his death: for a man shall be knownin his children.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	29	Bring not every man into thine house: for the deceitful manhath many trains.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	30	Like as a partridge taken [and kept] in a cage, so is theheart of the proud; and like as a spy, watcheth he for thy fall:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	31	For he lieth in wait, and turneth good into evil, and inthings worthy praise will lay blame upon thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	32	Of a spark of fire a heap of coals is kindled: and a sinfulman layeth wait for blood.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	33	Take heed of a mischievous man, for he worketh wickedness;lest he bring upon thee a perpetual blot.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	11	34	Receive a stranger into thine house, and he will disturbthee, and turn thee out of thine own.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	1	When thou wilt do good know to whom thou doest it; so shaltthou be thanked for thy benefits.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	2	Do good to the godly man, and thou shalt find a recompence;and if not from him, yet from the most High.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	3	There can no good come to him that is always occupied inevil, nor to him that giveth no alms.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	4	Give to the godly man, and help not a sinner.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	5	Do well unto him that is lowly, but give not to the ungodly:hold back thy bread, and give it not unto him, lest heovermaster thee thereby: for [else] thou shalt receive twice asmuch evil for all the good thou shalt have done unto him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	6	For the most High hateth sinners, and will repay vengeanceunto the ungodly, and keepeth them against the mighty day oftheir punishment.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	7	Give unto the good, and help not the sinner.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	8	A friend cannot be known in prosperity: and an enemy cannotbe hidden in adversity.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	9	In the prosperity of a man enemies will be grieved: but inhis adversity even a friend will depart.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	10	Never trust thine enemy: for like as iron rusteth, so is hiswickedness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	11	Though he humble himself, and go crouching, yet take goodheed and beware of him, and thou shalt be unto him as if thouhadst wiped a lookingglass, and thou shalt know that his rusthath not been altogether wiped away.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	12	Set him not by thee, lest, when he hath overthrown thee, hestand up in thy place; neither let him sit at thy right hand,lest he seek to take thy seat, and thou at the last remember mywords, and be pricked therewith.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	13	Who will pity a charmer that is bitten with a serpent, or anysuch as come nigh wild beasts?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	14	So one that goeth to a sinner, and is defiled with him in hissins, who will pity?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	15	For a while he will abide with thee, but if thou begin tofall, he will not tarry.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	16	An enemy speaketh sweetly with his lips, but in his heart heimagineth how to throw thee into a pit: he will weep with hiseyes, but if he find opportunity, he will not be satisfied withblood.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	17	If adversity come upon thee, thou shalt find him there first;and though he pretend to help thee, yet shall he undermine thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	12	18	He will shake his head, and clap his hands, and whisper much,and change his countenance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	1	He that toucheth pitch shall be defiled therewith; and hethat hath fellowship with a proud man shall be like unto him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	2	Burden not thyself above thy power while thou livest; andhave no fellowship with one that is mightier and richer thanthyself: for how agree the kettle and the earthen pot together?for if the one be smitten against the other, it shall be broken.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	3	The rich man hath done wrong, and yet he threateneth withal:the poor is wronged, and he must intreat also.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	4	If thou be for his profit, he will use thee: but if thou havenothing, he will forsake thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	5	If thou have any thing, he will live with thee: yea, he willmake thee bare, and will not be sorry for it.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	6	If he have need of thee, he will deceive thee, and smile uponthee, and put thee in hope; he will speak thee fair, and say,What wantest thou?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	7	And he will shame thee by his meats, until he have drawn theedry twice or thrice, and at the last he will laugh thee to scornafterward, when he seeth thee, he will forsake thee, and shakehis head at thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	8	Beware that thou be not deceived and brought down in thyjollity.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	9	If thou be invited of a mighty man, withdraw thyself, and somuch the more will he invite thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	10	Press thou not upon him, lest thou be put back; stand not faroff, lest thou be forgotten.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	11	Affect not to be made equal unto him in talk, and believe nothis many words: for with much communication will he tempt thee,and smiling upon thee will get out thy secrets:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	12	But cruelly he will lay up thy words, and will not spare todo thee hurt, and to put thee in prison.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	13	Observe, and take good heed, for thou walkest in peril of thyoverthrowing: when thou hearest these things, awake in thysleep.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	14	Love the Lord all thy life, and call upon him for thysalvation.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	15	Every beast loveth his like, and every man loveth hisneighbor.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	16	All flesh consorteth according to kind, and a man will cleaveto his like.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	17	What fellowship hath the wolf with the lamb? so the sinnerwith the godly.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	18	What agreement is there between the hyena and a dog? and whatpeace between the rich and the poor?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	19	As the wild ass is the lion's prey in the wilderness: so therich eat up the poor.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	20	As the proud hate humility: so doth the rich abhor the poor.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	21	A rich man beginning to fall is held up of his friends: but apoor man being down is thrust away by his friends.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	22	When a rich man is fallen, he hath many helpers: he speakeththings not to be spoken, and yet men justify him: the poor manslipped, and yet they rebuked him too; he spake wisely, andcould have no place.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	23	When a rich man speaketh, every man holdeth his tongue, and,look, what he saith, they extol it to the clouds: but if thepoor man speak, they say, What fellow is this? and if hestumble, they will help to overthrow him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	24	Riches are good unto him that hath no sin, and poverty isevil in the mouth of the ungodly.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	25	The heart of a man changeth his countenance, whether it befor good or evil: and a merry heart maketh a cheerfulcountenance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	13	26	A cheerful countenance is a token of a heart that is inprosperity; and the finding out of parables is a wearisomelabour of the mind.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	14	1	Blessed is the man that hath not slipped with his mouth, andis not pricked with the multitude of sins.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	14	2	Blessed is he whose conscience hath not condemned him, andwho is not fallen from his hope in the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	14	3	Riches are not comely for a niggard: and what should anenvious man do with money?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	14	4	He that gathereth by defrauding his own soul gathereth forothers, that shall spend his goods riotously.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	14	5	He that is evil to himself, to whom will he be good? he shallnot take pleasure in his goods.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	14	6	There is none worse than he that envieth himself; and this isa recompence of his wickedness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	14	7	And if he doeth good, he doeth it unwillingly; and at thelast he will declare his wickedness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	14	8	The envious man hath a wicked eye; he turneth away his face,and despiseth men.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	14	9	A covetous man's eye is not satisfied with his portion; andthe iniquity of the wicked drieth up his soul.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	14	10	A wicked eye envieth [his] bread, and he is a niggard at histable.
