The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	16	The fool saith, I have no friends, I have no thank for all mygood deeds, and they that eat my bread speak evil of me.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	17	How oft, and of how many shall he be laughed to scorn! for heknoweth not aright what it is to have; and it is all one untohim as if he had it not.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	18	To slip upon a pavement is better than to slip with thetongue: so the fall of the wicked shall come speedily.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	19	An unseasonable tale will always be in the mouth of theunwise.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	20	A wise sentence shall be rejected when it cometh out of afool's mouth; for he will not speak it in due season.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	21	There is that is hindered from sinning through want: and whenhe taketh rest, he shall not be troubled.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	22	There is that destroyeth his own soul through bashfulness,and by accepting of persons overthroweth himself.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	23	There is that for bashfulness promiseth to his friend, andmaketh him his enemy for nothing.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	24	A lie is a foul blot in a man, yet it is continually in themouth of the untaught.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	25	A thief is better than a man that is accustomed to lie: butthey both shall have destruction to heritage.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	26	The disposition of a liar is dishonourable, and his shame isever with him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	27	A wise man shall promote himself to honour with his words:and he that hath understanding will please great men.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	28	He that tilleth his land shall increase his heap: and he thatpleaseth great men shall get pardon for iniquity.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	29	Presents and gifts blind the eyes of the wise, and stop uphis mouth that he cannot reprove.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	30	Wisdom that is hid, and treasure that is hoarded up, whatprofit is in them both?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	31	Better is he that hideth his folly than a man that hideth hiswisdom.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	20	32	Necessary patience in seeking ing the Lord is better than hethat leadeth his life without a guide.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	1	My son, hast thou sinned? do so no more, but ask pardon forthy former sins.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	2	Flee from sin as from the face of a serpent: for if thoucomest too near it, it will bite thee: the teeth thereof are asthe teeth of a lion, slaying the souls of men.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	3	All iniquity is as a two edged sword, the wounds whereofcannot be healed.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	4	To terrify and do wrong will waste riches: thus the house ofproud men shall be made desolate.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	5	A prayer out of a poor man's mouth reacheth to the ears ofGod, and his judgment cometh speedily.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	6	He that hateth to be reproved is in the way of sinners: buthe that feareth the Lord will repent from his heart.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	7	An eloquent man is known far and near; but a man ofunderstanding knoweth when he slippeth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	8	He that buildeth his house with other men's money is like onethat gathereth himself stones for the tomb of his burial.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	9	The congregation of the wicked is like tow wrapped together:and the end of them is a flame of fire to destroy them.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	10	The way of sinners is made plain with stones, but at the endthereof is the pit of hell.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	11	He that keepeth the law of the Lord getteth the understandingthereof: and the perfection of the fear of the Lord is wisdom.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	12	He that is not wise will not be taught: but there is a wisdomwhich multiplieth bitterness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	13	The knowledge of a wise man shall abound like a flood: andhis counsel is like a pure fountain of life.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	14	The inner parts of a fool are like a broken vessel, and hewill hold no knowledge as long as he liveth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	15	If a skilful man hear a wise word, he will commend it, andadd unto it: but as soon as one of no understanding heareth it,it displeaseth him, and he casteth it behind his back.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	16	The talking of a fool is like a burden in the way: but graceshall be found in the lips of the wise.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	17	They enquire at the mouth of the wise man in thecongregation, and they shall ponder his words in their heart.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	18	As is a house that is destroyed, so is wisdom to a fool: andthe knowledge of the unwise is as talk without sense.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	19	Doctrine unto fools is as fetters on the feet, and likemanacles on the right hand.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	20	A fool lifteth up his voice with laughter; but a wise mandoth scarce smile a little.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	21	Learning is unto a wise man as an ornament of gold, and likea bracelet upon his right arm.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	22	A foolish man's foot is soon in his [neighbour's] house: buta man of experience is ashamed of him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	23	A fool will peep in at the door into the house: but he thatis well nurtured will stand without.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	24	It is the rudeness of a man to hearken at the door: but awise man will be grieved with the disgrace.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	25	The lips of talkers will be telling such things as pertainnot unto them: but the words of such as have understanding areweighed in the balance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	26	The heart of fools is in their mouth: but the mouth of thewise is in their heart.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	27	When the ungodly curseth Satan, he curseth his own soul.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	21	28	A whisperer defileth his own soul, and is hated wheresoeverhe dwelleth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	1	A slothful man is compared to a filthy stone, and every onewill hiss him out to his disgrace.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	2	A slothful man is compared to the filth of a dunghill: everyman that takes it up will shake his hand.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	3	An evilnurtured man is the dishonour of his father that begathim: and a [foolish] daughter is born to his loss.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	4	A wise daughter shall bring an inheritance to her husband:but she that liveth dishonestly is her father's heaviness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	5	She that is bold dishonoureth both her father and herhusband, but they both shall despise her.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	6	A tale out of season [is as] musick in mourning: but stripesand correction of wisdom are never out of time.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	7	Whoso teacheth a fool is as one that glueth a potsherdtogether, and as he that waketh one from a sound sleep.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	8	He that telleth a tale to a fool speaketh to one in aslumber: when he hath told his tale, he will say, What is thematter?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	9	If children live honestly, and have wherewithal, they shallcover the baseness of their parents.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	10	But children, being haughty, through disdain and want ofnurture do stain the nobility of their kindred.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	11	Weep for the dead, for he hath lost the light: and weep forthe fool, for he wanteth understanding: make little weeping forthe dead, for he is at rest: but the life of the fool is worsethan death.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	12	Seven days do men mourn for him that is dead; but for a fooland an ungodly man all the days of his life.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	13	Talk not much with a fool, and go not to him that hath nounderstanding: beware of him, lest thou have trouble, and thoushalt never be defiled with his fooleries: depart from him, andthou shalt find rest, and never be disquieted with madness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	14	What is heavier than lead? and what is the name thereof, buta fool?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	15	Sand, and salt, and a mass of iron, is easier to bear, than aman without understanding.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	16	As timber girt and bound together in a building cannot beloosed with shaking: so the heart that is stablished by advisedcounsel shall fear at no time.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	17	A heart settled upon a thought of understanding is as a fairplaistering on the wall of a gallery.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	18	Pales set on an high place will never stand against the wind:so a fearful heart in the imagination of a fool cannot standagainst any fear.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	19	He that pricketh the eye will make tears to fall: and he thatpricketh the heart maketh it to shew her knowledge.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	20	Whoso casteth a stone at the birds frayeth them away: and hethat upbraideth his friend breaketh friendship.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	21	Though thou drewest a sword at thy friend, yet despair not:for there may be a returning [to favour.]
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	22	If thou hast opened thy mouth against thy friend, fear not;for there may be a reconciliation: except for upbraiding, orpride, or disclosing of secrets, or a treacherous wound: for forthese things every friend will depart.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	23	Be faithful to thy neighbour in his poverty, that thou mayestrejoice in his prosperity: abide stedfast unto him in the timeof his trouble, that thou mayest be heir with him in hisheritage: for a mean estate is not always to be contemned: northe rich that is foolish to be had in admiration.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	24	As the vapour and smoke of a furnace goeth before the fire;so reviling before blood.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	25	I will not be ashamed to defend a friend; neither will I hidemyself from him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	26	And if any evil happen unto me by him, every one that hearethit will beware of him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	22	27	Who shall set a watch before my mouth, and a seal of wisdomupon my lips, that I fall not suddenly by them, and that mytongue destroy me not?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	1	O Lord, Father and Governor of all my whole life, leave menot to their counsels, and let me not fall by them.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	2	Who will set scourges over my thoughts, and the discipline ofwisdom over mine heart? that they spare me not for mineignorances, and it pass not by my sins:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	3	Lest mine ignorances increase, and my sins abound to mydestruction, and I fall before mine adversaries, and mine enemyrejoice over me, whose hope is far from thy mercy.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	4	O Lord, Father and God of my life, give me not a proud look,but turn away from thy servants always a haughty mind.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	5	Turn away from me vain hopes and concupiscence, and thoushalt hold him up that is desirous always to serve thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	6	Let not the greediness of the belly nor lust of the fleshtake hold of me; and give not over me thy servant into animpudent mind.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	7	Hear, O ye children, the discipline of the mouth: he thatkeepeth it shall never be taken in his lips.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	8	The sinner shall be left in his foolishness: both the evilspeaker and the proud shall fall thereby.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	9	Accustom not thy mouth to swearing; neither use thyself tothe naming of the Holy One.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	10	For as a servant that is continually beaten shall not bewithout a blue mark: so he that sweareth and nameth Godcontinually shall not be faultless.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	11	A man that useth much swearing shall be filled with iniquity,and the plague shall never depart from his house: if he shalloffend, his sin shall be upon him: and if he acknowledge not hissin, he maketh a double offence: and if he swear in vain, heshall not be innocent, but his house shall be full ofcalamities.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	12	There is a word that is clothed about with death: God grantthat it be not found in the heritage of Jacob; for all suchthings shall be far from the godly, and they shall not wallow intheir sins.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	13	Use not thy mouth to intemperate swearing, for therein is theword of sin.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	14	Remember thy father and thy mother, when thou sittest amonggreat men. Be not forgetful before them, and so thou by thycustom become a fool, and wish that thou hadst not been born,and curse they day of thy nativity.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	15	The man that is accustomed to opprobrious words will never bereformed all the days of his life.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	16	Two sorts of men multiply sin, and the third will bringwrath: a hot mind is as a burning fire, it will never bequenched till it be consumed: a fornicator in the body of hisflesh will never cease till he hath kindled a fire.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	17	All bread is sweet to a whoremonger, he will not leave offtill he die.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	18	A man that breaketh wedlock, saying thus in his heart, Whoseeth me? I am compassed about with darkness, the walls coverme, and no body seeth me; what need I to fear? the most Highwill not remember my sins:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	19	Such a man only feareth the eyes of men, and knoweth not thatthe eyes of the Lord are ten thousand times brighter than thesun, beholding all the ways of men, and considering the mostsecret parts.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	20	He knew all things ere ever they were created; so also afterthey were perfected he looked upon them all.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	21	This man shall be punished in the streets of the city, andwhere he suspecteth not he shall be taken.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	22	Thus shall it go also with the wife that leaveth her husband,and bringeth in an heir by another.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	23	For first, she hath disobeyed the law of the most High; andsecondly, she hath trespassed against her own husband; andthirdly, she hath played the whore in adultery, and broughtchildren by another man.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	24	She shall be brought out into the congregation, andinquisition shall be made of her children.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	25	Her children shall not take root, and her branches shallbring forth no fruit.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	26	She shall leave her memory to be cursed, and her reproachshall not be blotted out.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	27	And they that remain shall know that there is nothing betterthan the fear of the Lord, and that there is nothing sweeterthan to take heed unto the commandments of the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	23	28	It is great glory to follow the Lord, and to be received ofhim is long life.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	1	Wisdom shall praise herself, and shall glory in the midst ofher people.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	2	In the congregation of the most High shall she open hermouth, and triumph before his power.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	3	I came out of the mouth of the most High, and covered theearth as a cloud.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	4	I dwelt in high places, and my throne is in a cloudy pillar.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	5	I alone compassed the circuit of heaven, and walked in thebottom of the deep.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	6	In the waves of the sea and in all the earth, and in everypeople and nation, I got a possession.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	7	With all these I sought rest: and in whose inheritance shallI abide?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	8	So the Creator of all things gave me a commandment, and hethat made me caused my tabernacle to rest, and said, Let thydwelling be in Jacob, and thine inheritance in Israel.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	9	He created me from the beginning before the world, and Ishall never fail.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	10	In the holy tabernacle I served before him; and so was Iestablished in Sion.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	11	Likewise in the beloved city he gave me rest, and inJerusalem was my power.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	12	And I took root in an honourable people, even in the portionof the Lord's inheritance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	13	I was exalted like a cedar in Libanus, and as a cypress treeupon the mountains of Hermon.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	14	I was exalted like a palm tree in En-gaddi, and as a roseplant in Jericho, as a fair olive tree in a pleasant field, andgrew up as a plane tree by the water.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	15	I gave a sweet smell like cinnamon and aspalathus, and Iyielded a pleasant odour like the best myrrh, as galbanum, andonyx, and sweet storax, and as the fume of frankincense in thetabernacle.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	16	As the turpentine tree I stretched out my branches, and mybranches are the branches of honour and grace.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	17	As the vine brought I forth pleasant savour, and my flowersare the fruit of honour and riches.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	18	I am the mother of fair love, and fear, and knowledge, andholy hope: I therefore, being eternal, am given to all mychildren which are named of him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	19	Come unto me, all ye that be desirous of me, and fillyourselves with my fruits.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	20	For my memorial is sweeter than honey, and mine inheritancethan the honeycomb.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	21	They that eat me shall yet be hungry, and they that drink meshall yet be thirsty.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	22	He that obeyeth me shall never be confounded, and they thatwork by me shall not do amiss.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	23	All these things are the book of the covenant of the mosthigh God, even the law which Moses commanded for an heritageunto the congregations of Jacob.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	24	Faint not to be strong in the Lord; that he may confirm you,cleave unto him: for the Lord Almighty is God alone, and besidehim there is no other Saviour.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	25	He filleth all things with his wisdom, as Phison and asTigris in the time of the new fruits.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	26	He maketh the understanding to abound like Euphrates, and asJordan in the time of the harvest.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	27	He maketh the doctrine of knowledge appear as the light, andas Geon in the time of vintage.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	28	The first man knew her not perfectly: no more shall the lastfind her out.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	29	For her thoughts are more than the sea, and her counselsprofounder than the great deep.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	30	I also came out as a brook from a river, and as a conduitinto a garden.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	31	I said, I will water my best garden, and will waterabundantly my garden bed: and, lo, my brook became a river, andmy river became a sea.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	32	I will yet make doctrine to shine as the morning, and willsend forth her light afar off.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	33	I will yet pour out doctrine as prophecy, and leave it to allages for ever.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	24	34	Behold that I have not laboured for myself only, but for allthem that seek wisdom.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	1	In three things I was beautified, and stood up beautiful bothbefore God and men: the unity of brethren, the love ofneighbours, a man and a wife that agree together.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	2	Three sorts of men my soul hateth, and I am greatly offendedat their life: a poor man that is proud, a rich man that is aliar, and an old adulterer that doateth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	3	If thou hast gathered nothing in thy youth, how canst thoufind any thing in thine age?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	4	O how comely a thing is judgment for gray hairs, and forancient men to know counsel!
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	5	O how comely is the wisdom of old men, and understanding andcounsel to men of honour.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	6	Much experience is the crown of old men, and the fear of Godis their glory.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	7	There be nine things which I have judged in mine heart to behappy, and the tenth I will utter with my tongue: A man thathath joy of his children; and he that liveth to see the fall ofhis enemy:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	8	Well is him that dwelleth with a wife of understanding, andthat hath not slipped with his tongue, and that hath not serveda man more unworthy than himself:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	9	Well is him that hath found prudence, and he that speaketh inthe ears of them that will hear:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	10	O how great is he that findeth wisdom! yet is there noneabove him that feareth the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	11	But the love of the Lord passeth all things for illumination:he that holdeth it, whereto shall he be likened?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	12	The fear of the Lord is the beginning of his love: and faithis the beginning of cleaving unto him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	13	[Give me] any plague, but the plague of the heart: and anywickedness, but the wickedness of a woman:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	14	And any affliction, but the affliction from them that hateme: and any revenge, but the revenge of enemies.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	15	There is no head above the head of a serpent; and there is nowrath above the wrath of an enemy.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	16	I had rather dwell with a lion and a dragon, than to keephouse with a wicked woman.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	17	The wickedness of a woman changeth her face, and darkenethher countenance like sackcloth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	18	Her husband shall sit among his neighbours; and when heheareth it shall sigh bitterly.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	19	All wickedness is but little to the wickedness of a woman:let the portion of a sinner fall upon her.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	20	As the climbing up a sandy way is to the feet of the aged, sois a wife full of words to a quiet man.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	21	Stumble not at the beauty of a woman, and desire her not forpleasure.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	22	A woman, if she maintain her husband, is full of anger,impudence, and much reproach.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	23	A wicked woman abateth the courage, maketh an heavycountenance and a wounded heart: a woman that will not comforther husband in distress maketh weak hands and feeble knees.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	24	Of the woman came the beginning of sin, and through her weall die.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	25	Give the water no passage; neither a wicked woman liberty togad abroad.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	25	26	If she go not as thou wouldest have her, cut her off from thyflesh, and give her a bill of divorce, and let her go.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	1	Blessed is the man that hath a virtuous wife, for the numberof his days shall be double.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	2	A virtuous woman rejoiceth her husband, and he shall fulfilthe years of his life in peace.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	3	A good wife is a good portion, which shall be given in theportion of them that fear the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	4	Whether a man be rich or poor, if he have a good heart towardthe Lord, he shall at all times rejoice with a cheerfulcountenance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	5	There be three things that mine heart feareth; and for thefourth I was sore afraid: the slander of a city, the gatheringtogether of an unruly multitude, and a false accusation: allthese are worse than death.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	6	But a grief of heart and sorrow is a woman that is jealousover another woman, and a scourge of the tongue whichcommunicateth with all.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	7	An evil wife is a yoke shaken to and fro: he that hath holdof her is as though he held a scorpion.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	8	A drunken woman and a gadder abroad causeth great anger, andshe will not cover her own shame.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	9	The whoredom of a woman may be known in her haughty looks andeyelids.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	10	If thy daughter be shameless, keep her in straitly, lest sheabuse herself through overmuch liberty.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	11	Watch over an impudent eye: and marvel not if she trespassagainst thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	12	She will open her mouth, as a thirsty traveller when he hathfound a fountain, and drink of every water near her: by everyhedge will she sit down, and open her quiver against everyarrow.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	13	The grace of a wife delighteth her husband, and herdiscretion will fatten his bones.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	14	A silent and loving woman is a gift of the Lord; and there isnothing so much worth as a mind well instructed.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	15	A shamefaced and faithful woman is a double grace, and hercontinent mind cannot be valued.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	16	As the sun when it ariseth in the high heaven; so is thebeauty of a good wife in the ordering of her house.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	17	As the clear light is upon the holy candlestick; so is thebeauty of the face in ripe age.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	18	As the golden pillars are upon the sockets of silver; so arethe fair feet with a constant heart.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	19	My son, keep the flower of thine age sound; and give not thystrength to strangers.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	20	When thou hast gotten a fruitful possession through all thefield, sow it with thine own seed, trusting in the goodness ofthy stock.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	21	So thy race which thou leavest shall be magnified, having theconfidence of their good descent.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	22	An harlot shall be accounted as spittle; but a married womanis a tower against death to her husband.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	23	A wicked woman is given as a portion to a wicked man: but agodly woman is given to him that feareth the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	24	A dishonest woman contemneth shame: but an honest woman willreverence her husband.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	25	A shameless woman shall be counted as a dog; but she that isshamefaced will fear the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	26	A woman that honoureth her husband shall be judged wise ofall; but she that dishonoureth him in her pride shall be countedungodly of all.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	27	A loud crying woman and a scold shall be sought out to driveaway the enemies.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	28	There be two things that grieve my heart; and the thirdmaketh me angry: a man of war that suffereth poverty; and men ofunderstanding that are not set by; and one that returneth fromrighteousness to sin; the Lord prepareth such an one for thesword.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	26	29	A merchant shall hardly keep himself from doing wrong; and anhuckster shall not be freed from sin.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	1	Many have sinned for a small matter; and he that seeketh forabundance will turn his eyes away.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	2	As a nail sticketh fast between the joinings of the stones;so doth sin stick close between buying and selling.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	3	Unless a man hold himself diligently in the fear of the Lord,his house shall soon be overthrown.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	4	As when one sifteth with a sieve, the refuse remaineth; sothe filth of man in his talk.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	5	The furnace proveth the potter's vessels; so the trial of manis in his reasoning.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	6	The fruit declareth if the tree have been dressed; so is theutterance of a conceit in the heart of man.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	7	Praise no man before thou hearest him speak; for this is thetrial of men.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	8	If thou followest righteousness, thou shalt obtain her, andput her on, as a glorious long robe.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	9	The birds will resort unto their like; so will truth returnunto them that practise in her.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	10	As the lion lieth in wait for the prey; so sin for them thatwork iniquity.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	11	The discourse of a godly man is always with wisdom; but afool changeth as the moon.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	12	If thou be among the indiscreet, observe the time; but becontinually among men of understanding.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	13	The discourse of fools is irksome, and their sport is thewantonness of sin.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	14	The talk of him that sweareth much maketh the hair standupright; and their brawls make one stop his ears.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	15	The strife of the proud is bloodshedding, and their revilingsare grievous to the ear.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	16	Whoso discovereth secrets loseth his credit; and shall neverfind friend to his mind.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	17	Love thy friend, and be faithful unto him: but if thoubetrayest his secrets, follow no more after him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	18	For as a man hath destroyed his enemy; so hast thou lost thelove of thy neighbor.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	19	As one that letteth a bird go out of his hand, so hast thoulet thy neighbour go, and shalt not get him again
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	20	Follow after him no more, for he is too far off; he is as aroe escaped out of the snare.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	21	As for a wound, it may be bound up; and after reviling theremay be reconcilement: but he that betrayeth secrets is withouthope.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	22	He that winketh with the eyes worketh evil: and he thatknoweth him will depart from him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	23	When thou art present, he will speak sweetly, and will admirethy words: but at the last he will writhe his mouth, and slanderthy sayings.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	24	I have hated many things, but nothing like him; for the Lordwill hate him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	25	Whoso casteth a stone on high casteth it on his own head; anda deceitful stroke shall make wounds.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	26	Whoso diggeth a pit shall fall therein: and he that setteth atrap shall be taken therein.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	27	He that worketh mischief, it shall fall upon him, and heshall not know whence it cometh.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	28	Mockery and reproach are from the proud; but vengeance, as alion, shall lie in wait for them.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	29	They that rejoice at the fall of the righteous shall be takenin the snare; and anguish shall consume them before they die.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	27	30	Malice and wrath, even these are abominations; and the sinfulman shall have them both.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	1	He that revengeth shall find vengeance from the Lord, and hewill surely keep his sins [in remembrance.]
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	2	Forgive thy neighbour the hurt that he hath done unto thee,so shall thy sins also be forgiven when thou prayest.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	3	One man beareth hatred against another, and doth he seekpardon from the Lord?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	4	He sheweth no mercy to a man, which is like himself: and dothhe ask forgiveness of his own sins?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	5	If he that is but flesh nourish hatred, who will intreat forpardon of his sins?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	6	Remember thy end, and let enmity cease; [remember] corruptionand death, and abide in the commandments.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	7	Remember the commandments, and bear no malice to thyneighbour: [remember] the covenant of the Highest, and wink atignorance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	8	Abstain from strife, and thou shalt diminish thy sins: for afurious man will kindle strife,
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	9	A sinful man disquieteth friends, and maketh debate amongthem that be at peace.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	10	As the matter of the fire is, so it burneth: and as a man'sstrength is, so is his wrath; and according to his riches hisanger riseth; and the stronger they are which contend, the morethey will be inflamed.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	11	An hasty contention kindleth a fire: and an hasty fightingsheddeth blood.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	12	If thou blow the spark, it shall burn: if thou spit upon it,it shall be quenched: and both these come out of thy mouth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	13	Curse the whisperer and doubletongued: for such havedestroyed many that were at peace.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	14	A backbiting tongue hath disquieted many, and driven themfrom nation to nation: strong cities hath it pulled down, andoverthrown the houses of great men.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	15	A backbiting tongue hath cast out virtuous women, anddeprived them of their labours.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	16	Whoso hearkeneth unto it shall never find rest, and neverdwell quietly.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	17	The stroke of the whip maketh marks in the flesh: but thestroke of the tongue breaketh the bones.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	18	Many have fallen by the edge of the sword: but not so many ashave fallen by the tongue.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	19	Well is he that is defended through the venom thereof; whohath not drawn the yoke thereof, nor hath been bound in herbands.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	20	For the yoke thereof is a yoke of iron, and the bands thereofare bands of brass.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	21	The death thereof is an evil death, the grave were betterthan it.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	22	It shall not have rule over them that fear God, neither shallthey be burned with the flame thereof.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	23	Such as forsake the Lord shall fall into it; and it shallburn in them, and not be quenched; it shall be sent upon them asa lion, and devour them as a leopard.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	24	Look that thou hedge thy possession about with thorns, andbind up thy silver and gold,
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	25	And weigh thy words in a balance, and make a door and bar forthy mouth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	28	26	Beware thou slide not by it, lest thou fall before him thatlieth in wait.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	1	He that is merciful will lend unto his neighbour; and he thatstrengtheneth his hand keepeth the commandments.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	2	Lend to thy neighbour in time of his need, and pay thou thyneighbour again in due season.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	3	Keep thy word, and deal faithfully with him, and thou shaltalways find the thing that is necessary for thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	4	Many, when a thing was lent them, reckoned it to be found,and put them to trouble that helped them.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	5	Till he hath received, he will kiss a man's hand; and for hisneighbour's money he will speak submissly: but when he shouldrepay, he will prolong the time, and return words of grief, andcomplain of the time.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	6	If he prevail, he shall hardly receive the half, and he willcount as if he had found it: if not, he hath deprived him of hismoney, and he hath gotten him an enemy without cause: he payethhim with cursings and railings; and for honour he will pay himdisgrace.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	7	Many therefore have refused to lend for other men's illdealing, fearing to be defrauded.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	8	Yet have thou patience with a man in poor estate, and delaynot to shew him mercy.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	9	Help the poor for the commandment's sake, and turn him notaway because of his poverty.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	10	Lose thy money for thy brother and thy friend, and let it notrust under a stone to be lost.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	11	Lay up thy treasure according to the commandments of the mostHigh, and it shall bring thee more profit than gold.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	12	Shut up alms in thy storehouses: and it shall deliver theefrom all affliction.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	13	It shall fight for thee against thine enemies better than amighty shield and strong spear.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	14	An honest man is surety for his neighbour: but he that isimpudent will forsake him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	15	Forget not the friendship of thy surety, for he hath givenhis life for thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	16	A sinner will overthrow the good estate of his surety:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	17	And he that is of an unthankful mind will leave him [indanger] that delivered him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	18	Suretiship hath undone many of good estate, and shaken themas a wave of the sea: mighty men hath it driven from theirhouses, so that they wandered among strange nations.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	19	A wicked man transgressing the commandments of the Lord shallfall into suretiship: and he that undertaketh and followethother men's business for gain shall fall into suits.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	20	Help thy neighbour according to thy power, and beware thatthou thyself fall not into the same.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	21	The chief thing for life is water, and bread, and clothing,and an house to cover shame.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	22	Better is the life of a poor man in a mean cottage, thandelicate fare in another man's house.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	23	Be it little or much, hold thee contented, that thou hear notthe reproach of thy house.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	24	For it is a miserable life to go from house to house: forwhere thou art a stranger, thou darest not open thy mouth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	25	Thou shalt entertain, and feast, and have no thanks: moreoverthou shalt hear bitter words:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	26	Come, thou stranger, and furnish a table, and feed me of thatthou hast ready.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	27	Give place, thou stranger, to an honourable man; my brothercometh to be lodged, and I have need of mine house.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	29	28	These things are grievous to a man of understanding; theupbraiding of houseroom, and reproaching of the lender.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	1	He that loveth his son causeth him oft to feel the rod, thathe may have joy of him in the end.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	2	He that chastiseth his son shall have joy in him, and shallrejoice of him among his acquaintance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	3	He that teacheth his son grieveth the enemy: and before hisfriends he shall rejoice of him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	4	Though his father die, yet he is as though he were not dead:for he hath left one behind him that is like himself.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	5	While he lived, he saw and rejoiced in him: and when he died,he was not sorrowful.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	6	He left behind him an avenger against his enemies, and onethat shall requite kindness to his friends.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	7	He that maketh too much of his son shall bind up his wounds;and his bowels will be troubled at every cry.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	8	An horse not broken becometh headstrong: and a child left tohimself will be wilful.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	9	Cocker thy child, and he shall make thee afraid: play withhim, and he will bring thee to heaviness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	10	Laugh not with him, lest thou have sorrow with him, and lestthou gnash thy teeth in the end.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	11	Give him no liberty in his youth, and wink not at hisfollies.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	12	Bow down his neck while he is young, and beat him on thesides while he is a child, lest he wax stubborn, and bedisobedient unto thee, and so bring sorrow to thine heart.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	13	Chastise thy son, and hold him to labour, lest his lewdbehaviour be an offence unto thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	14	Better is the poor, being sound and strong of constitution,than a rich man that is afflicted in his body.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	15	Health and good estate of body are above all gold, and astrong body above infinite wealth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	16	There is no riches above a sound body, and no joy above thejoy of the heart.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	17	Death is better than a bitter life or continual sickness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	18	Delicates poured upon a mouth shut up are as messes of meatset upon a grave.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	19	What good doeth the offering unto an idol? for neither can iteat nor smell: so is he that is persecuted of the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	20	He seeth with his eyes and groaneth, as an eunuch thatembraceth a virgin and sigheth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	21	Give not over thy mind to heaviness, and afflict not thyselfin thine own counsel.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	22	The gladness of the heart is the life of man, and thejoyfulness of a man prolongeth his days.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	23	Love thine own soul, and comfort thy heart, remove sorrow farfrom thee: for sorrow hath killed many, and there is no profittherein.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	24	Envy and wrath shorten the life, and carefulness bringeth agebefore the time.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	30	25	A cheerful and good heart will have a care of his meat anddiet.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	1	Watching for riches consumeth the flesh, and the care thereofdriveth away sleep.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	2	Watching care will not let a man slumber, as a sore diseasebreaketh sleep,
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	3	The rich hath great labour in gathering riches together; andwhen he resteth, he is filled with his delicates.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	4	The poor laboureth in his poor estate; and when he leavethoff, he is still needy.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	5	He that loveth gold shall not be justified, and he thatfolloweth corruption shall have enough thereof.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	6	Gold hath been the ruin of many, and their destruction waspresent.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	7	It is a stumblingblock unto them that sacrifice unto it, andevery fool shall be taken therewith.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	8	Blessed is the rich that is found without blemish, and hathnot gone after gold.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	9	Who is he? and we will call him blessed: for wonderful thingshath he done among his people.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	10	Who hath been tried thereby, and found perfect? then let himglory. Who might offend, and hath not offended? or done evil,and hath not done it?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	11	His goods shall be established, and the congregation shalldeclare his alms.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	12	If thou sit at a bountiful table, be not greedy upon it, andsay not, There is much meat on it.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	13	Remember that a wicked eye is an evil thing: and what iscreated more wicked than an eye? therefore it weepeth upon everyoccasion.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	14	Stretch not thine hand whithersoever it looketh, and thrustit not with him into the dish.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	15	Judge not thy neighbour by thyself: and be discreet in everypoint.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	16	Eat as it becometh a man, those things which are set beforethee; and devour note, lest thou be hated.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	17	Leave off first for manners' sake; and be not unsatiable,lest thou offend.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	18	When thou sittest among many, reach not thine hand out firstof all.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	19	A very little is sufficient for a man well nurtured, and hefetcheth not his wind short upon his bed.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	20	Sound sleep cometh of moderate eating: he riseth early, andhis wits are with him: but the pain of watching, and choler, andpangs of the belly, are with an unsatiable man.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	21	And if thou hast been forced to eat, arise, go forth, vomit,and thou shalt have rest.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	22	My son, hear me, and despise me not, and at the last thoushalt find as I told thee: in all thy works be quick, so shallthere no sickness come unto thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	23	Whoso is liberal of his meat, men shall speak well of him;and the report of his good housekeeping will be believed.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	24	But against him that is a niggard of his meat the whole cityshall murmur; and the testimonies of his niggardness shall notbe doubted of.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	25	Shew not thy valiantness in wine; for wine hath destroyedmany.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	26	The furnace proveth the edge by dipping: so doth wine thehearts of the proud by drunkeness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	27	Wine is as good as life to a man, if it be drunk moderately:what life is then to a man that is without wine? for it was madeto make men glad.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	28	Wine measurably drunk and in season bringeth gladness of theheart, and cheerfulness of the mind:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	29	But wine drunken with excess maketh bitterness of the mind,with brawling and quarrelling.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	30	Drunkenness increaseth the rage of a fool till he offend: itdiminisheth strength, and maketh wounds.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	31	31	Rebuke not thy neighbour at the wine, and despise him not inhis mirth: give him no despiteful words, and press not upon himwith urging him [to drink.]
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	1	If thou be made the master [of a feast,] lift not thyself up,but be among them as one of the rest; take diligent care forthem, and so sit down.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	2	And when thou hast done all thy office, take thy place, thatthou mayest be merry with them, and receive a crown for thy wellordering of the feast.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	3	Speak, thou that art the elder, for it becometh thee, butwith sound judgment; and hinder not musick.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	4	Pour not out words where there is a musician, and shew notforth wisdom out of time.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	5	A concert of musick in a banquet of wine is as a signet ofcarbuncle set in gold.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	6	As a signet of an emerald set in a work of gold, so is themelody of musick with pleasant wine.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	7	Speak, young man, if there be need of thee: and yet scarcelywhen thou art twice asked.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	8	Let thy speech be short, comprehending much in few words; beas one that knoweth and yet holdeth his tongue.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	9	If thou be among great men, make not thyself equal with them;and when ancient men are in place, use not many words.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	10	Before the thunder goeth lightning; and before a shamefacedman shall go favour.

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	18	A man of counsel will be considerate; but a strange and proudman is not daunted with fear, even when of himself he hath donewithout counsel.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	32	19	Do nothing without advice; and when thou hast once done,repent not.

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	10	And all men are from the ground, and Adam was created ofearth:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	11	In much knowledge the Lord hath divided them, and made theirways diverse.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	12	Some of them hath he blessed and exalted and some of them hesanctified, and set near himself: but some of them hath hecursed and brought low, and turned out of their places.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	13	As the clay is in the potter's hand, to fashion it at hispleasure: so man is in the hand of him that made him, to renderto them as liketh him best.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	14	Good is set against evil, and life against death: so is thegodly against the sinner, and the sinner against the godly.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	15	So look upon all the works of the most High; and there aretwo and two, one against another.

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	20	As long as thou livest and hast breath in thee, give notthyself over to any.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	21	For better it is that thy children should seek to thee, thanthat thou shouldest stand to their courtesy.

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	23	At the time when thou shalt end thy days, and finish thylife, distribute thine inheritance.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	24	Fodder, a wand, and burdens, are for the ass; and bread,correction, and work, for a servant. .
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	25	If thou set thy servant to labour, thou shalt find rest: butif thou let him go idle, he shall seek liberty.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	26	A yoke and a collar do bow the neck: so are tortures andtorments for an evil servant.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	27	Send him to labour, that he be not idle; for idlenessteacheth much evil.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	28	Set him to work, as is fit for him: if he be not obedient,put on more heavy fetters.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	33	29	But be not excessive toward any; and without discretion donothing.

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	34	1	The hopes of a man void of understanding are vain and false:and dreams lift up fools.

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	34	3	The vision of dreams is the resemblance of one thing toanother, even as the likeness of a face to a face.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	34	4	Of an unclean thing what can be cleansed? and from that thingwhich is false what truth can come?

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	34	7	For dreams have deceived many, and they have failed that puttheir trust in them.

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	34	9	A man that hath travelled knoweth many things; and he thathath much experience will declare wisdom.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	34	10	He that hath no experience knoweth little: but he that hathtravelled is full of prudence.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	34	11	When I travelled, I saw many things; and I understand morethan I can express.

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	21	Forget it not, for there is no turning again: thou shalt notdo him good, but hurt thyself.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	22	Remember my judgment: for thine also shall be so; yesterdayfor me, and to day for thee.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	23	When the dead is at rest, let his remembrance rest; and becomforted for him, when his Spirit is departed from him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	24	The wisdom of a learned man cometh by opportunity of leisure:and he that hath little business shall become wise.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	25	How can he get wisdom that holdeth the plough, and thatglorieth in the goad, that driveth oxen, and is occupied intheir labours, and whose talk is of bullocks?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	26	He giveth his mind to make furrows; and is diligent to givethe kine fodder.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	27	So every carpenter and workmaster, that laboureth night andday: and they that cut and grave seals, and are diligent to makegreat variety, and give themselves to counterfeit imagery, andwatch to finish a work:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	28	The smith also sitting by the anvil, and considering the ironwork, the vapour of the fire wasteth his flesh, and he fightethwith the heat of the furnace: the noise of the hammer and theanvil is ever in his ears, and his eyes look still upon thepattern of the thing that he maketh; he setteth his mind tofinish his work, and watcheth to polish it perfectly:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	29	So doth the potter sitting at his work, and turning the wheelabout with his feet, who is alway carefully set at his work, andmaketh all his work by number;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	30	He fashioneth the clay with his arm, and boweth down hisstrength before his feet; he applieth himself to lead it over;and he is diligent to make clean the furnace:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	31	All these trust to their hands: and every one is wise in hiswork.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	32	Without these cannot a city be inhabited: and they shall notdwell where they will, nor go up and down:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	33	They shall not be sought for in publick counsel, nor sit highin the congregation: they shall not sit on the judges' seat, norunderstand the sentence of judgment: they cannot declare justiceand judgment; and they shall not be found where parables arespoken.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	38	34	But they will maintain the state of the world, and [all]their desire is in the work of their craft.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	1	But he that giveth his mind to the law of the most High, andis occupied in the meditation thereof, will seek out the wisdomof all the ancient, and be occupied in prophecies.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	2	He will keep the sayings of the renowned men: and wheresubtil parables are, he will be there also.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	3	He will seek out the secrets of grave sentences, and beconversant in dark parables.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	4	He shall serve among great men, and appear before princes: hewill travel through strange countries; for he hath tried thegood and the evil among men.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	5	He will give his heart to resort early to the Lord that madehim, and will pray before the most High, and will open his mouthin prayer, and make supplication for his sins.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	6	When the great Lord will, he shall be filled with the spiritof understanding: he shall pour out wise sentences, and givethanks unto the Lord in his prayer.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	7	He shall direct his counsel and knowledge, and in his secretsshall he meditate.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	8	He shall shew forth that which he hath learned, and shallglory in the law of the covenant of the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	9	Many shall commend his understanding; and so long as theworld endureth, it shall not be blotted out; his memorial shallnot depart away, and his name shall live from generation togeneration.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	10	Nations shall shew forth his wisdom, and the congregationshall declare his praise.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	11	If he die, he shall leave a greater name than a thousand: andif he live, he shall increase it.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	12	Yet have I more to say, which I have thought upon; for I amfilled as the moon at the full.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	13	Hearken unto me, ye holy children, and bud forth as a rosegrowing by the brook of the field:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	14	And give ye a sweet savour as frankincense, and flourish as alily, send forth a smell, and sing a song of praise, bless theLord in all his works.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	15	Magnify his name, and shew forth his praise with the songs ofyour lips, and with harps, and in praising him ye shall sayafter this manner:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	16	All the works of the Lord are exceeding good, and whatsoeverhe commandeth shall be accomplished in due season.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	17	And none may say, What is this? wherefore is that? for attime convenient they shall all be sought out: at his commandmentthe waters stood as an heap, and at the words of his mouth thereceptacles of waters.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	18	At his commandment is done whatsoever pleaseth him; and nonecan hinder, when he will save.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	19	The works of all flesh are before him, and nothing can be hidfrom his eyes.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	20	He seeth from everlasting to everlasting; and there isnothing wonderful before him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	21	A man need not to say, What is this? wherefore is that? forhe hath made all things for their uses.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	22	His blessing covered the dry land as a river, and watered itas a flood.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	23	As he hath turned the waters into saltness: so shall theheathen inherit his wrath.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	24	As his ways are plain unto the holy; so are theystumblingblocks unto the wicked.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	25	For the good are good things created from the beginning: soevil things for sinners.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	26	The principal things for the whole use of man's life arewater, fire, iron, and salt, flour of wheat, honey, milk, andthe blood of the grape, and oil, and clothing.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	27	All these things are for good to the godly: so to the sinnersthey are turned into evil.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	28	There be spirits that are created for vengeance, which intheir fury lay on sore strokes; in the time of destruction theypour out their force, and appease the wrath of him that madethem.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	29	Fire, and hail, and famine, and death, all these were createdfor vengeance;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	30	Teeth of wild beasts, and scorpions, serpents, and the swordpunishing the wicked to destruction.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	31	They shall rejoice in his commandment, and they shall beready upon earth, when need is; and when their time is come,they shall not transgress his word.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	32	Therefore from the beginning I was resolved, and thought uponthese things, and have left them in writing.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	33	All the works of the Lord are good: and he will give everyneedful thing in due season.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	34	So that a man cannot say, This is worse than that: for intime they shall all be well approved.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	39	35	And therefore praise ye the Lord with the whole heart andmouth, and bless the name of the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	1	Great travail is created for every man, and an heavy yoke isupon the sons of Adam, from the day that they go out of theirmother's womb, till the day that they return to the mother ofall things.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	2	Their imagination of things to come, and the day of death,[trouble] their thoughts, and [cause] fear of heart;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	3	From him that sitteth on a throne of glory, unto him that ishumbled in earth and ashes;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	4	From him that weareth purple and a crown, unto him that isclothed with a linen frock.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	5	Wrath, and envy, trouble, and unquietness, fear of death, andanger, and strife, and in the time of rest upon his bed hisnight sleep, do change his knowledge.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	6	A little or nothing is his rest, and afterward he is in hissleep, as in a day of keeping watch, troubled in the vision ofhis heart, as if he were escaped out of a battle.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	7	When all is safe, he awaketh, and marvelleth that the fearwas nothing.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	8	[Such things happen] unto all flesh, both man and beast, andthat is sevenfold more upon sinners.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	9	Death, and bloodshed, strife, and sword, calamities, famine,tribulation, and the scourge;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	10	These things are created for the wicked, and for their sakescame the flood.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	11	All things that are of the earth shall turn to the earthagain: and that which is of the waters doth return into the sea.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	12	All bribery and injustice shall be blotted out: but truedealing shall endure for ever.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	13	The goods of the unjust shall be dried up like a river, andshall vanish with noise, like a great thunder in rain.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	14	While he openeth his hand he shall rejoice: so shalltransgressors come to nought.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	15	The children of the ungodly shall not bring forth manybranches: but are as unclean roots upon a hard rock.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	16	The weed growing upon every water and bank of a river shallbe pulled up before all grass.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	17	Bountifulness is as a most fruitful garden, and mercifulnessendureth for ever.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	18	To labour, and to be content with that a man hath, is a sweetlife: but he that findeth a treasure is above them both.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	19	Children and the building of a city continue a man's name:but a blameless wife is counted above them both.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	20	Wine and musick rejoice the heart: but the love of wisdom isabove them both.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	21	The pipe and the psaltery make sweet melody: but a pleasanttongue is above them both.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	22	Thine eye desireth favour and beauty: but more than both cornwhile it is green.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	23	A friend and companion never meet amiss: but above both is awife with her husband.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	24	Brethren and help are against time of trouble: but alms shalldeliver more than them both.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	25	Gold and silver make the foot stand sure: but counsel isesteemed above them both.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	26	Riches and strength lift up the heart: but the fear of theLord is above them both: there is no want in the fear of theLord, and it needeth not to seek help.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	27	The fear of the Lord is a fruitful garden, and covereth himabove all glory.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	28	My son, lead not a beggar's life; for better it is to diethan to beg.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	29	The life of him that dependeth on another man's table is notto be counted for a life; for he polluteth himself with othermen's meat: but a wise man well nurtured will beware thereof.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	40	30	Begging is sweet in the mouth of the shameless: but in hisbelly there shall burn a fire.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	1	O death, how bitter is the remembrance of thee to a man thatliveth at rest in his possessions, unto the man that hathnothing to vex him, and that hath prosperity in all things: yea,unto him that is yet able to receive meat!
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	2	O death, acceptable is thy sentence unto the needy, and untohim whose strength faileth, that is now in the last age, and isvexed with all things, and to him that despaireth, and hath lostpatience!
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	3	Fear not the sentence of death, remember them that have beenbefore thee, and that come after; for this is the sentence ofthe Lord over all flesh.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	4	And why art thou against the pleasure of the most High? thereis no inquisition in the grave, whether thou have lived ten, oran hundred, or a thousand years.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	5	The children of sinners are abominable children, and theythat are conversant in the dwelling of the ungodly.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	6	The inheritance of sinners' children shall perish, and theirposterity shall have a perpetual reproach.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	7	The children will complain of an ungodly father, because theyshall be reproached for his sake.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	8	Woe be unto you, ungodly men, which have forsaken the law ofthe most high God! for if ye increase, it shall be to yourdestruction:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	9	And if ye be born, ye shall be born to a curse: and if yedie, a curse shall be your portion.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	10	All that are of the earth shall turn to earth again: so theungodly shall go from a curse to destruction.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	11	The mourning of men is about their bodies: but an ill name ofsinners shall be blotted out.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	12	Have regard to thy name; for that shall continue with theeabove a thousand great treasures of gold.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	13	A good life hath but few days: but a good name endureth forever.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	14	My children, keep discipline in peace: for wisdom that ishid, and a treasure that is not seen, what profit is in themboth?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	15	A man that hideth his foolishness is better than a man thathideth his wisdom.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	16	Therefore be shamefaced according to my word: for it is notgood to retain all shamefacedness; neither is it altogetherapproved in every thing.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	17	Be ashamed of whoredom before father and mother: and of a liebefore a prince and a mighty man;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	18	Of an offence before a judge and ruler; of iniquity before acongregation and people; of unjust dealing before thy partnerand friend;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	19	And of theft in regard of the place where thou sojournest,and in regard of the truth of God and his covenant; and to leanwith thine elbow upon the meat; and of scorning to give andtake;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	20	And of silence before them that salute thee; and to look uponan harlot;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	21	And to turn away thy face from thy kinsman; or to take away aportion or a gift; or to gaze upon another man's wife.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	22	Or to be overbusy with his maid, and come not near her bed;or of upbraiding speeches before friends; and after thou hastgiven, upbraid not;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	23	Or of iterating and speaking again that which thou hastheard; and of revealing of secrets.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	41	24	So shalt thou be truly shamefaced and find favour before allmen.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	1	Of these things be not thou ashamed, and accept no person tosin thereby:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	2	Of the law of the most High, and his covenant; and ofjudgment to justify the ungodly;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	3	Of reckoning with thy partners and travellers; or of the giftof the heritage of friends;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	4	Of exactness of balance and weights; or of getting much orlittle;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	5	And of merchants' indifferent selling; of much correction ofchildren; and to make the side of an evil servant to bleed.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	6	Sure keeping is good, where an evil wife is; and shut up,where many hands are.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	7	Deliver all things in number and weight; and put all inwriting that thou givest out, or receivest in.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	8	Be not ashamed to inform the unwise and foolish, and theextreme aged that contendeth with those that are young: thusshalt thou be truly learned, and approved of all men living.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	9	The father waketh for the daughter, when no man knoweth; andthe care for her taketh away sleep: when she is young, lest shepass away the flower of her age; and being married, lest sheshould be hated:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	10	In her virginity, lest she should be defiled and gotten withchild in her father's house; and having an husband, lest sheshould misbehave herself; and when she is married, lest sheshould be barren.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	11	Keep a sure watch over a shameless daughter, lest she makethee a laughingstock to thine enemies, and a byword in the city,and a reproach among the people, and make thee ashamed beforethe multitude.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	12	Behold not every body's beauty, and sit not in the midst ofwomen.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	13	For from garments cometh a moth, and from women wickedness.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	14	Better is the churlishness of a man than a courteous woman, awoman, I say, which bringeth shame and reproach.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	15	I will now remember the works of the Lord, and declare thethings that I have seen: In the words of the Lord are his works.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	16	The sun that giveth light looketh upon all things, and thework thereof is full of the glory of the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	17	The Lord hath not given power to the saints to declare allhis marvellous works, which the Almighty Lord firmly settled,that whatsoever is might be established for his glory.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	18	He seeketh out the deep, and the heart, and considereth theircrafty devices: for the Lord knoweth all that may be known, andhe beholdeth the signs of the world.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	19	He declareth the things that are past, and for to come, andrevealeth the steps of hidden things.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	20	No thought escapeth him, neither any word is hidden from him.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	21	He hath garnished the excellent works of his wisdom, and heis from everlasting to everlasting: unto him may nothing beadded, neither can he be diminished, and he hath no need of anycounsellor.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	22	Oh how desirable are all his works! and that a man may seeeven to a spark.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	23	All these things live and remain for ever for all uses, andthey are all obedient.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	24	All things are double one against another: and he hath madenothing imperfect.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	42	25	One thing establisheth the good or another: and who shall befilled with beholding his glory?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	1	The pride of the height, the clear firmament, the beauty ofheaven, with his glorious shew;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	2	The sun when it appeareth, declaring at his rising amarvellous instrument, the work of the most High:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	3	At noon it parcheth the country, and who can abide theburning heat thereof?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	4	A man blowing a furnace is in works of heat, but the sunburneth the mountains three times more; breathing out fieryvapours, and sending forth bright beams, it dimmeth the eyes.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	5	Great is the Lord that made it; and at his commandmentrunneth hastily.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	6	He made the moon also to serve in her season for adeclaration of times, and a sign of the world.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	7	From the moon is the sign of feasts, a light that decreasethin her perfection.
