The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	9	The beauty of heaven, the glory of the stars, an ornamentgiving light in the highest places of the Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	10	At the commandment of the Holy One they will stand in theirorder, and never faint in their watches.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	11	Look upon the rainbow, and praise him that made it; verybeautiful it is in the brightness thereof.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	12	It compasseth the heaven about with a glorious circle, andthe hands of the most High have bended it.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	13	By his commandment he maketh the snow to fall aplace, andsendeth swiftly the lightnings of his judgment.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	14	Through this the treasures are opened: and clouds fly forthas fowls.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	15	By his great power he maketh the clouds firm, and thehailstones are broken small.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	16	At his sight the mountains are shaken, and at his will thesouth wind bloweth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	17	The noise of the thunder maketh the earth to tremble: so doththe northern storm and the whirlwind: as birds flying hescattereth the snow, and the falling down thereof is as thelighting of grasshoppers:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	18	The eye marvelleth at the beauty of the whiteness thereof,and the heart is astonished at the raining of it.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	19	The hoarfrost also as salt he poureth on the earth, and beingcongealed, it lieth on the top of sharp stakes.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	20	When the cold north wind bloweth, and the water is congealedinto ice, it abideth upon every gathering together of water, andclotheth the water as with a breastplate.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	21	It devoureth the mountains, and burneth the wilderness, andconsumeth the grass as fire.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	22	A present remedy of all is a mist coming speedily, a dewcoming after heat refresheth.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	23	By his counsel he appeaseth the deep, and planteth islandstherein.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	24	They that sail on the sea tell of the danger thereof; andwhen we hear it with our ears, we marvel thereat.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	25	For therein be strange and wondrous works, variety of allkinds of beasts and whales created.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	26	By him the end of them hath prosperous success, and by hisword all things consist.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	27	We may speak much, and yet come short: wherefore in sum, heis all.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	28	How shall we be able to magnify him? for he is great aboveall his works.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	29	The Lord is terrible and very great, and marvellous is hispower.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	30	When ye glorify the Lord, exalt him as much as ye can; foreven yet will he far exceed: and when ye exalt him, put forthall your strength, and be not weary; for ye can never go farenough.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	31	Who hath seen him, that he might tell us? and who can magnifyhim as he is?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	32	There are yet hid greater things than these be, for we haveseen but a few of his works.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	43	33	For the Lord hath made all things; and to the godly hath hegiven wisdom.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	44	1	Let us now praise famous men, and our fathers that begat us.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	44	2	The Lord hath wrought great glory by them through his greatpower from the beginning.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	44	3	Such as did bear rule in their kingdoms, men renowned fortheir power, giving counsel by their understanding, anddeclaring prophecies:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	44	4	Leaders of the people by their counsels, and by theirknowledge of learning meet for the people, wise and eloquent aretheir instructions:

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	46	1	Jesus the son a Nave was valiant in the wars, and was thesuccessor of Moses in prophecies, who according to his name wasmade great for the saving of the elect of God, and takingvengeance of the enemies that rose up against them, that hemight set Israel in their inheritance.

The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	50	28	Blessed is he that shall be exercised in these things; and hethat layeth them up in his heart shall become wise.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	50	29	For if he do them, he shall be strong to all things: for thelight of the Lord leadeth him, who giveth wisdom to the godly.Blessed be the name of the Lord for ever. Amen, Amen.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	[A	Prayer o	 Jesus the son of Sirach.]	
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	1	I will thank thee, O Lord and King, and praise thee, O God mySaviour: I do give praise unto thy name:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	2	For thou art my defender and helper, and has preserved mybody from destruction, and from the snare of the slanderoustongue, and from the lips that forge lies, and has been minehelper against mine adversaries:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	3	And hast delivered me, according to the multitude of theymercies and greatness of thy name, from the teeth of them thatwere ready to devour me, and out of the hands of such as soughtafter my life, and from the manifold afflictions which I had;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	4	From the choking of fire on every side, and from the midst ofthe fire which I kindled not;
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	5	From the depth of the belly of hell, from an unclean tongue,and from lying words.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	6	By an accusation to the king from an unrighteous tongue mysoul drew near even unto death, my life was near to the hellbeneath.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	7	They compassed me on every side, and there was no man to helpme: I looked for the succour of men, but there was none.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	8	Then thought I upon thy mercy, O Lord, and upon thy acts ofold, how thou deliverest such as wait for thee, and savest themout of the hands of the enemies.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	9	Then lifted I up my supplications from the earth, and prayedfor deliverance from death.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	10	I called upon the Lord, the Father of my Lord, that he wouldnot leave me in the days of my trouble, and in the time of theproud, when there was no help.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	11	I will praise thy name continually, and will sing praiseswith thanksgiving; and so my prayer was heard:
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	12	For thou savedst me from destruction, and deliveredst me fromthe evil time: therefore will I give thanks, and praise thee,and bless they name, O Lord.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	13	When I was yet young, or ever I went abroad, I desired wisdomopenly in my prayer.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	14	I prayed for her before the temple, and will seek her outeven to the end.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	15	Even from the flower till the grape was ripe hath my heartdelighted in her: my foot went the right way, from my youth upsought I after her.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	16	I bowed down mine ear a little, and received her, and gatmuch learning.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	17	I profited therein, therefore will I ascribe glory unto himthat giveth me wisdom.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	18	For I purposed to do after her, and earnestly I followed thatwhich is good; so shall I not be confounded.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	19	My soul hath wrestled with her, and in my doings I was exact:I stretched forth my hands to the heaven above,and bewailed my ignorances of her.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	20	I directed my soul unto her, and I found her in pureness:I have had my heart joined with her from the beginning,therefore shall I not be foresaken.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	21	My heart was troubled in seeking her: therefore have I gottena good possession.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	22	The Lord hath given me a tongue for my reward,and I will praise him therewith.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	23	Draw near unto me, ye unlearned, and dwell in the house of learning.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	24	Wherefore are ye slow, and what say ye to these things,seeing your souls are very thirsty?
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	25	I opened my mouth, and said, Buy her for yourselves without money.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	26	Put your neck under the yoke, and let your soul receiveinstruction: she is hard at hand to find.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	27	Behold with your eyes, how that I have but little labour, andhave gotten unto me much rest.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	28	Get learning with a great sum of money, and get much gold by her.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	29	Let your soul rejoice in his mercy, and be not ashamed of his praise.
The Book of Sirach (or Ecclesiasticus)	Sir	51	30	Work your work betimes, and in his time he will give you your reward.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	1	And these are the words of the book, which Baruch the son ofNerias, the son of Maasias, the son of Sedecias, the son ofAsadias, the son of Chelcias, wrote in Babylon,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	2	In the fifth year, and in the seventh day of the month, whattime as the Chaldeans took Jerusalem, and burnt it with fire.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	3	And Baruch did read the words of this book in the hearing ofJechonias the son of Joachim king of Juda, and in the ears ofall the people that came to hear the book,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	4	And in the hearing of the nobles, and of the king's sons, andin the hearing of the elders, and of all the people, from thelowest unto the highest, even of all them that dwelt at Babylonby the river Sud.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	5	Whereupon they wept, fasted, and prayed before the Lord.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	6	They made also a collection of money according to every man'spower:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	7	And they sent it to Jerusalem unto Joachim the high priest,the son of Chelcias, son of Salom, and to the priests, and toall the people which were found with him at Jerusalem,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	8	At the same time when he received the vessels of the house ofthe Lord, that were carried out of the temple, to return theminto the land of Juda, the tenth day of the month Sivan, namely,silver vessels, which Sedecias the son of Josias king of Jadahad made,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	9	After that Nabuchodonosor king of Babylon had carried awayJechonias, and the princes, and the captives, and the mightymen, and the people of the land, from Jerusalem, and broughtthem unto Babylon.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	10	And they said, Behold, we have sent you money to buy youburnt offerings, and sin offerings, and incense, and prepare yemanna, and offer upon the altar of the Lord our God;
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	11	And pray for the life of Nabuchodonosor king of Babylon, andfor the life of Balthasar his son, that their days may be uponearth as the days of heaven:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	12	And the Lord will give us strength, and lighten our eyes, andwe shall live under the shadow of Nabuchodonosor king ofBabylon, and under the shadow of Balthasar his son, and we shallserve them many days, and find favour in their sight.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	13	Pray for us also unto the Lord our God, for we have sinnedagainst the Lord our God; and unto this day the fury of the Lordand his wrath is not turned from us.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	14	And ye shall read this book which we have sent unto you, tomake confession in the house of the Lord, upon the feasts andsolemn days.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	15	And ye shall say, To the Lord our God belongethrighteousness, but unto us the confusion of faces, as it is cometo pass this day, unto them of Juda, and to the inhabitants ofJerusalem,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	16	And to our kings, and to our princes, and to our priests, andto our prophets, and to our fathers:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	17	For we have sinned before the Lord,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	18	And disobeyed him, and have not hearkened unto the voice ofthe Lord our God, to walk in the commandments that he gave usopenly:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	19	Since the day that the Lord brought our forefathers out ofthe land of Egypt, unto this present day, we have beendisobedient unto the Lord our God, and we have been negligent innot hearing his voice.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	20	Wherefore the evils cleaved unto us, and the curse, which theLord appointed by Moses his servant at the time that he broughtour fathers out of the land of Egypt, to give us a land thatfloweth with milk and honey, like as it is to see this day.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	21	Nevertheless we have not hearkened unto the voice of the Lordour God, according unto all the words of the prophets, whom hesent unto us:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	1	22	But every man followed the imagination of his own wickedheart, to serve strange gods, and to do evil in the sight of theLord our God.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	1	Therefore the Lord hath made good his word, which hepronounced against us, and against our judges that judgedIsrael, and against our kings, and against our princes, andagainst the men of Israel and Juda,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	2	To bring upon us great plagues, such as never happened underthe whole heaven, as it came to pass in Jerusalem, according tothe things that were written in the law of Moses;
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	3	That a man should eat the flesh of his own son, and the fleshof his own daughter.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	4	Moreover he hath delivered them to be in subjection to allthe kingdoms that are round about us, to be as a reproach anddesolation among all the people round about, where the Lord hathscattered them.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	5	Thus we were cast down, and not exalted, because we havesinned against the Lord our God, and have not been obedient untohis voice.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	6	To the Lord our God appertaineth righteousness: but unto usand to our fathers open shame, as appeareth this day.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	7	For all these plagues are come upon us, which the Lord hathpronounced against us
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	8	Yet have we not prayed before the Lord, that we might turnevery one from the imaginations of his wicked heart.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	9	Wherefore the Lord watched over us for evil, and the Lordhath brought it upon us: for the Lord is righteous in all hisworks which he hath commanded us.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	10	Yet we have not hearkened unto his voice, to walk in thecommandments of the Lord, that he hath set before us.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	11	And now, O Lord God of Israel, that hast brought thy peopleout of the land of Egypt with a mighty hand, and high arm, andwith signs, and with wonders, and with great power, and hastgotten thyself a name, as appeareth this day:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	12	O Lord our God, we have sinned, we have done ungodly, we havedealt unrighteously in all thine ordinances.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	13	Let thy wrath turn from us: for we are but a few left amongthe heathen, where thou hast scattered us.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	14	Hear our prayers, O Lord, and our petitions, and deliver usfor thine own sake, and give us favour in the sight of themwhich have led us away:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	15	That all the earth may know that thou art the Lord our God,because Israel and his posterity is called by thy name.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	16	O Lord, look down from thine holy house, and consider us: bowdown thine ear, O Lord, to hear us.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	17	Open thine eyes, and behold; for the dead that are in thegraves, whose souls are taken from their bodies, will give untothe Lord neither praise nor righteousness:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	18	But the soul that is greatly vexed, which goeth stooping andfeeble, and the eyes that fail, and the hungry soul, will givethee praise and righteousness, O Lord.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	19	Therefore we do not make our humble supplication before thee,O Lord our God, for the righteousness of our fathers, and of ourkings.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	20	For thou hast sent out thy wrath and indignation upon us, asthou hast spoken by thy servants the prophets, saying,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	21	Thus saith the Lord, Bow down your shoulders to serve theking of Babylon: so shall ye remain in the land that I gave untoyour fathers.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	22	But if ye will not hear the voice of the Lord, to serve theking of Babylon,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	23	I will cause to cease out of the cites of Judah, and fromwithout Jerusalem, the voice of mirth, and the voice of joy, thevoice of the bridegroom, and the voice of the bride: and thewhole land shall be desolate of inhabitants.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	24	But we would not hearken unto thy voice, to serve the king ofBabylon: therefore hast thou made good the words that thouspakest by thy servants the prophets, namely, that the bones ofour kings, and the bones of our fathers, should be taken out oftheir place.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	25	And, lo, they are cast out to the heat of the day, and to thefrost of the night, and they died in great miseries by famine,by sword, and by pestilence.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	26	And the house which is called by thy name hast thou laidwaste, as it is to be seen this day, for the wickedness of thehouse of Israel and the house of Juda.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	27	O Lord our God, thou hast dealt with us after all thygoodness, and according to all that great mercy of thine,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	28	As thou spakest by thy servant Moses in the day when thoudidst command him to write the law before the children ofIsrael, saying,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	29	If ye will not hear my voice, surely this very greatmultitude shall be turned into a small number among the nations,where I will scatter them.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	30	For I knew that they would not hear me, because it is astiffnecked people: but in the land of their captivities theyshall remember themselves.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	31	And shall know that I am the Lord their God: for I will givethem an heart, and ears to hear:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	32	And they shall praise me in the land of their captivity, andthink upon my name,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	33	And return from their stiff neck, and from their wickeddeeds: for they shall remember the way of their fathers, whichsinned before the Lord.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	34	And I will bring them again into the land which I promisedwith an oath unto their fathers, Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob, andthey shall be lords of it: and I will increase them, and theyshall not be diminished.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	2	35	And I will make an everlasting covenant with them to be theirGod, and they shall be my people: and I will no more drive mypeople of Israel out of the land that I have given them.

The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	4	O Lord Almighty, thou God of Israel, hear now the prayers ofthe dead Israelites, and of their children, which have sinnedbefore thee, and not hearkened unto the voice of thee their God:for the which cause these plagues cleave unto us.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	5	Remember not the iniquities of our forefathers: but thinkupon thy power and thy name now at this time.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	6	For thou art the Lord our God, and thee, O Lord, will wepraise.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	7	And for this cause thou hast put thy fear in our hearts, tothe intent that we should call upon thy name, and praise thee inour captivity: for we have called to mind all the iniquity ofour forefathers, that sinned before thee.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	8	Behold, we are yet this day in our captivity, where thou hastscattered us, for a reproach and a curse, and to be subject topayments, according to all the iniquities of our fathers, whichdeparted from the Lord our God.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	9	Hear, Israel, the commandments of life: give ear tounderstand wisdom.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	10	How happeneth it Israel, that thou art in thine enemies'land, that thou art waxen old in a strange country, that thouart defiled with the dead,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	11	That thou art counted with them that go down into the grave?
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	12	Thou hast forsaken the fountain of wisdom.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	13	For if thou hadst walked in the way of God, thou shouldesthave dwelled in peace for ever.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	14	Learn where is wisdom, where is strength, where isunderstanding; that thou mayest know also where is length ofdays, and life, where is the light of the eyes, and peace.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	15	Who hath found out her place? or who hath come into hertreasures ?
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	16	Where are the princes of the heathen become, and such asruled the beasts upon the earth;
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	17	They that had their pastime with the fowls of the air, andthey that hoarded up silver and gold, wherein men trust, andmade no end of their getting?
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	18	For they that wrought in silver, and were so careful, andwhose works are unsearchable,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	19	They are vanished and gone down to the grave, and others arecome up in their steads.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	20	Young men have seen light, and dwelt upon the earth: but theway of knowledge have they not known,
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	21	Nor understood the paths thereof, nor laid hold of it: theirchildren were far off from that way.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	22	It hath not been heard of in Chanaan, neither hath it beenseen in Theman.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	23	The Agarenes that seek wisdom upon earth, the merchants ofMeran and of Theman, the authors of fables, and searchers out ofunderstanding; none of these have known the way of wisdom, orremember her paths.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	24	O Israel, how great is the house of God! and how large is theplace of his possession!
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	25	Great, and hath none end; high, and unmeasurable.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	26	There were the giants famous from the beginning, that were ofso great stature, and so expert in war.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	27	Those did not the Lord choose, neither gave he the way ofknowledge unto them:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	28	But they were destroyed, because they had no wisdom, andperished through their own foolishness.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	29	Who hath gone up into heaven, and taken her, and brought herdown from the clouds?
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	30	Who hath gone over the sea, and found her, and will bring herfor pure gold?
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	31	No man knoweth her way, nor thinketh of her path.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	32	But he that knoweth all things knoweth her, and hath foundher out with his understanding: he that prepared the earth forevermore hath filled it with fourfooted beasts:
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	33	He that sendeth forth light, and it goeth, calleth it again,and it obeyeth him with fear.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	34	The stars shined in their watches, and rejoiced: when hecalleth them, they say, Here we be; and so with cheerfulnessthey shewed light unto him that made them.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	35	This is our God, and there shall none other be accounted ofin comparison of him
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	36	He hath found out all the way of knowledge, and hath given itunto Jacob his servant, and to Israel his beloved.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	3	37	Afterward did he shew himself upon earth, and conversed withmen.

The Book of Baruch	Bar	4	23	For I sent you out with mourning and weeping: but God willgive you to me again with joy and gladness for ever.

The Book of Baruch	Bar	4	26	My delicate ones have gone rough ways, and were taken away asa flock caught of the enemies.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	4	27	Be of good comfort, O my children, and cry unto God: for yeshall be remembered of him that brought these things upon you.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	4	28	For as it was your mind to go astray from God: so, beingreturned, seek him ten times more.
The Book of Baruch	Bar	4	29	For he that hath brought these plagues upon you shall bringyou everlasting joy with your salvation.

The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	1	A copy of an epistle, which Jeremy sent unto them which wereto be led captives into Babylon by the king of the Babylonians,to certify them, as it was commanded him of God.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	2	Because of the sins which ye have committed before God, yeshall be led away captives into Babylon by Nabuchodonosor kingof the Babylonians.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	3	So when ye be come unto Babylon, ye shall remain there manyyears, and for a long season, namely, seven generations: andafter that I will bring you away peaceably from thence.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	4	Now shall ye see in Babylon gods of silver, and of gold, andof wood, borne upon shoulders, which cause the nations to fear.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	5	Beware therefore that ye in no wise be like to strangers,neither be ye and of them, when ye see the multitude before themand behind them, worshipping them.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	6	But say ye in your hearts, O Lord, we must worship thee.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	7	For mine angel is with you, and I myself caring for yoursouls.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	8	As for their tongue, it is polished by the workman, and theythemselves are gilded and laid over with silver; yet are theybut false, and cannot speak.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	9	And taking gold, as it were for a virgin that loveth to gogay, they make crowns for the heads of their gods.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	10	Sometimes also the priests convey from their gods gold andsilver, and bestow it upon themselves.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	11	Yea, they will give thereof to the common harlots, and deckthem as men with garments, [being] gods of silver, and gods ofgold, and wood.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	12	Yet cannot these gods save themselves from rust and moth,though they be covered with purple raiment.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	13	They wipe their faces because of the dust of the temple, whenthere is much upon them.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	14	And he that cannot put to death one that offendeth himholdeth a sceptre, as though he were a judge of the country.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	15	He hath also in his right hand a dagger and an ax: but cannotdeliver himself from war and thieves.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	16	Whereby they are known not to be gods: therefore fear themnot.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	17	For like as a vessel that a man useth is nothing worth whenit is broken; even so it is with their gods: when they be set upin the temple, their eyes be full of dust through the feet ofthem that come in.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	18	And as the doors are made sure on every side upon him thatoffendeth the king, as being committed to suffer death: even sothe priests make fast their temples with doors, with locks, andbars, lest their gods be spoiled with robbers.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	19	They light them candles, yea, more than for themselves,whereof they cannot see one.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	20	They are as one of the beams of the temple, yet they saytheir hearts are gnawed upon by things creeping out of theearth; and when they eat them and their clothes, they feel itnot.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	21	Their faces are blacked through the smoke that cometh out ofthe temple.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	22	Upon their bodies and heads sit bats, swallows, and birds,and the cats also.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	23	By this ye may know that they are no gods: therefore fearthem not.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	24	Notwithstanding the gold that is about them to make thembeautiful, except they wipe off the rust, they will not shine:for neither when they were molten did they feel it.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	25	The things wherein there is no breath are bought for a mosthigh price.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	26	They are borne upon shoulders, having no feet whereby theydeclare unto men that they be nothing worth.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	27	They also that serve them are ashamed: for if they fall tothe ground at any time, they cannot rise up again of themselves:neither, if one set them upright, can they move of themselves:neither, if they be bowed down, can they make themselvesstraight: but they set gifts before them as unto dead men.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	28	As for the things that are sacrificed unto them, theirpriests sell and abuse; in like manner their wives lay up partthereof in salt; but unto the poor and impotent they givenothing of it.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	29	Menstruous women and women in childbed eat their sacrifices:by these things ye may know that they are no gods: fear themnot.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	30	For how can they be called gods? because women set meatbefore the gods of silver, gold, and wood.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	31	And the priests sit in their temples, having their clothesrent, and their heads and beards shaven, and nothing upon theirheads.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	32	They roar and cry before their gods, as men do at the feastwhen one is dead.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	33	The priests also take off their garments, and clothe theirwives and children.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	34	Whether it be evil that one doeth unto them, or good, theyare not able to recompense it: they can neither set up a king,nor put him down.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	35	In like manner, they can neither give riches nor money:though a man make a vow unto them, and keep it not, they willnot require it.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	36	They can save no man from death, neither deliver the weakfrom the mighty.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	37	They cannot restore a blind man to his sight, nor help anyman in his distress.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	38	They can shew no mercy to the widow, nor do good to thefatherless.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	39	Their gods of wood, and which are overlaid with gold andsilver, are like the stones that be hewn out of the mountain:they that worship them shall be confounded.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	40	How should a man then think and say that they are gods, wheneven the Chaldeans themselves dishonour them?
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	41	Who if they shall see one dumb that cannot speak, they bringhim, and intreat Bel that he may speak, as though he were ableto understand.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	42	Yet they cannot understand this themselves, and leave them:for they have no knowledge.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	43	The women also with cords about them, sitting in the ways,burn bran for perfume: but if any of them, drawn by some thatpasseth by, lie with him, she reproacheth her fellow, that shewas not thought as worthy as herself, nor her cord broken.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	44	Whatsoever is done among them is false: how may it then bethought or said that they are gods?
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	45	They are made of carpenters and goldsmiths: they can benothing else than the workmen will have them to be.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	46	And they themselves that made them can never continue long;how should then the things that are made of them be gods?
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	47	For they left lies and reproaches to them that come after.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	48	For when there cometh any war or plague upon them, thepriests consult with themselves, where they may be hidden withthem.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	49	How then cannot men perceive that they be no gods, which canneither save themselves from war, nor from plague?
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	50	For seeing they be but of wood, and overlaid with silver andgold, it shall be known hereafter that they are false:
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	51	And it shall manifestly appear to all nations and kings thatthey are no gods, but the works of men's hands, and that thereis no work of God in them.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	52	Who then may not know that they are no gods?
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	53	For neither can they set up a king in the land, nor give rainunto men.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	54	Neither can they judge their own cause, nor redress a wrong,being unable: for they are as crows between heaven and earth.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	55	Whereupon when fire falleth upon the house of gods of wood,or laid over with gold or silver, their priests will flee away,and escape; but they themselves shall be burned asunder likebeams.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	56	Moreover they cannot withstand any king or enemies: how canit then be thought or said that they be gods?
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	57	Neither are those gods of wood, and laid over with silver orgold, able to escape either from thieves or robbers.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	58	Whose gold, and silver, and garments wherewith they areclothed, they that are strong take, and go away withal: neitherare they able to help themselves.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	59	Therefore it is better to be a king that sheweth his power,or else a profitable vessel in an house, which the owner shallhave use of, than such false gods; or to be a door in an house,to keep such things therein, than such false gods. or a pillarof wood in a a palace, than such false gods.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	60	For sun, moon, and stars, being bright and sent to do theiroffices, are obedient.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	61	In like manner the lightning when it breaketh forth is easyto be seen; and after the same manner the wind bloweth in everycountry.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	62	And when God commandeth the clouds to go over the wholeworld, they do as they are bidden.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	63	And the fire sent from above to consume hills and woods doethas it is commanded: but these are like unto them neither in shewnor power.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	64	Wherefore it is neither to be supposed nor said that they aregods, seeing, they are able neither to judge causes, nor to dogood unto men.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	65	Knowing therefore that they are no gods, fear them not,
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	66	For they can neither curse nor bless kings:
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	67	Neither can they shew signs in the heavens among the heathen,nor shine as the sun, nor give light as the moon.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	68	The beasts are better than they: for they can get under acover and help themselves.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	69	It is then by no means manifest unto us that they are gods:therefore fear them not.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	70	For as a scarecrow in a garden of cucumbers keepeth nothing:so are their gods of wood, and laid over with silver and gold.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	71	And likewise their gods of wood, and laid over with silverand gold, are like to a white thorn in an orchard, that everybird sitteth upon; as also to a dead body, that is east into thedark.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	72	And ye shall know them to be no gods by the bright purplethat rotteth upon then1: and they themselves afterward shall beeaten, and shall be a reproach in the country.
The Epistle (or letter) of Jeremiah (Jeremy)	EpJer	6	73	Better therefore is the just man that hath none idols: for heshall be far from reproach.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	1	There dwelt a man in Babylon, called Joacim:
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	2	And he took a wife, whose name was Susanna, the daughter ofChelcias, a very fair woman, and one that feared the Lord.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	3	Her parents also were righteous, and taught their daughteraccording to the law of Moses.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	4	Now Joacim was a great rich man, and had a fair gardenjoining unto his house: and to him resorted the Jews; because hewas more honourable than all others.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	5	The same year were appointed two of the ancients of thepeople to be judges, such as the Lord spake of, that wickednesscame from Babylon from ancient judges, who seemed to govern thepeople.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	6	These kept much at Joacim's house: and all that had any suitsin law came unto them.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	7	Now when the people departed away at noon, Susanna went intoher husband's garden to walk.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	8	And the two elders saw her going in every day, and walking;so that their lust was inflamed toward her.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	9	And they perverted their own mind, and turned away theireyes, that they might not look unto heaven, nor remember justjudgments.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	10	And albeit they both were wounded with her love, yet durstnot one shew another his grief.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	11	For they were ashamed to declare their lust, that theydesired to have to do with her.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	12	Yet they watched diligently from day to day to see her.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	13	And the one said to the other, Let us now go home: for it isdinner time.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	14	So when they were gone out, they parted the one from theother, and turning back again they came to the same place; andafter that they had asked one another the cause, theyacknowledged their lust: then appointed they a time bothtogether, when they might find her alone.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	15	And it fell out, as they watched a fit time, she went in asbefore with two maids only, and she was desirous to wash herselfin the garden: for it was hot.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	16	And there was no body there save the two elders, that had hidthemselves, and watched her.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	17	Then she said to her maids, Bring me oil and washing balls,and shut the garden doors, that I may wash me.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	18	And they did as she bade them, and shut the garden doors, andwent out themselves at privy doors to fetch the things that shehad commanded them: but they saw not the elders, because theywere hid.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	19	Now when the maids were gone forth, the two elders rose up,and ran unto her, saying,
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	20	Behold, the garden doors are shut, that no man can see us,and we are in love with thee; therefore consent unto us, and liewith us.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	21	If thou wilt not, we will bear witness against thee, that ayoung man was with thee: and therefore thou didst send away thymaids from thee.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	22	Then Susanna sighed, and said, I am straitened on every side:for if I do this thing, it is death unto me: and if I do it notI cannot escape your hands.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	23	It is better for me to fall into your hands, and not do it,than to sin in the sight of the Lord.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	24	With that Susanna cried with a loud voice: and the two elderscried out against her.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	25	Then ran the one, and opened the garden door.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	26	So when the servants of the house heard the cry in thegarden, they rushed in at the privy door, to see what was doneunto her.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	27	But when the elders had declared their matter, the servantswere greatly ashamed: for there was never such a report made ofSusanna.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	28	And it came to pass the next day, when the people wereassembled to her husband Joacim, the two elders came also fullof mischievous imagination against Susanna to put her to death;
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	29	And said before the people, Send for Susanna, the daughter ofChelcias, Joacim's wife. And so they sent.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	30	So she came with her father and mother, her children, and allher kindred.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	31	Now Susanna was a very delicate woman, and beauteous tobehold.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	32	And these wicked men commanded to uncover her face, (for shewas covered) that they might be filled with her beauty.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	33	Therefore her friends and all that saw her wept.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	34	Then the two elders stood up in the midst of the people, andlaid their hands upon her head.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	35	And she weeping looked up toward heaven: for her hearttrusted in the Lord.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	36	And the elders said, As we walked in the garden alone, thiswoman came in with two maids, and shut the garden doors, andsent the maids away.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	37	Then a young man, who there was hid, came unto her, and laywith her.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	38	Then we that stood in a corner of the garden, seeing thiswickedness, ran unto them.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	39	And when we saw them together, the man we could not hold: forhe was stronger than we, and opened the door, and leaped out.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	40	But having taken this woman, we asked who the young man was,but she would not tell us: these things do we testify.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	41	Then the assembly believed them as those that were the eldersand judges of the people: so they condemned her to death.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	42	Then Susanna cried out with a loud voice, and said, Oeverlasting God, that knowest the secrets, and knowest allthings before they be:
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	43	Thou knowest that they have borne false witness against me,and, behold, I must die; whereas I never did such things asthese men have maliciously invented against me.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	44	And the Lord heard her voice.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	45	Therefore when she was led to be put to death, the Lordraised up the holy spirit of a young youth whose name wasDaniel:
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	46	Who cried with a loud voice, I am clear from the blood ofthis woman.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	47	Then all the people turned them toward him, and said, Whatmean these words that thou hast spoken?
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	48	So he standing in the midst of them said, Are ye such fools,ye sons of Israel, that without examination or knowledge of thetruth ye have condemned a daughter of Israel?
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	49	Return again to the place of judgment: for they have bornefalse witness against her.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	50	Wherefore all the people turned again in haste, and theelders said unto him, Come, sit down among us, and shew it us,seeing God hath given thee the honour of an elder.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	51	Then said Daniel unto them, Put these two aside one far fromanother, and I will examine them.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	52	So when they were put asunder one from another, he called oneof them, and said unto him, O thou that art waxen old inwickedness, now thy sins which thou hast committed aforetime arecome to light.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	53	For thou hast pronounced false judgment and hast condemnedthe innocent and hast let the guilty go free; albeit the Lordsaith, The innocent and righteous shalt thou not slay.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	54	Now then, if thou hast seen her, tell me, Under what treesawest thou them companying together? Who answered, Under amastick tree.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	55	And Daniel said, Very well; thou hast lied against thine ownhead; for even now the angel of God hath received the sentenceof God to cut thee in two.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	56	So he put him aside, and commanded to bring the other, andsaid unto him, O thou seed of Chanaan, and not of Juda, beautyhath deceived thee, and lust hath perverted thine heart.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	57	Thus have ye dealt with the daughters of Israel, and they forfear companied with you: but the daughter of Juda would notabide your wickedness.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	58	Now therefore tell me, Under what tree didst thou take themcompanying together? Who answered, Under an holm tree.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	59	Then said Daniel unto him, Well; thou hast also lied againstthine own head: for the angel of God waiteth with the sword tocut thee in two, that he may destroy you.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	60	With that all the assembly cried out with a loud voice, andpraised God, who saveth them that trust in him.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	61	And they arose against the two elders, for Daniel hadconvicted them of false witness by their own mouth:
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	62	And according to the law of Moses they did unto them in suchsort as they maliciously intended to do to their neighbour: andthey put them to death. Thus the innocent blood was saved thesame day.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	63	Therefore Chelcias and his wife praised God for theirdaughter Susanna, with Joacim her husband, and all the kindred,because there was no dishonesty found in her.
The Book of Susanna (in Daniel)	Sus	1	64	From that day forth was Daniel had in great reputation in thesight of the people.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	1	And they walked in the midst of the fire, praising God, andblessing the Lord.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	2	Then Azarias stood up, and prayed on this manner; and openinghis mouth in the midst of the fire said,
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	3	Blessed art thou, O Lord God of our fathers: thy name isworthy to be praised and glorified for evermore:
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	4	For thou art righteous in all the things that thou hast doneto us: yea, true are all thy works, thy ways are right, and allthy judgments truth.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	5	In all the things that thou hast brought upon us, and uponthe holy city of our fathers, even Jerusalem, thou hast executedtrue judgment: for according to truth and judgment didst thoubring all these things upon us because of our sins.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	6	For we have sinned and committed iniquity, departing fromthee.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	7	In all things have we trespassed, and not obeyed thycommandments, nor kept them, neither done as thou hast commandedus, that it might go well with us.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	8	Wherefore all that thou hast brought upon us, and every thingthat thou hast done to us, thou hast done in true judgment.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	9	And thou didst deliver us into the hands of lawless enemies,most hateful forsakers of God, and to an unjust king, and themost wicked in all the world.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	10	And now we cannot open our mouths, we are become a shame andreproach to thy servants; and to them that worship thee.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	11	Yet deliver us not up wholly, for thy name's sake, neitherdisannul thou thy covenant:
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	12	And cause not thy mercy to depart from us, for thy belovedAbraham's sake, for thy servant Issac's sake, and for thy holyIsrael's sake;
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	13	To whom thou hast spoken and promised, that thou wouldestmultiply their seed as the stars of heaven, and as the sand thatlieth upon the seashore.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	14	For we, O Lord, are become less than any nation, and be keptunder this day in all the world because of our sins.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	15	Neither is there at this time prince, or prophet, or leader,or burnt offering, or sacrifice, or oblation, or incense, orplace to sacrifice before thee, and to find mercy.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	16	Nevertheless in a contrite heart and an humble spirit let usbe accepted.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	17	Like as in the burnt offerings of rams and bullocks, and likeas in ten thousands of fat lambs: so let our sacrifice be in thysight this day, and grant that we may wholly go after thee: forthey shall not be confounded that put their trust in thee.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	18	And now we follow thee with all our heart, we fear thee, andseek thy face.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	19	Put us not to shame: but deal with us after thylovingkindness, and according to the multitude of thy mercies.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	20	Deliver us also according to thy marvellous works, and giveglory to thy name, O Lord: and let all them that do thy servantshurt be ashamed;
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	21	And let them be confounded in all their power and might, andlet their strength be broken;
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	22	And let them know that thou art God, the only God, andglorious over the whole world.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	23	And the king's servants, that put them in, ceased not to makethe oven hot with rosin, pitch, tow, and small wood;
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	24	So that the flame streamed forth above the furnace forty andnine cubits.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	25	And it passed through, and burned those Chaldeans it foundabout the furnace.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	26	But the angel of the Lord came down into the oven togetherwith Azarias and his fellows, and smote the flame of the fireout of the oven;
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	27	And made the midst of the furnace as it had been a moistwhistling wind, so that the fire touched them not at all,neither hurt nor troubled them.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	28	Then the three, as out of one mouth, praised, glorified, andblessed, God in the furnace, saying,
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	29	Blessed art thou, O Lord God of our fathers: and to bepraised and exalted above all for ever.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	30	And blessed is thy glorious and holy name: and to be praisedand exalted above all for ever.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	31	Blessed art thou in the temple of thine holy glory: and to bepraised and glorified above all for ever.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	32	Blessed art thou that beholdest the depths, and sittest uponthe cherubims: and to be praised and exalted above all for ever.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	33	Blessed art thou on the glorious throne of thy kingdom: andto be praised and glorified above all for ever.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	34	Blessed art thou in the firmament of heaven: and above ail tobe praised and glorified for ever.

The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	50	O ye frost and snow, bless ye the Lord: praise and exalt himabove all for ever.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	51	O ye lightnings and clouds, bless ye the Lord: praise andexalt him above all for ever.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	52	O let the earth bless the Lord: praise and exalt him aboveall for ever.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	53	O ye mountains and little hills, bless ye the Lord: praiseand exalt him above all for ever.

The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	66	O Ananias, Azarias, and Misael, bless ye the Lord: praise andexalt him above all for ever: far he hath delivered us fromhell, and saved us from the hand of death, and delivered us outof the midst of the furnace and burning flame: even out of themidst of the fire hath he delivered us.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	67	O give thanks unto the Lord, because he is gracious: for hismercy endureth for ever.
The Prayer of Azariah	PrAzar	68	O all ye that worship the Lord, bless the God of gods, praisehim, and give him thanks: for his mercy endureth for ever.
The Prayer of Manasseh King of Judah	PrMan	1	O Lord, Almighty God of our fathers, Abraham, Isaac, andJacob, and of their righteous seed; who hast made heaven andearth, with all the ornament thereof; who hast bound the sea bythe word of thy commandment; who hast shut up the deep, andsealed it by thy terrible and glorious name; whom all men fear,and tremble before thy power; for the majesty of thy glorycannot be borne, and thine angry threatening toward sinners isimportable: but thy merciful promise is unmeasurable andunsearchable; for thou art the most high Lord, of greatcompassion, longsuffering, very merciful, and repentest of theevils of men. Thou, O Lord, according to thy great goodness hastpromised repentance and forgiveness to them that have sinnedagainst thee: and of thine infinite mercies hast appointedrepentance unto sinners, that they may be saved. Thou therefore,O Lord, that art the God of the just, hast not appointedrepentance to the just, as to Abraham, and Isaac, and Jacob,which have not sinned against thee; but thou hast appointedrepentance unto me that am a sinner: for I have sinned above thenumber of the sands of the sea. My transgressions, O Lord, aremultiplied: my transgressions are multiplied, and I am notworthy to behold and see the height of heaven for the multitudeof mine iniquities. I am bowed down with many iron bands, that Icannot life up mine head, neither have any release: for I haveprovoked thy wrath, and done evil before thee: I did not thywill, neither kept I thy commandments: I have set upabominations, and have multiplied offences. Now therefore I bowthe knee of mine heart, beseeching thee of grace. I have sinned,O Lord, I have sinned, and I acknowledge mine iniquities:wherefore, I humbly beseech thee, forgive me, O Lord, forgiveme, and destroy me not with mine iniquites. Be not angry with mefor ever, by reserving evil for me; neither condemn me to thelower parts of the earth. For thou art the God, even the God ofthem that repent; and in me thou wilt shew all thy goodness: forthou wilt save me, that am unworthy, according to thy greatmercy. Therefore I will praise thee for ever all the days of mylife: for all the powers of the heavens do praise thee, andthine is the glory for ever and ever. Amen.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	1	And king Astyages was gathered to his fathers, and Cyrus ofPersia received his kingdom.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	2	And Daniel conversed with the king, and was honoured aboveall his friends.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	3	Now the Babylons had an idol, called Bel, and there werespent upon him every day twelve great measures of fine flour,and forty sheep, and six vessels of wine.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	4	And the king worshipped it and went daily to adore it: butDaniel worshipped his own God. And the king said unto him, Whydost not thou worship Bel?
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	5	Who answered and said, Because I may not worship idols madewith hands, but the living God, who hath created the heaven andthe earth, and hath sovereignty over all flesh.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	6	Then said the king unto him, Thinkest thou not that Bel is aliving God? seest thou not how much he eateth and drinketh everyday?
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	7	Then Daniel smiled, and said, O king, be not deceived: forthis is but clay within, and brass without, and did never eat ordrink any thing.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	8	So the king was wroth, and called for his priests, and saidunto them, If ye tell me not who this is that devoureth theseexpences, ye shall die.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	9	But if ye can certify me that Bel devoureth them, thenDaniel shall die: for he hath spoken blasphemy against Bel. AndDaniel said unto the king, Let it be according to thy word.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	10	Now the priests of Bel were threescore and ten, besidetheir wives and children. And the king went with Daniel into thetemple of Bel.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	11	So Bel's priests said, Lo, we go out: but thou, O king, seton the meat, and make ready the wine, and shut the door fast andseal it with thine own signet;
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	12	And to morrow when thou comest in, if thou findest not that
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	hath eate	 up all, we will suffer death: or else Daniel,	that speaketh falsely against us.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	13	And they little regarded it: for under the table they hadmade a privy entrance, whereby they entered in continually, andconsumed those things.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	14	So when they were gone forth, the king set meats beforeBel. Now Daniel had commanded his servants to bring ashes, andthose they strewed throughout all the temple in the presence ofthe king alone: then went they out, and shut the door, andsealed it with the king's signet, and so departed.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	15	Now in the night came the priests with their wives andchildren, as they were wont to do, and did eat and drinck upall.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	16	In the morning betime the king arose, and Daniel with him.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	17	And the king said, Daniel, are the seals whole? And hesaid, Yea, O king, they be whole.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	18	And as soon as he had opened the dour, the king looked uponthe table, and cried with a loud voice, Great art thou, O Bel,and with thee is no deceit at all.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	19	Then laughed Daniel, and held the king that he should notgo in, and said, Behold now the pavement, and mark well whosefootsteps are these.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	20	And the king said, I see the footsteps of men, women, andchildren. And then the king was angry,
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	21	And took the priests with their wives and children, whoshewed him the privy doors, where they came in, and consumedsuch things as were upon the table.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	22	Therefore the king slew them, and delivered Bel intoDaniel's power, who destroyed him and his temple.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	23	And in that same place there was a great dragon, which theyof Babylon worshipped.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	24	And the king said unto Daniel, Wilt thou also say that thisis of brass? lo, he liveth, he eateth and drinketh; thou canstnot say that he is no living god: therefore worship him.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	25	Then said Daniel unto the king, I will worship the Lord myGod: for he is the living God.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	26	But give me leave, O king, and I shall slay this dragonwithout sword or staff. The king said, I give thee leave.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	27	Then Daniel took pitch, and fat, and hair, and did seethethem together, and made lumps thereof: this he put in thedragon's mouth, and so the dragon burst in sunder : and Danielsaid, Lo, these are the gods ye worship.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	28	When they of Babylon heard that, they took greatindignation, and conspired against the king, saying, The king isbecome a Jew, and he hath destroyed Bel, he hath slain thedragon, and put the priests to death.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	29	So they came to the king, and said, Deliver us Daniel, orelse we will destroy thee and thine house.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	30	Now when the king saw that they pressed him sore, beingconstrained, he delivered Daniel unto them:
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	31	Who cast him into the lions' den: where he was six days.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	32	And in the den there were seven lions, and they had giventhem every day two carcases, and two sheep: which then were notgiven to them, to the intent they might devour Daniel.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	33	Now there was in Jewry a prophet, called Habbacuc, who hadmade pottage, and had broken bread in a bowl, and was going intothe field, for to bring it to the reapers.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	34	But the angel of the Lord said unto Habbacuc, Go, carry thedinner that thou hast into Babylon unto Daniel, who is in thelions' den.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	35	And Habbacuc said, Lord, I never saw Babylon; neither do Iknow where the den is.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	36	Then the angel of the Lord took him by the crown, and barehim by the hair of his head, and through the vehemency of hisspirit set him in Babylon over the den.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	37	And Habbacuc cried, saying, O Daniel, Daniel, take thedinner which God hath sent thee.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	38	And Daniel said, Thou hast remembered me, O God: neitherhast thou forsaken them that seek thee and love thee.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	39	So Daniel arose, and did eat: and the angel of the Lord setHabbacuc in his own place again immediately.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	40	Upon the seventh day the king went to bewail Daniel:and when he came to the den, he looked in, and behold,Daniel was sitting.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	41	Then cried the king with a loud voice, saying, Great artLord God of Daniel, and there is none other beside thee.
The Book of Bel and the Dragon (in Daniel)	Bel	1	42	And he drew him out, and cast those that were the cause ofhis destruction into the den: and they were devouredin a moment before his face.
